After I have completed for you, O Sons, this book which is the last in the knowledge of medicine along with its supplement and I have reached the end in it through expositions of it and its declarations, it seemed good to me to complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of operation, that is, surgery with the hand.
Since operation with the hand is laid low in our region and at our time completely absent; perhaps the knowledge of it has perished, and its trace has been lost, and there remain only small descriptions in the books of the ancients which have been corrupted by hands; errors and hesitation occur until intentions are closed off and the force of it is prolonged, It seemed good to me to revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise in it according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation; and to come with forms of iron tools, and the rest of the instruments of work; which occurs through addition to declarations and through appropriate application.
The reason why a skilled craftsman of it is not found with his hand in this our time is that the art of medicine is long and its author should exercise himself before that in the science of anatomy which Galen narrated, until he knows the remedies of limbs, and their forms, and their connection and disconnection, and has knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, their number, and their origin, and veins, arteries, and quiet veins, and the locations of their outlets.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that name with name is much, and with work it is little, especially in the art of the hand.
We have already said about him at the beginning of this book.
Whoever is not acquainted with what we have said about anatomy, already falls into error, wherein men are killed: as I have seen many of those who are formed in this science, boast about it without knowledge, and without experiment.
I have seen a foolish physician cut off a scrofulous apostema from a woman's neck, and he cut some arteries in her neck: thus the woman bled to death in his hands.
I have seen another physician who presumed to extract a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large. Therefore, he reached for it and extracted it with a piece of the bladder. Thus the man died on the third day.
And I myself had already been summoned to extract it; and I saw, due to the size of the stone and the condition of the man, that he would die.
I have seen another physician who was receiving a stipend from some Duke of our land on account of his medical skill: and a black eunuch was with him, who was injured near the heel of his leg; and the physician, in ignorance, bound up the fracture above the wound with iron splints, strong bands, and nails, and did not allow the wound to breathe.
Then he bandaged him according to his own devices. Afterwards he dismissed him after some days and ordered him not to loosen the bandage: and he stood thus until an aposteme formed on his leg, and on his foot, and it reached destruction.
I was then called to him: and I hastened to loosen the bandage: and peace ensued, and he was freed from his pains.
However, the corruption had already been confirmed in the member: and I could not stop it.
Let it (the wound) therefore halt corruption from spreading throughout the member, until it is destroyed.
And I saw another physician who pierced a malignant apostema; and it ulcerated for days, until the corruption of its evilness with the Lord (of the disease) was revealed.
Because if a cancer is pure from black bile (melancholy), then it should not be approached with iron at all unless it is in a member that can bear it, to be cut off entirely.
And for this reason, O Sons (of the art), it is necessary that you know that an operation is divided into two divisions: one operation which is associated with safety; and another operation, by means of which there is danger in many dispositions.
And I have now awakened in every place of this book where the operation comes which has fear and dread.
Therefore it is necessary for you to beware of this and separate (it) yourselves from it; lest foolish men find a way to speak and disgrace (the art).
Therefore receive (the art) with care and protection, and treat your sick ones with ease and firmness, and use a better way leading to grace of God for health and praiseworthy success; and abandon terrible sicknesses difficult to heal; and remove from yourselves that which causes fear, so hesitation in faith and comfort may not enter upon you.
For it remains more to your glory, and higher in this world, and finally (leads) to the wealth of your possessions.
For Galen has already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat evil sickness; lest you be called an evil doctor.
Now this Treatise has been divided into three Chapters. ¶
First Chapter.
On Cautery with fire, and Cautery with sharp medicine, the procedure has been divided, and arranged from head to foot, as well as the forms of the instruments and tools for Cautery, and everything that is necessary in the operation.
Chapter Second.
On incision and perforation, phlebotomy and wounds; on the extraction of arrows and similar objects, and all of this is divided and arranged according to the forms of the instruments.
Chapter Third.
On restoration and relocation, cure of twisting, and similar conditions; divided and arranged from head to foot, and according to the forms of the instruments.
Before I recall the operation with him, it is necessary that I say the qualities of the remedies and the harm caused by it, and in what composition it should be displayed.
I say therefore that the discourse on the quality of the cautery and the harm it causes is a lengthy, subtle, scientific, and hidden secret.
Also, there were many wise men who spoke about it and disagreed among themselves; for myself, I am content with little of their discourse, fearing a lengthy discussion.
I say therefore that the cautery applies universally to every composition, which is with matter or without it; except for two compositions, which are hot composition without matter and dry composition without matter.
In hot and dry composition with matter, they disagreed. Some indeed said that the cautery is beneficial in it (hot and dry composition with matter). Others said the opposite, that the cautery is not suitable for this illness, which is due to heat and dryness; because the nature of fire is heat, and it is inappropriate to heal an illness that is hot and dry with heat and dryness.
And he who says the opposite said that by cautery it is beneficial for every illness due to heat and dryness which happens in the bodies of men; because when you compare a human body and its humidities with fire composition, you find the body of man cold.
And I myself say by his words; because I have already proven that to me many times.
However, it is not necessary that he comes to it unless the one who has already been proven and has experience in the last exercise of the chapter Cauterii, and knows the diversity of human compositions, and the disposition of illnesses in themselves, and causes of them, and their properties, and the space of time for them.
From the remaining temperaments (complexions), there is no fear for you; and especially in diseases that are cold and moist. Now all physicians agree on them, and they have not disagreed in the treatment with the cautery in those diseases.
And know, my sons, that from the secret of healing through cautery with fire, and its goodness over the cautery with medicine burning, it is because fire is simple, whose action does not extend beyond the member being cauterized, and it does not harm another joined member with it, unless there is a slight damage.
But the action of burning medicine extends to what is distant from the members; and perhaps it causes difficult healing of the disease in the member, and perhaps it kills (the patient).
Fire, however, because of its subtlety and goodness of substance, does not do that unless it is excessive.
Now this has become known to us through experience, because of the duration and effort required for study and art, as well as the position on the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse myself from the length of the discourse.
And if it were not forbidden to this book of mine, I would bring you the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies, by which it expels diseases that have been demonstrated in philosophical discourse, which would be clarified for your minds.
And know, my sons, that they themselves disagree on the time when the cautery should be done, and place the better time in truth.
And I say that the cautery is suitable at any time; therefore, the damage that occurs due to time is absorbed in the benefit that attracts with the cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary, strong, sudden pains that cannot tolerate delay; therefore, it is feared that what occurs from them will be greater than a small damage due to time.
And let not that enter your minds, O sons, that they do not consider, except for the common people and foolish physicians, that there is no always a return to health in the illness which is cured by cautery: and they set forth this as a consequence, and matters are not as they think: therefore because cautery is not, unless in place of medicine, which alters the complexion, and removes the humidities which are the causes, whence arises pain.
Nevertheless, cautery is superfluous over medicine due to its quick recovery and the strength of its operation, and its power of dominion: and it is possible that illness may return at some hour of time according to the complexion of the sick, and the location of his illness, and the strength of its power: and that which is prepared in his body from an aggregation of superfluidities in him: and that which has reached him for acquisition by foods and similar things from such causes, unless there is illness, in which cautery is administered.
A subtle illness in a member of few superfluidities and humidities, such as cautery of the tooth, may be possible that that pain will not return to him. But this is rare.
However, the speech of the common people again, that cautery is the last medicine, is true: not for what they intend in it: because they believe that there is no cure given by medicine, nor by any other after the departure of the cautery.
Matters are, however, the opposite of what they intend, and the purpose that cautery is the last medicine, is not, except when we administer modes of cure in some illness, and these do not give medicine: then afterwards we administer cautery, and it gives a cure: thence comes the idea that cautery is the last medicine, not according to the intention which the common people and many foolish physicians understand.
The ancients said that a cautery with gold is better than one with iron; and they said this only because of the equality of gold, and the loftiness of its substance; and they said that it does not cause a place for cautery to produce pus. That is not absolutely true; because I have proven that it does not do this in certain bodies without others.
And a cautery with it is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you make a fire cautery with gold in fire, it is not shown to you when it is heated according to the quantity that you wish, due to the redness of gold; and when it goes towards it, coldness, and if you add more heat upon it, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls from that into occupation; and for this reason, a cautery with iron is faster and closer to us, due to its rightness for the operation.
And I myself have arranged this chapter on cautery, according to chapters; and I have ordered it from head to foot: so that those who seek it will find what they want from it.
Chapter II.
Here the cauterization is directed at the lordship of moisture and coldness over the brain; which are the two causes of soda and excessive flow of fluids from the head to the eyes and ears, and excessive sleep, toothache, sore throat, and all disease that occurs due to coldness, such as paralysis, soda, epilepsy, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
The method of cauterization is that you command the sick person: to evacuate in the first place with purifying medicine cleansing the head for three or four nights, according to the strength of the sick person, and his age, and his habit.
Then command him to make an opening in his head with a new nail. Then make him sit before you squarely, so that he has placed his hands upon his chest.
Then place the palm of your hand on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever therefore your middle finger comes to be, mark that place with an unburnt brand.
Then heat the cautery in oil: whose shape is this.
Then place it upon the marked place with the unburnt brand, and you pull it down with a descent, by which your hand is gradually tightened, and you turn it. Then you quickly lift your hand and look at the place.
If you see that a quantity of bone or herb is exposed from the skull, then lift your hand. And if not, you place your hand again with the iron itself or with another if it becomes cold: until the bones, which I told you, are visible.
Then take something from salt, and dissolve it in water, and immerse the cotton in it, and place it upon the place: and leave it for three days.
Then place the cotton immerged in butter upon him, and leave it on the place until the scab of fire is destroyed. Then care for it with the four-part ointment until it is healed.
They say that when a wound remains more open, it exudes pus; therefore it is better and more helpful.
And some of them say that the skin should be cauterized until it reaches the bone: and the cautery should be held, until something thick of the bone is burnt.
Then after what has been burned from the bone, it is shaved, then it is cared for.
And some say that when cauterizing, it should be reached to the end, so that it imprints an impression in the bone to such an extent that the bone falls out, which happens as the form of a keratosis; or an instrument which women place infused with small alphabet letters: and they believe, that vapors from the head expire at this location, and the wound remains open for a long time.
Then it should be cauterized until it solidifies.
For me, however, these two types of cautery are not seen at all, except for certain men according to the way of fear.
And it is better, in my opinion, to let it go along with his own health.
For indeed the head becomes weak from the dissolution of its own continuity; as we have testified in other members: and particularly when the head of the weak is naturally frail: and the first type of cautery, indeed, is safer and better for me, and I use it: therefore operate with it for safety.
Chapter III.
When a chronic pain occurs throughout the head and it persists in an unwell person, using hyson (a type of tea), mustard, leeches, hot applications, and unguents. And especially if it has already been cauterized with one cautery as I have said, and none of those [remedies] provide any relief for him: then consider it. If the head of the unwell person is strong by nature and not weak, and finds intense cold: then cauterize with another cautery, but carefully. Then cauterize it on top of all his horns of the head with cautery, so that the skin is not penetrated and a quantity of bone as I have said is exposed. And cauterize it with one cautery at the occiput (the back part) of his head, in the place called "vas" (a hollow or cavity): it is a place where a ventous (pustule) is placed: grind your ointment and do not expose bone. For the unwell person finds intense pain due to this, and different from the pain of all other cauteries of the head.
And I say that this cautery should be in its place: it is necessary that it be the cautery with which horns of the head are cauterized, and the occiput (the back part) of his head should be cauterized more subtly with the cautery with which the middle part of the head is cauterized.
Chapter IV.
When pain and swelling occur in part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is treated with cleansing medicines, and other treatment is administered as I have said in the divisions of diseases, and this does not provide relief: then cauterization is done in two ways: either cauterization with a hot medicine burning: or with iron.
The cautery with burning medicine, is to take one garlic clove, peel it and cut off its ends from both sides. Then cut the painful area at the time with a wide lancet until there is a space under the skin where the tooth can be captured.
Insert it [the tooth] there under the skin until it is concealed; then press upon it with a proper plaster and let it remain for fifteen hours; then dissolve it and extract the garlic; and let it rest for two or three days; afterwards place the cautery submerged in butter on it until the place becomes pus; then care for it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish to do this with certain burning medicines, which I wrote about in the twelfth treatise on poisons.
The cautery of this [the gallbladder] with iron is to be done according to this method. Fire Cautery, whose form is as follows:
It is called the "Clavile": because the head of it is like a nail's shape, in which there is something rough, and in the middle of it is a small projection.
Then place it on the spot and hold your hand; and you turn the iron slowly with speed; and let the quantity to be burned be of the thickness of the skin, as its half. And lift your hand so that the artery below is not burned and there is bleeding.
Then immerse the cautery in water and salt, and place it on the spot for three days; then place the cautery with butter; afterwards care for it with an ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this half-skull with the tip of a second cautery (cultellarius). Beware not to cut an artery in this hemicranium, not old one properly.
On the method of cauterizing in the ancient hemicranium.
When you treat the hemicranium, as previously said in cure and in the division of diseases, and healing does not help: and when, from the illness, you see that what was said about cauterization with the first cautery or cauterization with fire is not enough, then it is necessary to prepare the cautery iron until it turns white, marking a line on the place of pain whose length is half the digit, or like that: and place your hand aside, and tighten it until you cut the artery, and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of continuous jaw movement during mastication so that the side or nerve moving it is not burned, thus causing a spasm.
And take care and caution regarding the flow of blood from the cut artery. There is fear in its cutting, and especially to him who does not know what he is doing, and is not diligent or experienced; and he gives up the operation with it first.
And I shall come with a reminder of the management of blood flow following the cutting of an artery according to its method, and in the place of this book.
If you see from the illness that this cautery is not enough for him, and you see the body of the patient bearing the cautery in the middle of the head as we said, then treat a wound until it heals.
And if you wish to administer the cautery as we said in the chapter on the extraction of an artery with a cautery having two blades. Cauterization is indeed better in this way and more suitable.
On the method of cauterizing ear pain.
When pain occurs in the ear due to coldness and is treated with solutions, and other treatment as we said in the division, but the pain does not subside, then cauterization with fire; and this is what is called a point, whose shape is as follows.
Then the point after its burning should be made circular around the entire ear, as it is turned; or around each side if pain is on both sides. And lengthen (the point) with the cautery slightly from the root of the ear after marking the places with hot iron; and let the quantity of the cautery be ten points on every ear, and so forth.
Then cure the areas until they heal.
Section on the method of cauterization in torturing.
Chapter VII.
The condition that is treated with cauterization due to torturing, is not anything other than those arising from phlegm, as we said in the division of diseases.
And avoid cauterization for types that occur due to exhaustion and spasm of the nerve.
When treating this type of torturing with herbs, mouth washes and gargles, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize the weak person with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, the second a little lower than the earlobe, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
Place your cautery on the opposite side of the weak part. Since softening does not occur unless in the healthy part.
And the shape of cauterization is to cauterize the point itself with the cautery directly at the tip of the upper end of the ear, slightly below the horn of the head; and another one on the earlobe; whose length should be according to the length of a thumb. And place your hand with the cautery until the thickness of half the skin is burned.
And this is the form of a Cautery, and it is a species made from a knife, whose shape is as follows: nevertheless, it should not be too subtle, as you see; and it is necessary that the knife in it should have little excess bulk.
Then take care of the location, when applied: until it heals.
§ On the method of cauterizing in ancient apoplexy.
When the apoplexy becomes old and your treatment does not help and the patient does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries on all the horns of his head, and a cautery in the middle of the head, as we said, and a cautery on the occiput of the head, according to what was mentioned; and the method of cauterizing should be according to what was mentioned.
Also, it is cauterized with a cautery on the face of the stomach: and it is more for the final treatment.
Then care for him, when applied.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in drink there are first of all large amounts of hyson tea, and cleansing pills for the brain.
Then shave completely the head of the sick one, and place on his head a plaster from synapism described in the book of plasters; place it often.
It is indeed the method of cautery; make this accordingly in the same order as I said there.
If therefore he is healed by it, that is good. If not: then make for him three cauteries on the back of his head, which are descending from the upper part of the head to the lower part of the eye; place between each cautery a thickness of a finger.
Then take care of the cautery, with that which came before it.
If you wish an addition and the sick one can endure it: then make a cautery in the middle. If you wish an addition: then cauterize him on top of both horns.
Then take care of him until he is healed; let the cautery be anointed in the form that was mentioned before.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in paralysis, and softening.
Chapter X.
It is necessary that you proceed with the cleansing of the head using hyson, and as we said before.
Then shave the head of the sick person; afterwards cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery over all the horns of the head, and with a cautery over the back part of it, and three over the spondyles of the neck.
If you need softening of the body with many of those [remedies], and if the patient is weak and the illness is strong: then cauterize him with four cauteries over the spondyles of the back, and the last one with a cautery, until most of his skin is burned off, and you scrape your hand. Then take care of him until he is cured; and thus the cautery should be used on Oliva (Olive oil).
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in Epilepsy.
A epileptic should not be cauterized unless his epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary to cleanse the brain of his first, with hyson, and with the rest of the treatment that I have mentioned in the division: when he is severely ill or he endures the taking of medications well.
If, however, he is a child who does not endure medications, then gargarism is administered and cleansing mastication for the brain before that for many days with good food purification.
Then scrape his head, afterwards cauterize him with a single Cauterio in the middle of the head according to what was mentioned before: and with another cauterio at the back of his head, and over all the horn of his skull with cauterio. If he is strong and tolerating, then cauterize him with the cauteries that I have mentioned in having paralysis, and softening of the body on spondiles of the neck and back: let the Cauterium be oiled according to the method mentioned before.
If, however, he is a child, then place a subtle cautery according to this method.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the cause of melancholy is corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries that I have mentioned in having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is an excess of declivities leading to melancholy and his body is damp, then give him in drink what cleanses his brain according to what was mentioned before: then scrape the head of the sick man, and make afterwards a well-centered tortellum made from linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of his head: let the sick man sitting square be held by all sides.
Then present the ointment. And it is more appropriate from ancient butter (of) sheep. And heat it over fire with a measured warmth that the finger can bear when it is immersed in it. Then evacuate (it) in the middle of its head in a circle, and let it cool down.
Do this to the sick one once a week, with the rest of his good regimen, until (he) is cured.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small holes in it, except that you hold (it) with the cautery; it should be smelling.
For this kind of cautery moistens the brain with its quality.
Then place on it a sponge soaked in butter (or) goose fat.
[Section heading] Method of Cauterizing for Descending Water to the Eye.
Chapter 13.
When you are told that water appears in the eye through the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and wash the sick one, with what cleans his head.
And keep him away from all moistness, and let him sit in a bath, on fasting days for some time.
Then command him to shave his head, and cauterize himself in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him on two sides with two cauteries, if there is no discharge of water from both eyes at the same time: or from one side, if there is no discharge of water from one eye: and cut off with the cautery all veins and arteries that are beneath the skin: and let the cauteries be long in width like the temples: and avoid bleeding.
If you see something coming from it (the affected area), then immediately cut it off with whatever medicine is possible: and I will come with wisdom, which is in the extraction of arteries, and their cutting off, and caution against bleeding.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, under two bones, with two lastly produced cauteries.
Chapter on the ancient method of cauterization in tears (eyes).
When the tears of the eyes are old and frequent, and they are over veins and arteries which are manifest on the outside of the head, it is verified that this is from superfluidities of cold, phlegmatic humors: then cauterize with the same cautery as I mentioned in the discharge of water, cauterize in the middle of the head, and with two cauteries on two temples, and with two cauteries on the neck under two bones. And if there is need for addition, then cauterize him carefully on all sides of the eye, over the edge of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in nasal foul smell (nasal discharge).
When you treat it as we said in division, and the medicine does not help: then hurry, and give three nights of infirmocochia in drink; then shave its head, and cauterize it with a medium cautery, using oil in the cautery. Then cauterize it with two cauteries and a small cautery, above two eyebrows under the hairs.
And beware of the artery, lest you cut it.
And this is the form of the Cautery Claw.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing for the softening of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by sickness or moistness: then cauterize the eyelid with one cautery, using this cautery in a lunar shape.
And if you wish, cauterize it above two eyebrows in any part with two cauteries; and the cautery should extend from both sides; and the length of the entire cautery should be according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not place your hand with the cautery at the very end, but rather according to the amount that is burned by the third eyelash.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs turn inward and poke the eye.
Cautery is in it according to two modes: either cautery with fire; or cautery with a burning medicine.
In cautery with fire, instruct the sick person to release their hairs before it, if they are among those who clean them, until they have been extended and matched in length. If they prick him at his origin: then constrict his eyes with a plaster so that they do not move until they are born.
When they are born and matched in length, then place the head of the sick one on your lap: then mark over the eyelids of his eyes with encaustic, mark what is in the shape of a myrtle leaf: and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a bowl soaked in egg white or slime of peas on the eye.
Then heat the fire-cautery, whose shape is as follows:
Then cauterize on the shape which you marked little by little in several places, until the surface of the skin burns, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, completely visible.
And the sign of the health of your work is that if you see the eyelid already contracted and hairs rising at the prick of the eye.
Then lift up your hand then: and release him for three days.
Then place a bowl with butter on it until the scab is removed. Then care for him with ointment until he is healed.
If some hair returns after an hour and the eyelid becomes soft: then repeat the cautery on that place as you did at first.
If the hairs are in the lower part: then cauterize it until they rise to their own place and match so that they do not prick the eye again.
It is to be ordered for the sick man to shave his hair until they are prolonged and evened out. Make from paper a shape of a myrtle leaf.
Then take from known soap and from unsoaked chalk, each a weight of an ounce or about that; then grind these together well with good grinding, and make it quickly so as not to get cold. Then spread it out from that on a cloth which you have made, as the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place it over the eyelid of one eye, or both eyes. Place under the eye a piece of cotton soaked in egg white, and place the head of the sick person on your chest.
Place your index finger on the medicine and press it slightly. You move it as often as the sick person feels the bite of the medicine, because his bite is like fire.
While it continues this which he feels as a bite, then release the medicine and move it with your finger. When the bite ceases, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And observe then if the eyelid is raised like when lifted by heat or incision, it is good; and if not, then repeat on the same place from the medicine where it does not press or darken, until your action is equal, and the eye is contracted.
Then place cotton with butter over it until the burnt skin is removed. Then care for him with diaphinicon ointment or another, until he is healed.
And it is necessary for you at the operation that you keep the last care, so that nothing from the medicine falls into the eye.
If the eyelid becomes soft after days and something from hairs falls into the eye, then repeat the medicine on that place which has been made soft by the eyelid, just as you did at first. Then care for him until he is healed.
And this is the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And know that human eyes differ in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that your consideration should be: and the way of straightness for him who is dedicated to this art should not be hidden.
Method of cauterizing in lacrimal fistula.
When treating fistula, if the cure as we said in the classification of diseases does not work: then it is necessary to cauterize it according to this method.
Command the sick one to put his head in your lap and hold his head servant's hands in such a way that it is not moved or shaken with his own head.
Then place cotton soaked in oil or slippery elm poultice on his eye: then heat the cautery whose shape is as follows.
Let it be concave like the shape of a goose feather quill, from one end of which is made the cautery; and if you want it to penetrate to the other end, and if you want it to extend upward in this manner.
However, this concave form is better for your work.
Then squeeze the fistula if it is open and draw out pus from it; and if it is not open, then open it and draw out its pus.
Then place on it the hot cautery.
And hold your hand near it for a moment on the cautery near the eye, at the part of the nose, so that your hand does not move or the sick person is disturbed; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye and destroy it.
If you reach at the beginning of your cautery to the bone, it will be good. And if not: then repeat the cautery once or twice, as needed; and leave it for three days.
Then place cotton with butter and heal it with an ointment of healing, until it heals.
If it exceeds forty days and does not heal, then place a sharp, corrosive medicine on it until the bone is exposed; and grind it according to its chapter.
And there is another mode of cautery for a fistula, which some of the first ones called it. Apply to the location of the fistula, and find it; then place upon it a fine cannula (camahan), that is, a fine tube, whose form this is [draws a diagram]. And pour upon it a quantity of drachmae of liquid lead, and hold your hand with good retention, and do not move the weak one at all, so that the liquid lead does not run or reach his eye.
It is necessary that you place on the eye of the weak one a hot compress steeped in egg white, or water.
For lead burns the spot of the fistula and heals it by a wonderful cure.
If the fistula is healed along with what we said through cautery, and cure, that is good. If not, then it is necessary to administer the nasal passage, and to bring back the fistula into the course of the nose, according to which it comes into its own proper place.
[Title: On the method of cauterizing in fissures of the lips.]
Many times fissures occur on the lip, which are called hairs, and especially in the lips of children.
Therefore, when you take care of these fissures along with what we said in the division of diseases, and cure does not help, then use a small cautery knife shaped like this [draws a diagram].
And let the hollow of it [the wound] be according to the subtlety of the blade.
Then place it [the hot iron] hastily into those cracks, until the cautery reaches the depth of the cracks.
Then take care of it with caustic until it heals.
Chapter on Cauterizing an Oral Fistula.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth: then it produces pus and bursts: afterwards it becomes putrid, and the pus runs and becomes a fistula: subsequently you should take care of it, and do not apply treatment to it, then it is necessary that fire be applied with caution according to its size, which can be contained in the fistula. Subsequently introduce the fire itself into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand, until the heated iron reaches its depth and end; do this once or twice.
Subsequently take care of it after that, with what has been said about treatment, until it is healed.
If the pus separates and heals, it will be good. And if it does not, then it is necessary to explore the place, and remove the corrupted bone according to what comes to its surface.
Chapter on Cauterizing in Softened Gums and Teeth.
When the gums become soft due to moisture and the teeth move, and it is treated with medicine but does not improve; then place the head of the sick person in your lap.
Subsequently apply fire cautery, whose shape will come later, so that you place the Cannula on the tooth; and introduce in it the heated cautery quickly; and hold your hand for a little while until the sick person feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth.
And remove your hand; then again apply the cautery several times, as you wish.
The sick person should fill his own bone with brine water, and hold it for an hour; and rinse it.
For the tooth is hardened by movement, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
Method of cauterization for tooth pain.
Chapter XXIII.
The cautery is with butter, take butter from the cow, and carry it in an iron cauldron or earthenware. Then receive the pot and cover it over the edge of the wound. Then immerse it in boiling butter and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it until it cools; then repeat it several times until the heat of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool or a cloth in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth; then place heated iron on top of it until the heat reaches the depth of the cavity of the tooth.
The cautery with fire is to heat the iron or brass pipe. Let there be something bulky in the body so that the sharpness of the fire does not reach the weak bone.
Then heat the cautery, whatever its shape will come; and place it on that tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do this several times as pain is relieved either on the same day or another day.
And when making an impression with the cautery, the weak bone should be filled with good butter and kept for an hour; then it is spit out.
And this is the shape of the cautery.
Cauterize with whatever tip you wish, as it is possible; and this is the form of the pipe.
Chapter on how to cauterize in ulcers.
When ulcers are due to phlegm and cold humors, and are not responding to medicines for digestion, and you wish a quick digestion; then use heated cautery with a hollow shape like this:
Having two open ends so that smoke exits at the cautery from one end: and place it ignited upon the ulcer once, and if necessary, again, until it reaches the depth of the ulcer.
If the ulcer is small: then place the cautery according to the size of the ulcer.
Then let it be for three days, and place warm butter on top of it until what the fire has burnt is removed.
Then treat it with tooth-paste ointment until the ulcer heals.
On the method of cauterization for the roughness of the vocal cords, and constriction of breathing.
When moisture collects over the windpipe and especially when it is accompanied by coldness of constitution, then the sick person should first be evacuated with dissolving medicines.
Then cauterize it in the neck at the root of the throat in a depressed place: and be careful not to reach the throat with the cautery nor the skin, unless something of the disease is involved.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the junction of the neck and collarbone in the lowest end of that joint: and let the cautery be small according to the method that was previously described.
Then treat it with what has been described before until it heals.

When there is coughing and sickness of the lungs due to cold moistures, and the patient does not have fever nor consumption (phthisis), and the illness is an old one: then cauterize it with two cauteries above the clavicle in shallow, empty, relaxed places. And (cauterize) with another one in the middle of the chest between two breasts; and let the cautery be a hollow one, as the previous one has been.
And if your (cauterization) is by pricking with a cautery called Punctum, whose shape has been described in the treatment of ear pain; and let there be pricks from thirty pricks up to about another.
Then take care of him with that (as described above), until he is cured.
And now let the cautery have three branches; according to this shape. Why is cauterization performed when you perform it with a substitute for three cauteries.

Chapter on the method of cauterizing the stomach.
When cold and much moisture occur in the stomach until it removes itself from its mixture, and catarrhs multiply for it, and continuous methods of treatment do not suffice: then the sick person should lie on his back, extend his legs, and put forth his hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, with a cautery of the size of a finger under the concavity of the chest and a hooked cautery, and two cauteries below the sides of one cautery, until the figure of the cauteries becomes a triangle. And extend between them so that they do not unite when there is pus.
And the depth of the cautery shall be the size of two thirds of the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be in this shape without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this shape: and let the cautery which makes this cautery be one in the shape of a circle according to this shape.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking it with the one who fears this cautery, and there is to be a mark made on the stomach according to the quantity desired, as with wax; then the same (stomach) is cauterized with the point cautery; then it is cared for with the cure that preceded until it heals.
On the method of cauterizing the epiploon coldly.
When there is pain in the epiploon due to coldness and moistness, or due to gross windiness until it exits from its natural outlet, and the sick person has been treated with what was said before, but does not improve, then the sick person should lie on his back on a table, and marks are made with wax with three points of cautery according to this figure, and the same quantity below the hypochondria, where the human elbow reaches; and there should be space between each cauterium equal to the thickness of a digit; and the cautery should be long enough for the body; and do not press your hand hard with the cauterium.
And the quantity to be burned should not exceed the thickness of the skin; half of it should not be added; and the sick person should stand on his feet.
If (the patient) is not standing, then let him lie down who has already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the form of the cautery.
And it is possible for you to use these three points of cautionery with a sharp-pointed cautery when you have subtlety and wisdom in the art.
And beware that you do not proceed to the utmost in cauterization, and when the thickness of the skin is burned, the body is burned completely, and it reaches the intestines; because the skin there is delicate, therefore know this.
Method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When it happens that there is an exiture, and you want to know if that abscess is in the liver flesh or its tunica: then, if it is in the liver flesh, a weak pain and heaviness without sharpness will occur; and if it is in the tunica of the liver, with intense pain, it becomes evident that the treatment has exhausted the doctors.
Therefore, the patient must lie down on his neck. Then form the place of the abscess with the hot iron; then heat the cautery that resembles a rod. And this is its shape. And cauterize with that iron until the entire skin is burned and it reaches the pus, until all the pus comes out; then treat him with treatments for discharge until he is healed.
And it is not necessary to use this method of cautery, unless the person's devotion to the art of medicine is prolonged; and whose hands these diseases occur with experience; then dare on such operations.
But it is better to abandon it in my opinion.
Method of cauterizing pleurisy.
The ancients said that the cautery with the roots of Aristolochia is to be used for cold pleurisy as follows. And you should receive from the dry roots of Aristolochia a longer root, which is found among them, and let it be as thick as a finger. Then immerse it in oil; then ignite it. Then cauterize with one iron in that which is between the junction of the collarbone and neck, and with two small irons under the jaw a little downward slope to the part that is below the beard.
And with two cauteries also, in that which is between the fifth and sixth ribs downwards towards the back slightly; and with one cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from behind: one in that which is between the two scapulae; and with two cauteries from the sides of the chest, the lower one being the one that is between the two scapulae.
And it is not necessary that you press your hand with the cautery, rather it should be done so that the smell of the skin is evident.
And certain ancients have said that there are some who use the cautery made of iron resembling a rod; they heat it and insert it into that which is between the ribs until they reach the abscess with it, and the pus comes out: as we said in the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is fear, for either the weak man dies immediately, or a fistula occurs at that place which does not heal.
Chapter 32. On the method of cauterizing the Spleen Head.
When you treat the disease of the spleen, as we said in the treatment of diseases and your treatment does not work, then cauterization is used for it according to three modes, all of which are correct.
One is that you make three or four cauteries in the length of the spleen according to the figure of the cauteries of the liver, whose preceding figure has already been given.
And let the thickness between each cautery be as thick as a finger or more or less.
And the method of cauterization shall be equal to that which we said in the cauterization of the liver.
And you must not press your hand with the cautery; and let the patient be lying on his back.
Another method of cauterization is: holding two cauteries, as we have said in the chapter on dislocation of the humerus; and lift the skin, which is directly over the spleen, where it reaches the weak elbow on the left side; and your lifting of the skin should be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then insert two hot irons deeply, until they pierce the skin from the other side; then withdraw the cautery; thus four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another iron having three prongs.
Then care for the cautery after you release it to emit pus for many days; indeed, it is more beneficial than the others that have come before in the treatment.
Chapter on the method of cauterization in Hydropsy.
A cautery does not fall in Hydropsy, unless strictly indicated.
When you treat a Hydropsy patient according to the methods of treatment that we have mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize it with four cauteries around the navel, one over the stomach, another over the liver, one over the spleen, two behind the back between the vertebrae, and one on the front of the stomach, and another on the front of the heart; and the depth of the cautery should be approximately the thickness of the skin.
Then release the open cautery to let it emit pus for a long time.
Do not evacuate the patient from treatment after cauterization, as it is necessary that two intentions be applied to him; and healing will hasten towards him with divine aid.
The form of the cautery with which the abdomen is cauterized should be clavicular; according to its previous form. And the one with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped, according to its previous form.

When they are incised in hydropic conditions and filled with citron water: it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot at the site between auricularem and anularem [joints]; then remove your hand with the cautery, without twisting it; afterwards, remove your hand; do not return to it at all.
For indeed, the citron water will boil, and let the cautery be in this shape [round or oval].
Then, make two cauteries on both legs and let each leg have two cauteries; let the cautery have an end like a small knife, and let it be along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other lower than that, about halfway down the leg; and above the hip, there should be two cauteries; leave the open cautery without prolonged treatment so that some water boils out of it; then treat it with what I have said before.
On the method of cauterization in the opening of the abdomen.
In cuius modi cauteri in fistula vesicae
When the abdomen is opened by cold and moisture so that its powers of retention and digestion in the stomach and intestines are weakened, it should be treated with methods of healing, but it does not heal: and you see a sick person who can tolerate an excessive cautery due to strong vitality, then you cauterize it with a large cautery over its own stomach, according to what was previously mentioned in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery and four fine cauteries around the navel and a fine cautery on the clavicle, and with a large cautery over the alum on top of the small intestines or with two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moisture and a sick person who can tolerate it, then you cauterize it with a large cautery over the breastbone and over the entire ilium: and possibly you may add two small cauteries near the stomach.
For it is a treatment that does not miss its effect.

In cuius modi cauteri in fistula recti, in
When there are old hemorrhoids in the anus, many or one, and they are thick, cold or corrupted with moisture, and they are treated with what was said in the division, but healing does not occur: then cauterize it with three cauteries over the lower part of the hipbone slightly below the iliac crest in a triangular shape under the almond-shaped mark, and with a cautery under the navel like two fingers.

Incapitulare de modo cauterizandi althelulum

Chapter on the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Incipitur de modo cauterizandi fistulum in anum

Chapter on how to cauterize the anus in dislocation.

[Heading: The method of cauterizing in Sciatica.]
When pain occurs in the buttock of an ankle and its cause is coldness and dampness: and the sick person is treated as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not help, and it worsens: then it is necessary that you release the sick person from thick humors with foul pills or with artificial pills and similar things. And be careful with all your cauterizations so that you do not burn the nerve or a major artery and harm the sick person through this, or cause contracture.
And I myself have seen one and another who cauterized above the tendon [limb], and burned it in the cauterization, and the leg swelled until the tumor reached the foot, and it was perforated all over, and the whole foot decayed; then there was a rupture of the abdomen, and death followed that.
If the pain is in two parts at the same time, cauterize each one according to this method.
Some wise men have said that in the cauterization of an aneurysm, this is the method for doing it. Make a cup-shaped instrument of iron, whose diameter is half a palm [about 2 inches]; and at its opening it should be according to the size of the nail tip or less; and within this cup there should be a third cup.
And let the space that is between all the cups be equal to the size of a knuckle; and let the cups be open from two sides; and let their height be like a knuckle or two knuckles; and make handles of iron appropriately for the cups.
Then heat it in fire until it turns red and sparks; then place it on the dish of the weak anvil laid upon a healthy side. Therefore, cauterize it with three round cauteries at once.
Then let it be for three days. Then pack it with butter; and leave the open wound for many days. Then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Says Albucasis, in this form of cautery, we are not accustomed to use it much due to the terror of its appearance; and therefore, because few are found who dare upon it.
Nevertheless, it is among the good cauterizations for him who can bear it, and finds a place for it.
The cautery with stimulating medicines is to make two samia having a perforated armillary sphere, into which descends the hinge of its door from brass or iron, long enough for the wall; whose height should be two knots, or as if they themselves.
And let the space that is between them be of the thickness of a finger, and they should be open below and above; and let them hold each other according to this form.
Then place it on the dish of the weak anvil, laid upon a healthy side. And press your hand heavily on the dish of the weak anvil. Then pour water between the two circles that has been heated slightly with fire and hold it for the length of an hour; let the weak one bear its biting and burning, for he finds the bite like fire until the biting ceases.
Then wash your hand with the tool and clean the weak anvil with warm water along with sweet water; then let it be for three days.
Place the butter on top of it until the burnt blackness is removed; and let it stay for some days, and a pus will run from it. This is the last remedy.
Then treat that with ointments until it heals.
If the pain extends to the hip or leg, make a socket for it containing water, as you did with the anchor equally.
This is the method of hot water: and I have already written about it in the treatise on the correction of medications. Take alkali and half the quantity of unburnt lime, grind each separately; put them in a new pot whose lower part is pierced with a small hole, according to the amount that enters the radius; put another earthenware pot below it; throw alkali and lime into water, which will submerge them by a finger; when you compress them with your hand, good compression; let go of the pot until the sharp water comes down through the pierced part of the earthenware pot.
Then combine all that water and throw it on another lime; boil until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strong for sharpness, which is administered in many medical operations, and in the cauterization of other members. Since it performs the operation of fire itself.
And among the medicines are those with which anchors are cauterized, also as tesisie, and honey of cardamom, and lime with soap, so that each is mixed together.
And Galen himself reported in his telling about the cure of a man, from whom pain in the anchor and the sciatic vein was cured; he said it was very effective. And he said, because it does not require another treatment, and because it was healed from one application, until he returned, because perhaps he himself went into the bath, and already came out healthy from it.
And it is to be taken from green mustard: and if green mustard is not found, dry mustard should be taken, fresh: and it should be ground well with some fat, and placed on the place where there is pain, or leg, or hip: and it should be tied, and left for a quantity of three hours, or until the patient feels the relaxation caused by the heat. Then introduce him into the bath.
When his body becomes warm, introduce him into the sun. For the pain retreats, and it heals.
And know that no one should use cautery with these medicines unless after the evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides says that goat's feces, when used to cauterize the sciatic vein, should be applied in this way: and make the cautery according to this method. Take wool and immerse it in ancient oil, and place it on the deep place that is between the big toe of the foot and the heel, and nearer to the heel.
Then take dry goat's feces and burn it in fire until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it on the wool and leave it until it is extinguished. Repeat this process. Do not stop doing this until the sensation reaches to the ankle and the pain stops.
And this method of cautery is called Vaccinum cautery.

This disease often occurs in small children.

On the method of cauterization for gout, and its associated pains.
Chapter XLVI.
When therefore gout (Podagra) is treated for a cold cause and the pains are not relieved, then cautery removes them.

Chapter on the method of cauterizing ruptures.
When rupture occurs in the groins and the intestine or spermatic cord descends towards the testicle, which is beginning: then it is necessary to order the sick person to fast on his own day. And he shall use from the softening substances, so that the stool may descend from his belly.
Then he shall sit between your hands upon his back: and command him to hold his breath until it comes out or appears a hernia or an intestine.
Then bring him back with your fingers and mark the place of rupture on his neck with wax seal together with a seal like half of a circle above his body.
Then heat the cautery in this shape until it becomes white and throw sponges on it. Then bring the intestine or hernia into its hollow. Then let the servant put his hand on the place so that the intestine does not come out: and you have already opened between the legs of the weak one, and placed a pan under him and another servant is serving at his legs and another one at his chest holding his hands.
Then place the cautery on the seal upon him with your hand holding it straight. Hold him until you find the bone with it; or if you have not found the bone in the first attempt, do it again with another position.
And be careful to observe the exit of the intestine at the time of your cautery, lest you burn him and harm or kill him by that or great suffering.
And know this, that when you do not find the bone with the cautery, your work does not succeed.
It is necessary that the cautery be subtle for children according to their measurement.
Then take care of him with ointments until he is well.
Let the weak one lie down on his back for forty days until the wound is closed.
It is necessary that you provide him with food according to the length of his treatment time, so that his belly may be softened and not expel the intestine in attempts or in evacuations.
Then when one wishes to operate after forty days, then administer a correctly made bandage and hold it for another forty days.
And reduce from labor, and fill with food and drink, and with vehement voices.
For when this treatment is used, thus it heals completely by cure.
And I will say the cure for hernias with an incision in its own chapter.
But when hernias occur in the rest of the abdomen, and they are beginning and there is a desire not to add them, then cauterize the hernia with a round cautery according to its size: and let that which is burned be as third of it from then on. Then care for it as I have said: and do not add it.
And some of the first ones have said that a hernia should be cauterized with a triangular cautery in this shape.
After signing it with an encase, and a line is placed which is across its width on the upper side of the hernia, and another line downwards. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery tongs.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing in pains due to accident or trauma.
Chapter XLVIII.
When pain occurs in some members due to an accident or trauma, and the pain persists for a long time, and there is no healing with medications, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with a puncture cautery.
And let the cautery for all members be according to its size, and its smallness, and weakness, and power, and location of twisting, and pain from it.
If it heals with the first cautery, it is good. If not: then apply the cautery on him again.
Because it is customary for these pains to move from one limb to another that is nearer. Therefore, you must follow them with the cautery until the sick person is healed.
Chapter on the mode of cauterizing in leprosy.
Leprosy are sometimes benefited by cautery, with great benefit. And primarily the types of leprosy caused by corruption of phlegm and melancholy: therefore when considering cauterization of it.
If leprosy is beginning and you have treated it with what was said in the division and it does not improve or stop: then beware of corruption spreading over his entire constitution; then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the head, known as the fontanel, and the second below it facing the forehead at the end of the hairline, and two on top of the two horns, and one behind on the occipital bone.
And finally place your hand with the cautery slightly, until it makes a small impression on the bone, and the skin is separated from it; so that the expiration of gross vapors from it is alleviated, and cauterize also over the spleen, according to what preceded.
But if leprosy has spread over the sick person and is apparent: then it is necessary that you cauterize with these cauteries which were mentioned on the head, and a cautery over the tip of the nose, and two cauteries over both cheekbones, and two cauteries over both shoulder blades, and six over both hip bones, and one large one over the alhahosos at the base of the spine and one above it, in the almeidati; and two on the ankles: that is, one on each ankle, and two on the elbows, and two on the wrists, and two on the tendons of the chest, and cauterize over the entire joint of his fingers of both hands and feet, and cauterize over the entire heel of both feet, and the soles of both hands.
Be careful not to burn the nerves that are on top of the heel bone, last one.
And sometimes it is burned with an iron over the cheek bone, and another over the bone of the stomach, and another over the jawbone.
And know that, the more cautery you apply, the greater is the help, and the better it is.
And know that the sick person does not feel pain from the cautery, as healthy people do; therefore, because his body has already become numb.
It is necessary that the cauteries be of different sizes and shapes according to the members and joints; following the types of iron tools.
Then take care to burn with cautery made from wheat flour and honey, and with other treatments until it heals.
Chapter on the mode of burning in unconsciousness.
When a member becomes unconscious and is treated with medicines, oils, plasters, and does not heal, then burn the unconscious member with cauteries, according to the size of the member or its smallness.
And let your cautery penetrate somewhat into the depth of the skin. Then take care of it with an ointment until it heals.
And sometimes the burning is done for a kind of unconsciousness that happens in the hand and foot, in the joints of the back near the exits of the nerves that move that member; and the unconsciousness is removed.
But do not presume to do it unless he who knows the anatomy of the members and the exit of the nerves moving the body is present.
Chapter L.I (caput means chapter or head)
When an ulcer becomes old and does not improve with any of the remedies of medicine; then burn it with a deep cautery somewhat, according to the thickness of the skin, until the white part is removed and the color changes.
Then take care of yourself with a mixture of grain of wheat, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of fennel, and blood of a dove, and blood of a heron; from each of these be equal parts; mix all these together, spread them on a cloth, and let them adhere to the place until it heals.
Method of cauterization for Cancer.
When cancer is beginning and you wish to stop it; then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, as it rotates (revolves).
The wise have said that it should be cauterized with the last cautery in the middle.
But to me it does not seem good; for I fear that it will burn (ulcerate); and I have already seen this happen many times.
And it is better to cauterize around it with a circular cautery, as we have said; or with many cauteries.
Method of cauterization for Adubelati (carcinoma of the anus).
When someone has a boil, and it slows down in maturation, either due to an excess causing it or due to the person being old and weak with little blood, or due to time and the desire to hasten in the maturation of the boil, then cauterize its surrounding area with small and numerous cauteries. Then let it go [the boil]. For it will hasten in maturation by itself.
If you wish to pierce it with a cautery, then heat the cautery with fire, which has this form.
Place it in the center of the boil until it penetrates the skin; let the cautery be weak, so that the flow of pus may be relieved.
Then care for [the wound] until it heals.
Chapter on cauterizing a cancerous tumor.
Chapter LIV.
Corrosion is nothing but walking corruption consuming itself, just as fire consumes dry wood.
If you see corrosion in a place that can bear cautery with fire, then the cautery should be large, small and large nails as appropriate to the place where the corrosion is present.
Then cauterize it from all sides until you root out the entire corruption and there remains nothing of it deep within.
Then let it be for three days and place over the cauterized places ground sulfur with oil until all scabs are removed and all corruption is gone.
Then care for it with ointments that promote flesh growth.
If after three days you see that new flesh is growing healthily without corruption, it is good.
And if not: then repeat the cautery on the part remaining from the corrupted places.
Corrosion is sometimes treated with a strong medicine. The sore rises where the cautery was applied.
However, cautery with fire is more effective; and I have already said that cautery with a strong medicine is useful in division; therefore, use it when you need it there.
Chapter on the method of cauterizing nails and warts.
Chapter 50.
This ailment frequently occurs in the lower parts of feet: and it is a large, filtered matter that harms the foot.
And indeed, among them there are two modes of cautery: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
As for the one with fire, it is to be made like a concave cautery similar to a vulture's pen: which should be made of iron, according to its size containing a nail at all parts: and it should have delicate edges.
Then place the heated one upon the nail. Then turn the hand with the cautery around the nail, until the cautery reaches the depth of the nail: and leave it for three days, until it begins to discharge pus. Then apply ointment of wild malva leaves crushed with salt on it, and leave the ointment upon it during the night. For this, it will be uprooted from its roots.
Then care for the place with a healing salve until it is healed.
If they are not converted and frequently occur on the surface of the body, especially in hands and feet: then administer cautery with hot water: and it is to take a cannula of copper or iron or from a vulture's pen: and place it upon the nail or althea. Then pour a little hot water into the cannula: hold your hand and you turn it with the compression of your hand for a short time, so that the tip of the cannula is pressed against the root of the nail, and let the hot water find its way to the deep, to the root of the nail: and let the patient wait for a short while after the bite of the hot water an hour.
Then release it, for the nail is uprooted with its roots.
Perform the procedure on each one (part) after the other, until you reach all that are within the body.
Then care for them once they have been removed, with that which generates flesh from ointments.
On the method of cauterizing in the tremor (shaking palsy).
When trembling due to coldness in a nerve occurs to someone, or from quartan fever, or something else: then it should be cauterized with four or five cauteries on the dorsal spine, and between each dorsal spine with a cautery, and in its chest with a cautery, and on its stomach with a cautery.
For trembling ceases with cauterization of oil, and health hastens from the illness of coldness.
On the method of cauterizing Albatheir (Al-Buhaitar).
Chapter LVII (67th chapter).
Sometimes in the body Albathir (Abscesses) are expelled, that is, pustules which come from corrupted materials.
Therefore, when they appear, they should first be cauterized on every head of the pustule with a subtle cautery and myrtle wood, whose tip is lit with fire. Or with the root of long Aristolochia (Aristolochia serpentaria). Or with a lens-shaped cautery.
And sometimes they are cauterized for the beginning of its (Abscess's) expulsion according to this method, and they do not increase; and excess is broken, making them (the pustules) disappear, and healed from it.
Nevertheless, it should be done afterwards with venesection.
On the method of cauterizing in bleeding from an artery in a wound.
Often bleeding from an artery occurs which is cut near a wound, which happens from outside, or at the incision of a boil, or a cautery member, and similar things; and it becomes difficult to separate him.
When therefore it happens to someone, then approach with your hand to the opening of the artery, and place your pointing finger upon it: and tie it tightly, until the blood is held under your finger and nothing escapes from it.
Then place a small oil lamp cautionery, and many in number: and blow upon them until they are very hot.
Then take one of them, either small or large, according to the wound and place where the artery is broken, and place the cautionery upon the vein, after you remove your finger quickly: hold the cautionery until the blood is cut off.
If it is expelled when you lift your finger from the opening of the artery, and extinguish the cautionery, then take another cautionery quickly, from those which are prepared in the fire.
Therefore do not cease to do that with one after another until the blood is cut off.
And beware, lest you burn the nerve which is there, and some other evil happens to the weak person.
And know that when blood flows from the artery, then it is not possible to cut it off: especially since the artery is large, unless with one of four methods. Or with a cautionery, as we have said. Or with extraction, when it has not been extracted. For when it is pulled out, the ends contract and the blood is cut off. Or it may be tied with a strong thread. Or medicines of the property for cutting off blood are placed upon it, and it is tightened with a suitable constriction plaster.
But he who administers the cutting off with a thread and tightening with a bandage, or placement of burning objects and similar things, does not fully cure him, unless rarely.
If it happens to anyone and the physician is not present nor the medicine: then begin with the positioning of the index finger over the opening of that vein, as we have told, and with strong compression until the blood is obstructed from the superior part of the wound, and on the artery. And let the finger not be removed, on it with cold water of strong coldness always, until the blood freezes, and swells, and is cut off.
And meanwhile let him consider in it what needs cautery or medicine.
Chapter on incisions, perforations, and phlebotomy in wounds and their likes.

And for that reason, it is necessary that the caution be stronger because in the operation that is in this chapter, evacuation often falls with blood, with which life stands during the opening of a vein or an incision over an abscess, or the opening of the exit, or treatment of the wound, or extraction of an arrow, or incision on a stone and their likes: from all of which are associated tremor, fear, and death occurs in many of them.
And I warn you, lest it fall upon you where there is hesitation, for sometimes it falls upon you in this art as with the modes of men with the modes of weaknesses.
