[Section] On the treatment of water that collects in the heads of children.
Chapter 1.
Know that this ailment often occurs in boys during childbirth: either when the midwife tightens the boy's head without restraint.
And it sometimes happens due to hidden causes which are not known.
And indeed I myself have not seen this sickness in others than boys: and to everyone whom I saw it happened, death followed: therefore it seemed to me fitting to abandon the operation in it.
And indeed I myself have seen a boy whose head was filled with water, and his head swelled every day until he could not sit upon himself, because of the size of his head: and the moisture increased, until he died.
And indeed this moisture, either accumulates between skin and bone; or accumulates under the bone on the sacrum.
And the operation on him, if there is moisture between skin and bone, and the abscess is small, then it is necessary that you make a slit in the middle of the head, one fissure in width: and the length of the fissure shall be as two knuckles, until the moisture runs out.
And this is the form of the trepan (trephine).
If then the moisture is more increased, and the abscess is larger, then place these two slits, according to this form.
And if the moisture is under the bone, and the sign of it is that you see openings of the skull from every part: and water gushes out when you press it with your hand towards the inside, and it does not hide from you: then it is necessary that you make three slits in the middle of the head, according to this method.
And after the incision, extract all the moisture. Then tie the slits with bandages and small pieces of cloth. Then pour wine and oil on it for five days.
Then cut the ligament and care for the wound with probes and ointments.
And do not let go of the head without balance (or equilibrium). Feed the sick with dry food of slight moisture until the limb recovers and is healed.
Another method of incision is to consider where it appears that the size of the abscess is, and the collection of water (or pus).
Because sometimes it is more in the back of the head or in the forehead, or in the right or left side.
Therefore, with incision, ascend where it appears to you the abscess and filling of water: and cut it as far as possible for you.
And observe that you do not incise the artery and let blood flow, and the sick person dies from this blood loss with the evacuation of moisture.
Section on incising arteries that are after the ears.
Chapter II.
When catarrhs occur to the eyes or chest and it persists, and no treatment with medications is effective: then the final cure is in that, incision of these two arteries.
Therefore, when you wish to cut them (the arteries), let the sick person shave his head. Then scrape the place with a rough cloth, so that the arteries appear. Then let the sick person tighten his neck with any of his own towels. Then consider where the vein is pulsating. And both places are depressed areas that are behind the ears and are rarely hidden, except in some people.
Then mark both with hot iron and cut each one with a spatula on both sides, the incision reaching the bone: and let it be across the width of the head.
And if you wish, introduce a spatula under the artery and cut it from above with the incision.
And let the length of the incision be as two fingers joined.
When a vein is cut, blood gushes out by pulsatile discharge, which leaps to the inner parts with frequent jumps.
If, however, an artery does not appear to the sense, then it is necessary that measurements be made with the cubit (span) of three fingers. Then mark with encaustum (wax), and cut up to the bone.
And that which should be drawn out from the blood is 6 ounces, and perhaps you will draw more or less from it. Cut (the artery) entirely according to the quantity that appears to you from the strength of the patient and the fullness of the artery itself.
Then, consider for the wound. If there remains anything towards the bone from the sifac (gristle), then cut it so that a hot abscess does not occur; then stitch the wound with linen strips.
Then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
Chapter on the extraction of arteries that are in the temples.
Chapter III.
When an old hemicrania or acute catarrh due to acidic moistures and warmth in the temples occurs, or an old wound, violent, and similar ones: and it is treated with methods of curative medicine, but it does not help: then we have been experienced in dealing with such ailments, extraction of arteries from the temples, or cauterization of them, as we have narrated.
The method of operation for these is to shave the sick hairs that are on the temples and stretch towards the visible artery in the temple. It is indeed shown to you by its pulse and it rarely hides except in a few men or when there is a violent cold.
If it hides from you, then the sick person should bind his head with any cloth of his, then rub the place with a rough cloth. Or fumigate the place with hot water until it appears to you in a clear manifestation. Then take the spatholem, which I have prepared earlier. Then scrape the skin with it easily until you reach the artery. Then thrust a hook into it and extract it upwards until you extract it from the skin, and make it come out from all sides of the tunics that are under it.
If, however, the artery is delicate: then turn it with the tip of the hook. Then cut off the part according to its length so that the ends contract and there is no blood flow. For if it is not cut and if it is not separated, the blood does not rise deeply.
Then evacuate the blood up to six ounces, down to three.
If the artery is large: then it should be tied in two places with strong double thread, silk or gut, or with alum-soaked threads so that putrefaction does not reach it before the wound is consolidated and there is blood flow.
Then cut off the excess, which is between two ligaments. Do that at that hour, or another hour.
And if you wish, cauterize it with a cautery up to the bone, with a small cautery; until its ends are cut off and it remains in place for that same operation.
And it is better work, unless if he is weak with a fever, or of cool constitution. Because the cautery is from those that help to stop wetnesses. Therefore it is better remedy.
And after the extraction of the arteries, the place should be filled with old clay; and lumps well-made powdered charcoal should be placed on top of it.
And after the solution, it is to be treated with dry medications that cause flesh to grow and with linen until it heals.
If, however, during the operation there is a bleeding from an artery, then hasten to cut it off with a cautery, or fill the place with wax; and press your hand until the blood stops. If there is nothing from those present for you, then place your finger on the place until the blood freezes. And anoint the place with water of intense cold, until the sharpness subsides and it is bound as necessary.
And because the vein is lighter and easier to extract, it is to cauterize the vein with this cautery having two blades; and the sharpness of the two blades should be like alum. However, they are much less sharp than two knives. Because if they are as sharp as two knives, both freeze; and do not cut flesh with swiftness. Since they have some thickness, heat is to be kept in them and the flesh is cut swiftly; whence this work is better than any other, lighter and easier.
This is the form of the cautery.
And let the space between two knives be of the size of a finger's thickness, after you mark two places with wax; then place both hot ones until they reach the bone and cut the vein in two places: to loosen what is between its extremities. They will not be completely fused with this cautery.
Chapter IV.
Chapter on the treatment of frequent and acute tears from the eyes.
When tears are persistent and their course is from the veins that are on the outside of the skull of the head: and no treatment medicine is applied to them with medicines, and you see the face of the sick person turning red, and you feel walking on the forehead as if it were the walking of ants: and the eyes are weakened, moist, so much so that the hairs on them are already corroded with corrosion: and the eyelids have been heated due to the sharpness of the tears: then, in the treatment of them, the ancients resorted to this operation, and they named it treatment, with a sword.
To command the sick person to shave the hairs on his forehead. Then make three equal cuts in the forehead, each as long as a finger, and let the length of one cut be approximately equal to the nose's length in the middle of the forehead, and the second one slightly longer than the movement of the elbow, and the third on the other side: and avoid cutting arteries that are on both sides: and extend your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and let the space of all cuts be the width of three connected fingers: and have a piece of sponge prepared or dry cloth, with which you can squeeze blood.
Then insert the sharp ends of two spatulas whose shape is as follows: From the first incision on the temple side to the second incision: and scrape with it the entire skin that is between the two cuts, along with the flesh above the eye. Then do the same from the middle incision to the second incision. Then remove the first spatula and insert another tool called a sharp scalpel from one side, not sharp on the other side. And this is its form.
Place the sharp side facing towards the flesh attached with skin and the blunt side facing the bone; push it until it reaches the middle fissure, and cut along with it all vessels that descend from the head to the eyes, except that the incision should be continuous as far as it appears on the skin.
Then make that [instrument] in the middle fissure up to another fissure.
And when an equal amount of blood flows out, squeeze the places from the vessels that are coagulated.
Then place a linen cloth from an old oven on every fissure and put over them small pieces soaked in wine, oil or vinegar. And beware of developing a hot abscess.
On the third day dissolve the ligature and administer a large infusion with warm water. Then treat that [area] with a basilicon ointment and the others that are used for wounds until it is healed.
Chapter 5.
Chapter on treating sharp tears and catarrh of the eyes from the interior parts of the head.
When someone experiences sharp, frequent catarrh or tears, and you see that their eyes are weakened, small, and their sight is already diminished; and the eyelids are ulcerated, and hairs fall from them, and there is intense pain deep within the head, accompanied by sneezing: then take, among these conditions, what those materials or catarrh do not come unless from many veins.
A better treatment for them is this. And it is to advise the sick one to shave his forehead. Then make one cut in the middle of the forehead, or a little less wide on either side, starting from the left temple to the right temple; and let the incision reach as far as the bone; and move your hand away from the temples that move during chewing until the bone is exposed; and dry up all the blood with a sponge.
Then separate the cut between the two lips of the wound with a heated iron or with linen rags. Then tie it above with thread; and soak the thread with wine and oil to prevent a hot abscess from forming.
And when you release it, and see that the abscess is about to subside: then you must break open the bone until flesh begins to grow within it.
Then care for it with a drying dressing that promotes the growth of flesh; as if you were to take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of colophony, and prepare an ointment from them, which should be applied for the growth of flesh in these wounds.
Chapter VI.
[Paragraph on the treatment of an ear wound.]
Everything that falls into the ear is one of four types: either a mineral stone, similar to a stone such as iron and wood; or it is from a plant, such as chickpeas and beans; or it is liquid, such as water, vinegar, and similar substances; or it is some kind of animal.
When a stone falls into the ear, or any kind of stone not growing within the ear, expose the ear alone: if therefore you see a stone, then pour something from violated oil or sesame into the ear. Then administer extraction of it, and make him sneeze with some snuff, and place cotton in the nostrils at the coming of the sneeze, after you put around the ear fragments from cloth or wool, and stretch the ear towards above.
For many times it goes out with this care.
If it does not go out, then administer the extraction of it with Genti, that is, with subtle Pizigaroli: whose shape is this.
If therefore it goes out with Genti, it is good.
And if not, then administer the extraction of it with a blind subtle hook in little repetitions.
If it does not go out by that, then make a pipe from copper and insert the end of the pipe into the ear opening quite a lot, and plug what is around the pipe with wax softened with oil so that there is no wind path except the pipe: then draw out with your strong attraction.
For many times it goes out with what we have said. If it does not go out in this way: then take from helkalimbat or from liquid, that is, prepared gluten which birds are caught with, a small amount of it: and put it at the end of the radius when you have placed a suitable cup over it: then insert it into the ear opening with ease after you have removed the ear from moisture.
If it does not go out with all that we have said, then hurry to cut it before a hot abscess or spasm occurs.
And the method of cutting is, to take an unwell person first in the head: and draw out from his blood according to its power. Then make the patient sit with you and turn his ear upward, and make a small opening at the base of the ear in the fatty part at its lowest point; let the opening be in the shape of a moon until you reach the stone; then remove it together with what is possible for you using your instruments.
Then make an opening with caution and care from your side until it heals.
If something falls into the ear that is one of the grains which grow and swell, then administer extraction for it.
If it does not come out on its own, then take a thin, delicate probe of this shape.
And administer with it the removal of that species from the grains which fall into the ear and do not do this when you think that the grain is already humidified by the ear's moisture before putting it in many fragments; then remove it with forceps, or with a delicate implement, or with suction, as we said, since extraction is relieved.
However, when water enters the ear, the patient should use sneezing with it at first and already fill his ear with some heated old wine; and the water is lying on top of that ear where the water is. If it comes out through this [the probe], it is good.
And if it does not: then take many small and soft stones, heat them slightly with fire, and have the patient insert one from them into the ear's opening; and salt his foot on that side and strike with another stone upon the stone in the ear. Therefore, do not stop doing this with stones and stones until all the water comes out.
And now the water comes out in such a way that you can take one from parchment or reed and insert its end into the ear; and ignite the other end with fire until it burns as much as possible. Then proceed with another syringe, and do this repeatedly until all the water comes out: and extract it with a cannula according to what was previously stated on the stone.
When extracting an animal that has entered it (if its body is small, like a flea, or similar), care for it as I said in the division.
But if it has a large body, which can be felt by touch: then administer its extraction with forceps and curettes: and its substance is easier for all who are required to work in the ear.
In the extraction of worms generated in the ear, when you care for it with what I said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and your care does not help: then it is necessary to look at the ear in sunlight. If therefore something appears there from worms, then extract it with forceps or subtle curettes.
If however nothing appears there, then take a cannula with this form, narrow at the bottom, wide at the top: and insert its fine end into the ear according to the capacity that the sick person can tolerate: then suck with strong suction. Repeat this until all the worms come out.
If they do not obey you to leave (the ear), then surround the cannula with poppy seeds and beeswax, as I said on the stone.
If they do not come out with what I said, then administer the distillations that the ancients have been familiar with for killing worms: and you will find this in the treatment of distillations.
And let your outflow be with olive oil and medications into the ear with this tool, whose shape is depicted here. As you see, make it from silver or brass, narrow at the bottom and wide at the top, with a small hole at the bottom.
The implement within the concavity of the cannula should be made of suitable bronze. Take therefore the radish, and roll its surface with an appropriate covering; then pour oil, or juice, or whatever medicine you wish into the cannula; let it be made of gold; then insert the heated radish tip, and press it gently with your hand until the oil in the concavity is forced out and the sick person feels it inside; and whatever is poured into the ear should already be slightly heated by fire; take care not to distill anything cold into it; for medicine does not tolerate extreme coldness.
Chapter VII.
On the treatment of auricular impaction (Gold filling).
Sometimes, some infants are born from their mothers' wombs without the auditory passages being pierced.
And it also happens to some people that an auricular impaction occurs as a result of a wound or growth within the ear.
And this auricular impaction sometimes occurs deep within the ear canal, which is not visible to the eye; and sometimes it occurs near the outer ear opening, and can be seen.
Therefore, that which occurs deep within the ear, and is not apparent to the eye, is difficult to cure in many cases.
And in that which is visible to the eye, one should place the sick person's ear on the sun and observe it; then if you see the impaction, open it with a fine spatula whose shape is as follows: its end should have a small notch, part of which is sharp; the rest of the spatula should be made of two rounded sides to avoid damaging the ear.
If the auricular impaction is due to a growth within the ear, then hold it with a fine tweezer and cut it out easily and forcefully until all the growth is removed.
If there is an opening in the depth of the ear: then take thin radiation, linen, and heat it slightly with fire; afterwards send it into the ear's flesh.
If you find an opening with it, when the patient is weakened by illness and deafness, attempt to open it easily; be careful not to wound the nerves of the ear.
Then place linen in the ear according to the size of the hole you have made, and wrap it with Egyptian ointment; do this for several days until you are assured that the wound is healed.
Or take linen and immerse it in rosewater, grind zinc into powder over it, and use it.
If you see the ear already discharging pus: then take out the linen and let it dry with another piece of linen that has been wrapped in a cerotic made with rose oil, until the warm pus settles; then care for it until it is healed.
If there is bleeding instead (of pus): then immerse a sponge or cloth in cold water and place it on the ear; and use the rest of the treatment that was mentioned for removing the blood flow, in the treatise on distillations.
Chapter on treating Eyelids by Althelas.
Chapter VIII.
Those who occur in the eyelids of the eyes are sometimes moist and sometimes dry.
Therefore, hold them with forceps or tweezers, and cut them at their roots with a spatula. Then place powdered zinc over the area.
If blood flows from them, then cauterize them with a fine lenticular cautionery.
And cauterizing them is better after an incision. Multotiens enim redeunt quando remanet ex radicibus suis aliquid: They often return when something remains from their roots. And when they are cauterized with fire, those roots are burned, and they do not return.
§ On the care of swollen eyelids.
Chapter IX.
Often it happens that something similar to a swollen eyelid occurs in its strength and hardness, and for this reason it is called Grando; and it is an accumulation of thick moisture on the upper eyelid, and on the lower eyelid.
Therefore, the operation is to see if it is a Grando proceeding from that which appears on the eyelid, and if they move to all parts, and its nature is easy.
Make an incision therefore above it in a lengthwise direction. Then scrape off from all sides with ease, until it reaches the end. Then hang it down with a hook and cut it off.
If, however, the cutting off of it is not prepared for you beforehand, unless you pierce the eyelid with a slight incision first, then it hurts the weak one in some way.
If the incision is large: Then join it with a stitch, and take care of it until it heals.
And if it is small, no harm will come to you from it. Anointing restores it and fleshes it out.
If the Grando is turned towards the inner part of the ear and lies on its outer surface, then turn the eyelid inside out, and hang the Grando down with a hook; besides that, you will need an incision, and press it from all sides.
If the eyelid is stretched by the incision, no harm will come to you from it.
Then wash the eye after the incision of the Grando with salt water; and take care of the place until it fleshes out, until the weak one heals.
On the treatment of swellings on the eyelids.
De curatione ulceris oculi qui est
The swelling which arises on the upper eyelid is called Axirnath, and this happens most frequently in children. It causes their eyes to become heavy, and they get cataracts in the mornings and are unable to see the light of the sun, because tears flow towards it; and for that reason you can always see them lying on their faces and sleeping on them, and their eyelids are wet under the eyebrows, which have already been covered by swelling. The appearance of the Axirnath is visible to the eye, and when you press the place with your fingers, you feel the Axirnath between them.
And the method of treatment is that the patient should place his head in your lap.
Then take a linen cloth and prepare a bandage in it. Make a circle of the bandage according to the size that contains the Axirnath on all sides. Place it on top of the bandage, and press it with your fingers on all sides to gather the Axirnath in the middle of the circle.
Then find a place in the middle of the wetness with a small incision, and the incision should not be larger than that which occurs in phlebotomy in deep veins.
Or it is necessary to make an incision through the entire skin until you reach the Axirnath, because in many cases the Axirnath comes out from the opening like a piece of white fat.
Pull it out with the cloth that you have inserted between your fingers on the outside; and you turn your hand to the right and left until it is dispersed. Be careful not to add anything in the incision so that you do not reach the eye with the spatula and harm it.
If the Axirnath is not apparent to you at the beginning of the crack, you shall add a little into the crack with ease until the Axirnath appears. Then remove it as we have said.
Then immerse the cloths in vinegar and water, and place them over the place, and tie it with small stones.
And there are men who grind salt, and they place it in the hollow of the crack, so that it melts what remains from that moisture.
Then take care of it until it heals.
If, however, a boil occurs at the place, then take care of it with soothing plasters until it heals.
[Chapter heading:] On the methods of Ataxmir for eyes, that is, when the eyelid softens so that it weeps as it should not.
Chapter XI.
When hairs grow on the eyelids beyond the natural course of hairs and turn white, then they harm the eye and bring about symptoms such as continuous tears, softening of the eyelid, and opacity, until it leads to the cause of eye destruction.
And Ataxmir indeed cures the eyes according to four methods. Or by cauterization with fire. Or with sharp medicine, as stated in the chapter on cauterization. Ataxmir is treated by incision and suturing. By reeds, as I shall say.
You should place the head of the sick person on your lap. Then, turn the eyelid of the eye with your left hand.
If it is thus turned, it is good. And if not: insert a needle into it where there is a thread from the lower part of the eyelid, and let the needle penetrate through the thread above, and let it be near the hairs themselves, that is, near the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow: and pull the thread towards the top with the eyelid, and turn it with a rod.
Then find in the inner part of the eyelid under the added hairs with a spatula slipping from the greater tear duct to the lesser tear duct.
Then extract the thread, and put a small piece of cotton or cloth under the eyelid: then mark the eyelid with pitch (encaustic), as if it were like the figure of a myrtle leaf.
Nevertheless, the figure must be made according to the size and elevation of the eyelid, since this is varied among humans.
For there are those who require that the amount be cut from the eyelid according to the size that is softened by the eyelid.
Then with the spatula find on top of the lines that you marked, and begin from the greater tear duct to the lesser tear duct, and let there be a split near the natural hairs, as thick as the radius.
Then insert a hook into one of the two corners of the skin. Then scarify it entirely. Then join the two lips with suture using a sharp needle and fine wool thread: and remove blood, and make what exceeds from the threads on the eyebrows adhere, with some things that stick to it, if you wish to do this: and if not, do not treat it.
Then release the suture and threads for three or four days, afterwards take care of it.
And if you wish, release the wound without suture, and take care of it as it dries and contracts. For the eyelid should be lifted during bandaging of the wound and its dressing, but it will be better in the future.
This method of healing was taught by the ancients (Ataxmires).
However, there is concern about the patient in this procedure, but it is a good operation and there is no fear in it.
And another method is also in Ataxmires: it is to mark signs on the eyelid in the shape of a myrtle leaf, as we have told before.
Then lift the eyelid with three separated or united combs according to the following shape, then cut off what is excess with small scissors according to this shape with equal incisions.
If it is not possible for you to hold the comb and it does not fit, then take a needle with thread and insert it in the middle of the figure; insert another thread near the larger tear duct and another thread near the smaller tear duct; and bind threads on your fingers with equal tension.
Then lift your hand with an equal elevation; and lift the skin where the wound is marked, as we have told before.
Then bind together the lips of the wound with suture and take care of it until it heals.
If a boil occurs at your incision or tear, bind it with thread and pitch and similar substances from soothing ointments.
And sometimes the eyelashes of the eyelid may also turn.
Therefore, you must use what we have said in the incision; but suturing on both sides is more artificial. On the treatment of Ataxmir with dogs.
And turn the eyelid over, and cut the fissure that is within, as I have told you. Then make two canines or two thin sticks, whose length is equal to the length of the eyelid and their width less than the width of a spatula; and you have already cut at both ends of each where you hold the sutures.
Then attach each one to the superfluous part of the eyelid of the eye with a spatula and tie two canines from both sides with a tight knot, and let it be for several days. For the contracted skin will die, darken, and rot until it falls off by itself.
If it delays, then cut it with scissors. Then take care of it until it heals.
When it has consolidated, clean the eyelid and do not pluck the hairs.
And this is the form of two canines which you should make according to this figure and size.
Chapter 12.
On the removal of irritating hairs from the eye with a needle.
The operation is to take a thin needle and insert a fine silk thread into it gently. Then tie the ends of it and knot both ends with a very thin knot; and let the length of the threads be one palm (about 5 inches).
Then take another fine thread for Alinxotatis and tie its ends if you wish.
Then place the patient's head in your lap and let it be near the sun so that the operation may be seen; since this is a delicate or fine operation.
Then insert the needle with Alinxotatis into the root of the eyelid and make it penetrate quickly into the eyelid until you pull out the natural hair from above.
Then draw the needle above the aneurysm and insert it into the aneurysm; if there is one, or two, or three, not more than that.
Then draw your hand along with it, until the needle emerges from the aneurysm with its own hair.
If the aneurysm is drawn out and its own hair does not come out with it; draw the aneurysm downwards, with the thread you have inserted into it, until the aneurysm comes out through the upper opening, and you see it with your eye; then draw out the aneurysm and the thread, and pull both out, close the eye, and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair adheres to its place and flesh grows over it.
If the hair is short, then take a long hair from among natural hairs and draw it along with it; or leave it until it grows out, and then draw it out when it has grown sufficiently far.
Chapter XIII.
When this aneurysm happens to the eye, it is called "Leporina.
This aneurysm may be natural or accidental.
Therefore, the accidental aneurysm arises from the consolidation of a wound, a cut, a cauterization, or similar things.
The method of treatment for it is to find the consolidated area and separate the lips of it, and put a linen cloth inside, tie it until it heals.
It is not appropriate to use medicines that dry and constrict when treating it; for if you do so, the aneurysm becomes worse than before; instead, use softening substances such as fenugreek; and embrocation with water in which althea has been boiled, with linseed; and apply daquilon ointment, which has been melted with some oil; and wrap it with linen, and treat it with that.
Thy treasure of care is, that thou strive with all thy skill, so that it not harden, according to the former shape that was first.
This operation indeed, which we have said, is no more than a correction of Alzahrak, so that the form of the place does not return to what it was altogether.
Section on the care of Alzahrak in the lower eyelid, which is a wrinkling or contraction upward towards right and left.
Chapter XIII.
This Alzahrak which occurs below, is indeed what is truly called Alzahrak. And it is natural, and it is accidental.
And the accidental one is made from wound, or split, or cautery, and similar things.
And the method of operation in it is, that you take a pointed instrument, in which there is a double thread, and you stain it in the flesh, and make it penetrate from the left tear duct to the right tear duct, until the thread reaches both extremities of the flesh.
Then stretch the flesh upwards with a point, and cut it with a broad chisel. If therefore the shape of the eyelid returns as it should be, it is good.
And if not, take radium, and place it in the split, and turn the eyelid with it: and cut two splits on the inner side of the eyelid, and let their extremities be at the angles of the incision, until they converge and form an angle: until when they are gathered together, the shape becomes this shape, and is the Greek letter lambda.
Then remove that flesh in quantity, which is its sharp edge below, from what follows the eyelid. Then gather the separated parts: or her with a wool thread.
Then care for those (injuries) with what we have said, regarding softening medicines and linen, until they heal.
And if Alxatrati occurs from a split or suture, or cautery: then it is necessary to find a flat split beneath the eyelashes, as previously described. Then separate between two lips with linen, as we have said.
The summary of the treatment for Alxatrati, whether above or below, is that the operation should be performed on it, as prepared according to the form of Alxatrati.
Indeed, it has many variations in its shape: and the skillful craftsman prepares his mind with any method that is possible for him, until he brings back the figure to a natural form or close to it, and the patient himself, according to what suits him from the operation and instruments in numerous positions.

§ On the adhesion of the eyelid with the conjunctiva or cornea.
Sometimes this consolidation occurs in many people, so that the upper eyelid adheres to the white of the eye and prevents it from performing its natural functions.

Then pour salt water into the eye, rinse it with water: or distill it on him from sifted snow dissolved in water.

On the incision of the nail and the protrusion of flesh from the tear ducts.
Chapter XVI.
Know that the nail is in two ways. Or it is nerve-like and resembles a hard horn, delicate. Or it is not nerve-like, resembling frozen wetness of white, which when struck with iron or attempted to be picked up with a nail, is broken off and the nail does not embed in it.
And neither of these types begin except from the larger tear duct, until it gradually enters, covering the eye, and prevents light, and movement of the eye.
And the method of operation in its incision is that the sick person places his head in your lap. Then open the eyes of him and lift the eyelid with your hand. Then grasp the nail with a few-times folded nails and extend it towards the upper part. Then take a needle and insert it into the nail with a horse's, cow's or sheep's hair, and make sure it is thin; bend the tip of the needle slightly and pierce it through the middle of the nail and tie the nail with thread and extend it towards the upper part; and scrape the side of the nail following the pupil as if you were pulling it with hair up to its end.
Then cut the remainder at the root of the tear duct with a thin spatula or small forceps; and let the natural flesh of the tear duct remain, so that no continuous flow of tears occurs from the incision.
And sometimes the nail is extended with a forceps alone; or with a thread, as we said. Then it is scraped with a soft spatula, whose shape is as follows.
And beware, lest the spatula touch the nail's cornified layer and cause a break there, and the hole is punctured through.
Then after the incision, throw something crushed salt or made of wine vinegar into the eye and let it remain for another day. Then care for it as necessary, until it is healed.
If the nail is not nerve-filled and you cannot insert an awl into it nor does a forceps fit into it, then this kind of nail is repeatedly treated with medications and heals as I narrated in the division.
If you wish to cut it (the nail), then open the eye of the patient and take a delicate, soft, fragile and sharp spatula in the following shape. And grind the nail above with a fine file. If you see that it is becoming rarefied and crushed and a file has been pressed into it, then pour from your hour into the eye vinegar made of wine vinegar or red vinegar or ground salt and close the eye until another day.
Then repeat the procedure until the entire thing is removed. Unless it is a warm abscess in the eye, then leave that alone and care for the abscess until it heals.
Then repeat the procedure with a file until it heals.
The protrusion of the eyelid flesh (chalazion), if it causes great harm in the eye, is suspended with a forceps and cut from it; not too close to the incision so as not to disrupt the flow of tears.
Then apply milk or red colocynth (or one made from zinc), until it heals.
On eye-lid incision and flesh born therein.
Chapter Seventeen.
There arises sometimes in the eyes of men a red flesh, either composed or laid over, until it covers the pupil or approaches or presses upon the eyelids and perhaps turns the eyelids outward; and it resembles the rose of Balaustium.
And the treatment for this is also that the weak one should put his head in your bosom. Then open his eyes and collect the entire flesh with suitable forceps; and hold it with a single forcep or tongs.
Then cut the flesh first, until you finish it all with the knife. And be careful not to hurt the eye during the operation; and let your cut, when you make it, be as we described in the incision of the nail, or with small forceps, such as those used for cauterizing the asebel (a type of wart), according to its shape after this chapter.
When your cut is completed and all the alguardenic (the red flesh) is removed, then fill the eye with brine; or sprinkle in it red powder and similar substances from corrosive medicines; and place over the outer eye a piece of warm cotton with white egg: to protect it from hot inflammation.
If some of the alguardenic remains and you are dominated by hot blood, and fear a hot inflammation; then let go of the eye and take care of it with what soothes the inflammation.
Then repeat the operation over him until it heals.
And do the same with any additional flesh that may occur in the eye of this type.
It is necessary that every weak eye of an alien, whether from a natural or accidental cause, be treated with iron in surgery: and you shall not insert your hand into any of these operations until you see that this member is able to bear such operation.
Chapter on the collection of Sebel (Seba) from the eye.

Chapter XVIII.
It is necessary for you first, that you consider whether the eye in which is Sebel, is strong and there is no sickness in it except Sebel; then collect Sebel from it.

Then collect the veins with subtle forceps and remove the blood by the hour after the hour until you see the veins removed from the eye and resolved; and beware lest you harm the eye with the tips of the forceps.

Chapter: On reducing Arissat to the nose.
Chapter XIX.
The surgeon is named Arisato. He cures a fistula with a cautery or with sharp medicine burning, according to the account that preceded it.
If it is not cured (the fistula), then there is no skill in it: except to lance over the abscess at its birth, and extract all moisture that is in it and pus, until the bone is exposed.
When the bone is exposed, and you see in it corruption or blackness, then scrape it with the instrument, which has this shape.
And it is called the rasp of the skull.
Make it from iron india, and its head should be round like a razor, which is pierced with a file, or pierced with the fine point of aliskilfer: and place it on the corrupted part of the bone.
Then turn it with your fingers, and press your hand slightly, until you know that the corruption is already scraped away: do this several times.
Then restore the place with dry medicines made of styptics.
If the place consolidates and flesh grows in it, and the course of pus stops: and remains forty days, and does not renew, and does not abscess, and no accident occurs in it: then you will know that it is already healed.
And if not, then there is no skill in it, except to lead the fistula back to the nostril, according to this shape.
And it is to scrape the bone in the second joint with iron, or with sharp medicine: and when the bone is exposed, then take a drill according to this shape, the tip of which is iron, triangular: and the wood of it should be a pyramid extended to the tip, as you see.
Then place it on the bone itself: and let it be near the tear duct: and extend your hand slightly away from the eye. Then turn your hand with the lancet until it penetrates the bone and feels weak. By this you will know that air is coming out of it, when you hold your hand over his nose.
Then restore the place with medicines drying, as I have taught you.
When the flesh is born and the place hardens; then the matter that flowed outward, returns to the nose; it is therefore lighter above the sick man.
Chapter on the Reduction of Eyelid Protrusion.
Chapter XX.
When the eye bulges completely and no harm or reduction occurs in vision: then it is necessary to release the patient; afterwards, apply leeches to him; subsequently, place blisters on the neck without incision, but with suction.

And the method of fleas is as follows: you should take soft cloths in large quantities and fold each cloth four times; make many from them; then place one on top of another according to how much the eye needs; then tighten them with a strong bandage.
And repeat the application of blisters with suction without incision.
Then remove the blisters and allow the eyelid to remain closed during day and night.
If the bandage becomes soft again, then it is necessary to tighten it a lot; afterwards, remove the bandage after day and night as previously mentioned.
If you see the eye returning to its normal appearance, that is good; otherwise, repeat the plaster, fleas, tightening and blisters until it heals.
[Paragraph on] Incision of the conjunctiva.

Chapter on the treatment of Alcomnat.
Chapter XXII.
This ailment called Alcomnat is nothing but pus that accumulates in the eye, similar to water descending from it, and it is not the same.
And the method of treatment for this is that you make the patient sit on a prepared chair or straight chair.
Then take hold of his head with both hands from the sides and move him until you see pus come out towards the lower parts of your eyes. Then it is shaped and does not descend, and the vision is cleared; let the patient see as he did before; and if it does not descend towards the lower part, know that it is water.
If, however, no preparation for the descent of pus is made as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands. Then take a fine probangue and puncture it with it slightly on the horny pad near the junction of the conjunctiva with the corneal membrane at the corona, until the pus comes out.
When it comes out, then pour warm water into the eye in which you have mixed honey; or water boiled with burned hay and honey; then cleanse with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
On the care of the water that descends into the eye, or cataract.
Chapter XXIII.
We have already said the kind of water suitable for division and expulsion, then take it accordingly in health.
