Chapter XXIII.
Chapter on the treatment of a newborn's flesh in the nose.
Whenever diverse fleshes are born in the nose, some of which resemble the many feet of a scorpion: and from it is cancerous flesh, stony, dark colored: and from it is the gentle flesh, not dark colored.
Therefore, for that gentle flesh which is among those fleshes, not fraudulent, nor cancerous, you must make the sick person sit with his face opposite the sun and open his nostrils; then thrust a hook into those fleshes; afterwards drag them towards the outside and cut what you have grasped from it with a thin, sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all the flesh has been removed.
If something remains of it from whose removal is not possible: then shave that with a small instrument easily, until nothing remains from it. If however blood dominates over you or a hot boil occurs: then apply to it as required; or if it is from malicious boils, then quickly proceed with cauterizing it until the blood separates and all the flesh is removed.
Then pour vinegar, water, or wine into the nose after cutting. If however the nose opens and moisture goes up to the palate, then you know that he is already well.
If however the moisture does not penetrate as required, then you know that there is flesh born within the upper bones of the nose, to which the instrument did not reach with cutting.
Then you must insert a thread of linen with some thickness and many knots; and place between every knot an amount equal to the length of a finger or less; and let the sick person thrust one end of the thread into his nose with a rod, or with whatever he can manage after making it similar to a syringe: and pull out the smelly stuff until it reaches the cavity, and goes out above the throat.
And indeed many times do boys in schools perform this, and it is an easy matter for him who desires.
Then place two ends of the cord, one that exits through the nose, and the other that remains inside the nose. Then, with a pair of scissors or a knife, cut the flesh along with the knots that are on the cord. Do this until you know that the flesh is now separated from the knots of the cord.
Then remove the cord; place linen moistened with Egyptian ointment in the nose after bleeding has stopped. Do this for three days or more until the ointment has completely corroded all that remains of the flesh.
Then place a lead tube at the end in the nose for some days until it heals.
If, however, it requires a dry cure, use this method.
For the purge to be made with oil and other medications into the nose, make it of silver or copper; it should resemble a small lamp, open like a snail shell, and its passage should also be similar.
And if you wish to make a closed tube, as in a tube.
And the snail shell instrument for the purge should be filled and perforated; it should have a handle at its end with which to hold it while heating oil or whatever you wish from infusions and fluid substances within it.
Chapter 25.
A deviated nose, known as a Thelul, often arises at the end of the nose and grows larger with days until it becomes an ugly sight.
Therefore, when it first appears, cut it off completely at its base. Then place on the spot, either cautery, or a medicine burning at its place.
If the incision does not widen, then consider if it is hard and black, with few senses; then do not touch it with iron because it is cancerous ulcer.
For I have often seen one who made an incision in a tumor and great evil happened to him who had it.
And if the tumor is soft and not black, and you see that it is possible to make an incision in its entirety, then evacuate the weakened part and incise it without fear or timidity; and care for the place with it as it exudes and constricts, until it heals.
Chapter 26.
Chapter on stitching the nose, lip, and ear.
Know that when there is a loosening of continuity in one of these cartilages, the operation does not help much unless in some people.
Therefore when something happens to anyone of these, you should examine if it is a recent wound with its blood; and then gather two pieces of the wound together with stitches; then care for it until it heals.
And if there is a loosening of continuity in the lips and they are already separated, and each part has become healthy; then it is necessary to remove all parts appearing from the skin until it bleeds. Then gather two lips with stitches, tie them and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood and pulverized aloes over the bleeding; then place a piece of ointment plaster called diafinicon on top of the powders, and another piece of any consolidating plasters; and leave it bound for two or three days. Then loosen it, change the medicine; and leave it until the threads fall off by themselves. Then care for it with an ointment until it heals.
The method of suturing is to gather the solution of continuity or with needles, as we have explained in the suturing of the abdomen; or gather the solution with thread, as I have shown you.
Chapter 27.
Chapter on the extraction of lip nodes.
Many men happen to have hard lesions on the inside of their lips, similar to grains of grass; some of them are smaller and others larger.
Therefore, it is necessary to turn the lip, find on top of every node of it, and hang it with a hook, and cut it from all sides.
Then fill the place after the cut with wax, until the blood is separated.
Then it is rubbed with vinegar and the place where there is an inflammation is treated with it until the wounds heal.
Chapter 28.
Chapter on cutting the flesh of a child over the gum.
Often, flesh grows on the gum which is called 'abulus' by the ancients.
Therefore, it is necessary to hang it with a hook or hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, and let the pus run out or the blood.
Then place wax on the spot or other healing powders over it.
If that flesh comes back after treatment, which often happens, then cut it a second time and cauterize it; for it does not come back after cauterization.
Chapter 29.
Chapter on grinding teeth with iron.
Whenever abscesses form on the surface of teeth from both the inside and outside parts, and between the gums and hard enamel, they sometimes turn black, become citrine-colored, or green, until corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul due to this.
Therefore, you must make the sick person sit between your hands, and his head in your bosom, and shave the tumor and tooth, where the cortex appears to you, and something similar to sand remains until there is nothing left; and similarly do with blackness, and greenness, and yellowish, and others until they are cleaned.
If what is in them is removed from the beginning by reason, that is good; but if not, then repeat the razing upon them on another day, the second, and the third, until at last the study comes to an end in that which you desire.
And know that the tooth requires razors of various shapes and forms, according to which it is prepared for your operation; because the razor with which the tooth is shaved from the lower part is different from the razor with which the tooth is shaved between the teeth, according to other shapes.
And these shapes of the razors should be prepared by you, which you see.
Chapter 30.
Chapter on the extraction of tooth pain.
It is necessary that you treat the tooth from its pain with all diligence and to delay in extracting it. For it is not possible to replace it when it is extracted; because its substance is lofty; until there is no excuse for extracting it, then if the sick person must be compelled to extract it himself, it should be strengthened and certified by you that the tooth in pain.
For often the sick person is deceived by pain and thinks that it is in the tooth and extracts it himself; then the pain does not subside until the diseased tooth is extracted.
We have already seen this from the operation of phlebotomists.
When the sick person is certified by you that the tooth in pain is himself, then it is necessary that you scarify around the tooth with a spatula, in which there is something of virtue, until the gums are loosened from all sides; then move it with your fingers, or with delicate tweezers in the first place gradually, until you shake it.
Then place the large forceps in those places well, and hold the head of the weak between your knees so that it remains still; then pull the tooth straight out, so as not to break it.
If it does not come out, then take one of those instruments and insert it under it from every side with ease, and try to move it as you did at first.
If the tooth is perforated or corroded, then it is necessary to fill the hole with a cloth and tighten it with the tip of a thin radius so as not to break it during your extraction with forceps.
It is necessary that you perform careful scarification around the gums on all sides in many places.
And be mindful of your strength so as not to break it and a part of it remains and returns over the weak one from that greater evil which is its original pain.
And beware that you do not make the same mistake as those who are ignorant in their haste and audacity during extraction, and instead administer what I have said.
For many times they make great illnesses come upon men, which are difficult to break and all of whose roots remain or some of them; or extract it with some jaw bones, as we have often testified to this.
Then after extraction, it is washed with wine, or with vinegar and salt.
If bleeding occurs from the places (for it often happens), then grind some wax and fill the place with it; if not, cauterize it if you do not have wax.
The handles of the fine forceps with which the tooth is moved should be long at the end and short at the grip, thick so as not to split when it is pressed against the tooth; they should be like the grips of large forceps, until when you tighten them, they do not bite themselves, nor split; the ends should be short and made of iron or well-made file, straight at the ends; and in their ends there should be teeth, some of which enter into others and tighten with a decent constriction, strong.
And sometimes [there are] extremities like the shape of a bird's beak, which is called ciconia, and [they are] strong constrictions.
Chapter XXXI.
On the extraction of teeth, and the removal of fractured jaw bones.
When something remains at the site of tooth extraction that breaks, then it is necessary to place warm butter on the spot for one or two days until the location softens; afterwards, introduce algasti, or forceps, whose tips are similar to the beak of a bird called ciconia. This is the shape of the forceps.
The tips of them are made like a file inside out; or like an aliskilfegi.
If it does not come out of you with these forceps, then it is necessary to carve a cavity over the root and peel off all the flesh, and introduce an instrument called Palanca parva, whose shape is as follows.
Let the tip be short and slightly thicker; and not soaked, lest it breaks.
If the root comes out through this, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to help with other instruments whose shapes are as follows.
The shape of the first one is a triangle with a certain thickness.
The shape of the thin triangle tip.
And with other instruments and tools which have been mentioned for tooth extraction.
Also helpful is this instrument resembling a large nail with a twisted triangle tip and some thickness, so as not to break; and it should not be soaked.
And know that there are many tools for teeth; and likewise, the rest of the instruments are not mentioned; but a prudent and skillful craftsman finds for himself the tool according to the operation and diseases indicated by them.
Because there are diseases for which no ancient instrument was found, due to the diversity of their species.
If however a bone from the jaw, or any bone of the face, breaks or putrefies: then examine over it in its place with what suits it from the instruments and forceps which I mentioned for extraction of roots, and assist with the device whose shape is this.
Let something of thickness gradually be placed within it to tighten or hold the bone, so that it does not flee and move away, until the bone is expelled; then restore the place with appropriate medications for it.
If there is a small decay in the bone, then scrape it away from its decay, and care for it until it heals.
Chapter XXXII.
On the suture of prominent teeth over others.
When teeth protrude not according to their natural course, it becomes ugly due to that shape; and especially when this happens in women, and girls, namely in the soft ones.
Therefore, you should examine. For if a tooth is born after another tooth and it does not settle, or its suture, nor cutting of it is possible; then extract it: and if it is attached with another tooth, then cut it with this tool, whose shape is this.
It resembles a small beak, and it is made of iron with a very sharp tip.
And let your cut be such that you make the cut over many days, and because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that another tooth is not disturbed.
If it protrudes for suture cutting: then cut it with a file made of iron, whose shape is this.
Let it be entirely of iron, and its handle small with many sharp points, like a file used to make a needle; with which you should gently file the tooth little by little over many days, so that another tooth is not disturbed and it falls out; then smooth it, in the end scrape it with some rasps.
If it is a tooth, from which a piece breaks off and injures the tongue, then it is necessary that the edge be smoothed out until its roughness is removed, and it becomes level; and it should be flattened so as not to injure the tongue nor corrupt speech.
Chapter XXXIII.
On the extraction of teeth with gold threads.
When there occurs a shock or jolt to the front teeth from being struck or by accident, and the weak person cannot hold what he eats to prevent it from falling out; and you have treated them with medicinal poultices, but the treatment has not been effective: then it is appropriate that they be fastened with a gold thread, since silver becomes green and putsrefies after days, but gold never changes.
And let the thread be of a medium thickness between fineness and coarseness according to its quantity that it may hold between the teeth.
The shape of the extraction is such that you take the thread and insert it double between two healthy teeth; then you wind it with its two ends between the moved teeth, whether one or several, until you reach the sutures up to the healthy tooth on the other side. Then wind it again up to the part from which you began; and hold your hand with finesse and wisdom until it is not removed entirely; and let your pressure when you tighten the thread be at the roots of the teeth so that it does not come out.
Then cut off the excessive ends of the thread with scissors; and collect both, and twist them together; and conceal these beneath the healthy tooth and the moved tooth so as not to injure the tongue; then let it be tightened until it remains in that state.
If it loosens or breaks, fasten it with another thread, and it will remain in that state for a long time.
And this is the form of teeth, and the figure of grinding of two healthy teeth, and two moving teeth, as you see.
And sometimes it happens that one tooth or two return to their places after the loss of each (tooth), and remain as we have said; and this does not occur unless the skilled and experienced craftsman makes it happen.
And sometimes a tooth is shaped from the bones of a cow; and it is made like the form of a tooth, and placed in its position, so that it is strengthened and held firm as we have said; and it remains and serves for a long time.
Chapter XXXIIII.
When this ligament that happens under the tongue is natural, because it is born with man, or accidental, from a wound that has already consolidated.
And the operation in it is to open the weak bone in its head in your pouch and lift up its tongue; then cut that nerve-ligament through its width until it is disconnected from its restraint.
If there is something hard and knotted in it, and it is from the consolidation of a wound: then thrust an awl into it, and bore through its width until you cut the ligament, and the knot is released.
And beware, lest there be a cleft in deep flesh, and you cut an artery there, and bleeding occurs.
Then it is to be lapped up with water of rose, or with vinegar, or cold water.
Then place under the tongue a piece of linen cloth which the sick man holds all night so that it does not consolidate again.
If there is bleeding, then place over the place a piece of mustard seed powder. If blood conquers you, then cauterize the place with a lentiginous cautery which is suitable for it; then take care of it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter XXXV.
Occasionally there occurs under the tongue a boil resembling a small frog, which prevents the tongue from performing its natural function and perhaps it swells so much that it fills the bone.
And the operation in it is to open the weak bone before the sun: and observe the boil.
If therefore you see it of a black or dark color, hard, in which no unhealthy sensation is found: then do not touch it, because it is cancer.
If it is hollowed out towards whiteness, in which there is moisture, then throw in a hook and cut it with a fine chisel and free it from all sides. And if your blood is constrained by it during your operation hour, then place a gauze soaked in vinegar upon it until the blood is removed; thereafter return to your operation until you extract it with its appendage.
Thereafter it is washed with vinegar and salt; care for it with the appropriate treatment until it is healed.
Chapter on the treatment of two cysts (abscesses).
Chapter XXXVI.
Whenever cysts (abscesses) resembling boils occur in the throat, that is, swellings that occur outside; and they are called the two Amigdalae: which, when you treat with what we have said in the division, and they do not heal, then consider.
If therefore it is a hard abscess, of dark color, with few senses: then do not touch it with iron.
And if it is red in color and the root of it is thick: then do not touch it even with iron, fearing bleeding, but rather let it be until it matures. And thereafter either perforate it or it will burst by itself.
If it is white in color, round and the root of it is subtle: then it must be cut.
And the operation on it is to consider before its operation whether the abscess has become quiet and warm with complete rest, or whether it decreases somewhat: then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head be in your lap; and open his mouth and receive a servant between his hands, and press his tongue downward with an instrument of this shape.
Make it from silver, or brass, that it may be as subtle as a knife.
When you press it with your tongue and the boil is shown to you, and falls before your eyes: then take a hook, and pierce it in the middle, and pull it out as far as possible, besides pulling some of the skin along with it.
Then cut it with an instrument, whose form is as follows. It resembles forceps; but its ends should be curved, so that the opening of each is in the direction of the other's point; take care therefore that it is made of steel or brass impregnated with aluminum.
If this instrument is not present, then cut it with a spatula, whose form is as follows. Be sharp at one end, not sharp at the other end.
And after you cut one acorn (boil), cut the other according to this same form of cutting.
Then, after the cutting, let the sick person gargle with cold water, or with vinegar and water.
If there should be a flow of blood, let him gargle with water in which the rinds of pomegranates have been boiled; or the leaves of myrtle, and similar ones from other herbs, until the flow of blood is removed: then take care of him, until he is cured.
And sometimes boils other than acorns (boils) arise in the throat. Therefore, cut them according to what I said about the cutting of two acorns equally.
I myself have healed a woman from a boil that was born in her throat, which was dragging towards the flesh, and only a few senses remained, which had almost closed her throat: and the woman breathed through a narrow mouth, and she had already prohibited her from eating, and drinking water: and by now it had come close to death, if it had lasted one day, or two days.
The wound or sore had risen to such an extent that it expelled two branches, until they emerged through the two nostrils.
I therefore hastened and fastened a hook onto one of them. Then I pulled it out, and a large piece came away with it.
Afterwards, I cut off the remaining part where it was seized in the nostril.
Then I did to the other what had come out from the second nostril.
Then I opened his mouth and pressed his tongue; then I fastened a hook onto the sore; afterwards I cut off a part of it, and nothing more came out except a little blood; so the woman's throat was healed, and she began to drink water immediately, and afterward took food.
I did not cease to cut from that sore repeatedly for a long time; and the sore would follow wherever I was cutting, until it became too prolonged, and with it that.
I then heated an iron and cauterized the sore in the woman's throat.
She then remained well; afterwards I went away, and I did not know what God had done with her after me.
[Section heading: On the incision of a sore in the throat.]
Chapter XXXVII.
When a catarrh descends to the throat and a sore forms, which is large; it is then called perpendicular; and if it is round and thick in the lower part, it is then called a goitre (gland).
When it is treated with what I have said in the previous division, and there is no improvement; and you see that the sore is warm and soft; then it should be cut.
And if what is gathered around it is round and not long, and is red or blackish or dark in color, and there is no feeling; then it should be cut. There is fear concerning the sick one.
Therefore, when you see it as I have said from its whiteness and its length, so that you make the sick one sit before the sun; and press his tongue with the instrument of which the story has gone before: then fasten a hook in his wound, and pull it downwards: and cut it with one of two instruments which I said for incising two amygdala.
And it is necessary that you do not cut from it, unless what is added exceeds the natural limit without addition.
For if you cut from it more, you harm the voice and speech.
Then after the cutting, use what we have said for the incision of two amygdala; and take care of it until it heals.
If the sick one fears cutting: then it is necessary that you use cunning for his cauterization without fear and dread.
And the method of cauterizing it is not unless with sharp water: and it is, that you place the head of the sick one on your breast. Then press his tongue with the instrument which I said. Then take from the water which I said to you in the chapter of cauterizing, and fashion a ladle with it not extinguished, and place it neither thick nor thin, and fill with it the depression of this instrument, whose shape is as follows:
The cavity where medicine is placed should be concave, like the cavity of a cochlea's radius.
Place the instrument along with the medicine upon the ulcer itself: and let the sick man lie on his side, so that the salve may run from his mouth due to the internal medicine, so that nothing may fall from it into his throat, and thus harm him.
Then hold your hand with the medicine. And you apply it to the ulcer by handfuls for half an hour until you see it become darkened and the bite of the medicine subside.
And if you wish to apply a poultice, you wrap it around the extremity of the radius and pour the poultice with medicine, then insert the radius with the poultice into the cannula until the poultice sticks to the ulcer.
Do this repeatedly, until you achieve what you wish from the cauterization of the vein. Then let it go: for it burns and falls away within three or four days.
If you need to repeat the medicine, repeat it; and after cauterization, clean the area around the vein with a poultice soaked in butter and make it clean with that which is around it from the medicine; and wipe it with cold water.
Externally it is to be treated with embrocation, and internally with gargarisms, until it heals.
Therefore, this method of treatment is healthier than incision and less fearful.
And sometimes an ulcer is also treated with something more subtle than cautery and incision: it is treated with suffumigation, according to this method. Take camphor, hyssop, origanum, rutus, asafoetida, chamomile, abrotanum and similar herbs: and grind them all together or some of them in a pot, and immerse them with vinegar, and boil: the pot should be well coated with lime: and there should be a hole in the middle of the pot, over which a concave instrument is placed according to this method.
Make it from silver or copper, and introduce the tip, where the grain is, into the sick man's bone, until the vapor reaches the wound through the cannula, until the ulcer becomes much darkened.
Then repeat over it many times, until it burns.
And beware not to perform this treatment at the beginning of an abscess's onset. Generally, add in abscess: and it is not proper to do this unless at the cooling down of that abscess's heat.
If this tool is not present to you, then take a reed, and prepare the rind of an egg on its tip so that the bone does not burn because the eggshell rind prevents the heat from burning the bone; and this is good treatment with benefit.
Chapter on the extraction of thorns, and bones from the throat.
Chapter XXXVIII.
Often a bone or a fish spine adheres to the throat.
Therefore, you should remove what appears from among them that lies beneath the vision, after pressing the tongue with an instrument in the sun, and it is revealed to you that it is in the throat.
And what is not apparent to you and hidden in the throat, it is necessary that you make a weakened man vomit before the food is digested in the stomach. Perhaps the thing attached will come out through vomiting.
Or the weakened man swallows a piece of nutmeg or radish root or a dry bread crumb, or takes a piece of dried sea sponge, softens it and ties it to a thread; then he swallows that. When it reaches the place where the thorns or bones are and they are being removed, then it comes out.
If it does not come out with what has been said, then use a lead tool in this shape.
The object should be thicker than the radius slightly, and at its end there should be an opening, which can easily pass through the throat; and it should have its head raised upwards.
And let him be careful of touching his epiglottis to avoid a cough and push with it a bone or a splinter, or introduce it himself with his hand (the instrument).
But if the patient introduces it (the object), this is better, because of his knowledge about the place where it is attached; and he should push downward or pull his hand with the instrument upward, all that according to its quantity which is prepared for him until it comes out.
Chapter on Extraction of Leeches.
Chapter 39.
When a leech is treated with what I said about its division in the cure with medicines and it does not work, then consider in the throat of the sick person before the sun or after pressing his tongue with the instrument that I told you.
If your vision falls upon a leech, extract it with a small hook or with fine forceps.
If this is not possible with them (the fine forceps), then take a concave tube, insert it into the throat of the sick person as far as the throat; then insert into the concavity of the tube hot iron with fire. Repeat this often: and let the sick person abstain from water for the whole day.
Then let him take cold water rinse and open his mouth in it; and wash his throat with it and do not swallow anything from it; move the water one hour after another with his hand. For a leech, as soon as it feels water, it falls out.
If it does not come out with what we mentioned, then fumigate the sick person with bedbugs or with camphor with the instrument that I told you about for the fumigation of the windpipe.
Repeat it frequently, because it will fall by itself.
The method of suffumigation is to take the pot containing live prunes with fire; and let the pot be covered with a cover, having a hole in its middle; and arrange the end of the instrument in that hole.
Then cast the suffumigation and let the patient put his mouth at the end of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the suffumigation does not escape before you know that the suffumigation has reached the bloodsucker. For the bloodsucker will fall immediately.
If it does not fall, then repeat the suffumigation frequently.
Let the patient endure thirst, eat salt and other things, but drink no water.
Therefore it is necessary for him to come out with this regimen.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the bloodsucker is extracted from the throat when it falls upon it.
It resembles forceps, as you see; except that it has this curvature which penetrates into the throat. And its end is similar to the beak of a bird called ciconia, which has the roughness of a file; when it grasps something, it does not release it completely.
[Chapter: On opening abscesses, and their cutting, and treatment in general.]
Chapter XL (40).
The species of abscesses are many, according to the memory of them, that is one and one in this book; and they are various in their perforation, and cutting of themselves from two modes.
One of them is of the species of an abscess on itself, and because it encompasses moistures.
And the second method is due to places, where it happens from the body.
Because an abscess happening on the head is one thing, and an abscess happening in the anus is another: and an abscess happening in a fleshy place is another from an abscess happening in joints: and each of them has its own judgement according to operation.
And from abscesses there are some that it is not necessary to perforate, unless after the maturation of pus in them and its completion: and there are those that it is necessary to perforate, while they are raw and do not mature according to their completion.
Like abscesses which are near joints.
Because when an abscess happens near a joint, and extends to be its length, until it putrefies that which is around it perhaps corrupts ligaments or the nerves of that joint's union; therefore it is a cause closer to the contraction of that limb.
Or is an abscess near the main part of the body; because if you delay the perforation of it until it matures, it will harm either him or through that main part of the body.
Or it is near the anus, perforate it while it is immature: and it is not necessary to perforate a raw abscess, not completed digestion, unless it is near the anus, so that it does not rot deeply and spread to the inside of the anus, and become a fistula, or become at its end that does not heal.
It is necessary that you know the hour of perforation of the abscess, when it has matured according to its completion: and it is in sedation of pain, recovery of fever, and diminution of redness, and pulse, and acuteness of headache of the abscess; and other signs.
It is necessary that you make the same perforation in the lower part of the abscess, and of more prominent protrusion: and let the perforation extend along the body's length, if the abscesses are in the parts of the hands and feet, and places of arms, shoulders, tendons, nerves, arteries, and finally in all equal places where there is no reflection.
In those which reflect, proceed with the perforation according to that limb.
When the abscess is in fleshy places: then it is better to leave the perforation of it until its digestion is confirmed, as we said according to our completion.
Since if you perforate it beforehand, the course of the pus is extended from it, and there are many filths and dirtiness, and perhaps its opening hardens and deepens.
And some abscesses should be perforated according to the width of the body due to necessity, or according to that limb which it needs.
And it is necessary to make a small perforation for small abscesses and a large one for large ones: or many sections according to the size of the abscess.
And there are abscesses in which the skin should be concaved: and it should be cut when it has become like a cloth, and made into an end, which is already dead; just as what happens with many of them, that they bubble, and with buboes.
And there are those which should be cut by a section having three angles. And there is one of them, from which it is cut as the shape of the leaf of the myrtle tree.
Like an inguinal abscess.
And there are those in which a round incision or crescent-shaped incision is administered, and similar ones by sections.
What has no head, such as are the soft ulcers, should be pierced through with a shallow puncture, or only superficially.
It is necessary that when an abscess is large and has collected much pus, you pierce it so that it does not spread and you extract all the pus at once; rather, extract a part of it from it. Then the abscess should be opened until another day. Then, extract something from the pus again.
Do this frequently according to the degree, until it comes out; especially if the patient is weak in strength, or a woman pregnant, or a small child, or an old man decrepitus: for the animal spirit often dissipates with the exit of pus; and perhaps the weak one will die, and you will not receive payment.
Therefore beware of this chapter with great caution.
After your puncture, by which you pierce the abscesses, it is necessary that you clean the wound; and reflect. If then the wound of the abscess is small, or the incision is plain, then apply linen cloths, or an old bandage. If the abscess is large and there are many cracks from the puncture, then you must insert linen into every crack until they meet each other.
If in the abscess you have cut off a part of the skin, or hollowed out its circumference; then it is necessary that you fill it with an old bandage, or as when fabric is woven or flax is combed without wetness; and bind it for three days.
Then cast it out, and care for it with whatever is necessary from the salve until it heals.
If blood flow occurs during your procedure, then apply cold water and vinegar, after which a cloth is soaked in them; and place it over the site of the blood flow many times.
If the bleeding persists, then it is necessary to administer a regimen, treatment, and powders which I have mentioned in many places of this our book, and from division.
If it is winter time and the place of the boil contains many nerves: then it is necessary to pour hot poultices with wine and oil onto those areas.
And if it is summer, and the areas are fleshy: then it is necessary to place cold poultices that have been soaked in water, oil, or wine and oil, and let it all be cold. Until the third day, as we have said, then it is necessary to dissolve the boil, remove it, and administer treatment for its healing until it heals.
Therefore, this is what is essential for the universal knowledge of treating boils.
According to the way of distinguishing, I have already said about every boil, how the pathway for its healing is discussed individually in chapters.
Chapter 41.
Chapter on cutting boils that occur on the head skin.
Small boils that occur on the head skin are of the types of knots contained by layers like small bags; as if they were inflated with chicken pus.
And their types are many.
They are fat ones: and there are those that contain a moisture similar to mud: and those that contain a moisture similar to soap and poultices: and others like them, and there are hard stone-like ones.
And in the cutting of all of them, and their removal, there is no fear, as long as it does not make an opposition to the artery during its cutting.
And the operation in their cutting is to try it out with a tool whose shape comes after this, which is called the Probe, until you know what it contains.
If it contains moisture, then dry it by making a cut along its length with a surface incision: in this manner.
Begin with an incision along line b to line g. When the moisture is evacuated, then remove the scab that contains that moisture, and do not leave anything beneath it.
For often it returns if anything remains from it.
Then immerse the wound in Egyptian ointment if it is present; and if not, in water and salt. Fill the wound with it and leave it until another day. For what remains of the scab will corrode itself.
Then repeat over the wound with the second Egyptian ointment, and the third, and as often as necessary until you are confident that nothing remains from the scab. At this point care for the wound with ointment until it is healed.
If an abscess contains a thick knot: then cut it open in this manner, making an incision with the shape of a cross; and place probes between the divisions of the incision, and scrape off all the scab from every side; and try your strength in extracting the membrane that contains it.
But if it opposes an artery, then do what I will tell you afterwards.
And similarly for an abscess that is a stone, cut it open and treat it the same way as we said for the others.
Cutting into an abscess that is a stone is easier since there is little blood and moisture. Sometimes these types of abscesses are found in the head in some humans, where there is no moisture deep within them.
This is because I made an incision over an abscess in the head of a very old woman, and found the abscess to be as hard as a solid stone, rough, white, that could not be broken; and if someone struck it with a probe, they would injure themselves.
In other kinds of boils occurring in the head, except for those boils that occur on children's heads and at the roots of ears, section of all of them should be a superficial incision.
Always perform perforation from the lower part of them to ease the flow of pus towards the lower parts.
Then, take care of it with whatever is appropriate for its cure.

Chapter XLIII.
Section of the epiglottis due to an ulcer within the throat.
The ancients said this section of the epiglottis and I have not seen anyone in our land who has done it; this is their writing.
In those with synanchysis (swallowing difficulties), it is necessary to avoid the section of the epiglottis, since it does not provide any benefit; because all veins and lungs are weak.
In those who have a hot ulcer in the mouth, throat, or both salivary glands, when there is no illness in the channel (canal), it is necessary to use the section of the epiglottis to avoid destruction caused by swelling.
Therefore, when we wish to section the epiglottis, it should be done under three or four circles of the epiglottis, with a small section along its width, in that which is between two circles by quantity; this location is suitable for sectioning, since it lacks muscle and blood vessels are distant from it.
If the surgeon is afraid, then it is necessary that he spreads the skin of the throat with a hook. Then make an incision in the skin until you reach the channel; avoid blood vessels if you see any of them.
Then section the sifac as we have said; it is indicated by the mucus that comes out of the channel along with what breaks and the separation of the voice.
Let the open wound heal at some time.
When the fear of inflammation arises, bring together two pieces of wound skin, and if possible only the skin without cartilage.
Then administer medications that make flesh grow, until it heals.
Says Albucasis. Thus ends the discourse we have narrated, its explanation is only when they see that one of these abscesses has already opened up the throat of the sick person: and he is raised up above death, and desires to be cut; they go to cut the Epiglottis, so that the sick person may breathe over the wound site with a certain breathing, and save himself from death: and for this reason they commanded to let the open wound heal, until the malice of the disease is consumed, and the malice is three days long, as if it were itself: then they commanded to sew up the wound, and care for it until it heals.
And that which I saw myself was that a maidservant received a knife and sent it into her throat, and she cut a part of the windpipe with it.
And I was summoned to treat her, and found her groaning, as is the groan of the dead.
I then tore open the wound and found that blood had come out from the wound, though not much. Thus I was reassured that she had not severed the vein or artery; and air was coming out of the wound.
Therefore I approached and sewed up her wound, and treated it until she was well: and nothing happened to the maidservant except a hoarseness of voice; and she returned after a few days to a better state of health.
Thus I say: that there is no fear in cutting the Epiglottis.

Chapter XLV.
Chapter on the section above the knots.
There are many kinds of knots, and I have already said all their species in division; and it is necessary that here the difference between a knot and an abscess be explained, since there is a doubt about it.
Therefore I say that when an abscess is hot and feverish, and intense pains, until the ebullition of superfluity is suppressed and putrefaction is completed; then indeed fever and heat cease.
But a knot is not hotness nor fever, nor pains; and it contains them in a kist or sac, which is their own proper bag, and it is according to the color of the body; and its origin is as a chickpea, and it is made like a grape, and greater or lesser.
And they are according to two species: either fatty: or containing moisture. The colors of moisture are many, as I have said in the division.
Therefore, when you arrive at the treatment of a knot, you must try it and inquire about it first with the instrument that is called Intromissum, according to its form as it will come in the chapter that follows this.
The method of examination for boils and all knots is to receive this instrument and insert it into the moist place that you find in the boil: and you rotate your fingers with it slowly until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the skin. Then lay your hand upon it according to the measure of the size of the boil.
Then extract the Intromissum, and observe what comes out following its trail.
If moisture flows out running, regardless of its color: then cut it off with a superficial incision, as I have said regarding the other boils.
And if no moisture flows out following the trail of the Intromissum: then you know that it is fatty: cut off over it with an incision in the shape of a cross, according to this form, as I have taught you: and hang it up with tongs, and strip off the skin from all sides easily: and guard the kistin if possible above it, so that you extract the healthy one along with the knot.
If the kistin bursts during the operation and it is not possible to extract the healthy one: then extract it in pieces until nothing remains of it.
For if something remains little or much from it, the knot returns most of all.
If it overwhelms you and something remains little: then fill the wound at the completion, with certain corrosive powders: and tie the wound, and place on top of it what sits the boil, warm: and care for it along with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
If therefore it is a large knot, then its two lips, and care for it with that which adheres to it because it has become flesh.
If it is a pulsating vein that is opposite you or if it is not pulsating: then be careful, and fill the place with boiled wine and leave it tightly bound for two or three days until the wound rots and the boiling of blood subsides; then return to cut what remains from the knot.

Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell during sleep (that is, when they begin to become dirty in sleep) until they resemble women's breasts; and they remain putrid afterwards.

If the breast droops to the lower part and softens due to its size, as it happens with women: then it is necessary to make an incision in both of its upper sides with two crescent-shaped cuts similar to this shape, one containing the other at the ends so that the larger line contains the smaller, according to this shape from line b to line g. Cure it until it heals.

Chapter XLIX.
On the Section of an Apostema due to an Artery and a Vein.
When an artery ruptures and the skin above it consolidates, it often happens that an apostema forms there; and similarly, a vein may also rupture, causing an apostema and inflation to form in it.
And the signs by which it is recognized that an apostema and inflation are due to an artery or a vein are as follows: when the apostema is due to an artery, it is long and clustered deep in the body; and when you press the apostema with your fingers, it feels as if there is a hissing sound.
And what is for the Vein, is round in obvious body.
And the incision over this abscess is an error, and especially what is under armpits, groins, neck, and in many places of body; and it is very large. Therefore, care must be taken with iron in its treatment, and what is also in the extremities or head, care must be taken there as well.

Then puncture the place that is between two ligaments with a lancet until all the blood in it comes out, and the abscess is dissolved.
Then administer a treatment that generates pus, until the ligaments fall; then care for it with suitable ointments until it heals.
If the abscess is from an incision of a Vein, then it is necessary that you hold with your hand what you can from the abscess with skin. Then bind the abscess with a good ligament; according to what I told you in the ligature of a vein, with two parts and two ends of thread.
If you fear that the thread will be pulled out, then insert another point with another thread under the entire abscess near the incision; press, and bind your threads in four places.
Then cut the abscess in the middle of it, until when it comes out what is inside: then cut the redundancy of the skin, and release what is tied from it.
Then place on top of the boil that you have submerged in wine, and oil. Then administer a treatment which is made with linen cloths and ointments until it heals.
Book of the Head.
Chapter on abscess occurring from the twisting of nerves.
As an abscess occurs in an artery or vein, so it occurs in nerves: which occurs in them by a blow, or it occurs from excessive labor and similar things: and it happens most often in places assisting the bones (or joints), or heels, and in any place where the joints are moving: and the abscess is severe.
It resembles its color to the rest of the body and is found in several positions without pain: and when it is compressed with violence, it feels weak, like a faintness.
And the abscess is not gathered deep within the body, rather it is under the skin, and it moves to every part: and it does not reach forward or backward, neither towards the front nor towards the back.
What is found in the joints, therefore, should not be invaded with an iron tool. Perhaps there will be contraction.
But in that which is found in the head or forehead, puncture the skin with a lancet. If it is a small abscess, then hold it with forceps and cut it from the root.
And if it is large, then tie it with a hook and scour it: then remove it, and pack the wound with stitches: and treat it until it heals.

Chapter LII.
Chapter on the treatment of umbilical hernia.
A protrusion of the umbilicus occurs for many reasons. It may be due to hernias of the scrotum, which is above the abdomen; and it goes out from there either the althub or the intestine, according to what happens in other ruptures. Or it may be due to blood flowing from a vein, or an artery, as was mentioned earlier. Or it may be due to obstruction of wind in that place.
If it is due to a hernia of the scrotum and a protrusion of the testis; then its color is similar to that of an abscess and it is soft, without pain; and its position appears different. And if it is due to the protrusion of the intestine, then its position is, with what has been said, more pronouncedly different. When you press it with your fingers, it is concealed; then it returns, and perhaps there is a sound; and it becomes greatly enlarged at the entrance of the bath, and causes great pain.
But if it is due to moisture, it is soft; then it does not become concealed when pressed with the hand, nor does it contract, nor does it increase in size.
If it is due to blood, then with these signs an abscess appears dark red on the side of the back.
But if it is due to flesh grown; then the abscess is heavy, large, hard, and fixed to a certain extent according to its quantity.
If it is due to wind; then when touched, it is soft.
And the treatment in that case is to consider then whether the protrusion of the umbilicus is due to blood from an artery or vein, or wind; then it is necessary to forbid treatment of it. For in that case there is fear and dread, as I taught you in the chapter where I said abscesses due to an artery and vein.
If the protrusion of the navel is due to the intestine or hernia: then it is necessary that you command the patient, so that he holds his breath and stands extended and still. Then mark with the hot iron around the entire navel. Afterwards, order him to lie down on his back upon your hands. Then, with a broad spatula, circle around the navel in the area you have marked with the hot iron. Afterwards, stretch the middle part of the wound with a large hook. Then bind him around in a tight knot with thread or with a strong silk cord: and let the knot of the ligature be called an alexandrine.
Afterwards, open the extended middle part of the wound above the ligature. If you then find the hernia already captured by the ligature: then draw out the alexandrine, and insert your index finger into it, and push the intestine back towards the abdomen; and if you find a hernia, then take it with a hook and cut off its excess.
But if it is an artery or vein against you: then circle it much. Then return to your operation. And take two needles and insert strong threads into them; and insert the two needles into the circle you have made around the wound in the shape of a cross, causing them to pierce it.
Then tie the wound in four places with the needles; and if you wish, remove the needles and let the rotten flesh extend: and let it fall off by itself; or cut it when it becomes soft and rots.
Then care for him with what is necessary from ointments, until he is healed.
If the protrusion of the navel is from a hernia in him or from moisture: then sink the wound as we have said. And draw out blood, or moisture, which you find in it.
Then take care of the place with it that it heals.
Chapter LIII.
Chapter on the treatment of CANCER.
We have already said in the division of the species of cancer, and how to treat it with medications; and we must beware of treating it with iron, lest it be ulcerated; and we have said that cancer is generated in the matrix, and we have given a warning about its treatment.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer is in a place where it can be eradicated; such as when cancer is in the breast, hip, or similar members, to extract all of it; especially when it is beginning small.
But if it has grown old and is large, do not approach it.
For I could not heal from it anyone; nor have I seen anyone before me who reached that.
And the operation on it, when it is placed as we have said, is to precede and dissolve a weak person from black choler several times. Then make phlebotomy of it if you find it with a clear swelling.
Then prepare the weak person with a preparation in which he is placed during the operation.
Then thrust the hook-like instruments into the cancer that suit it. Then hollow out the cancer from all sides with the skin, according to examination, until nothing remains of its roots; and let the blood flow, but do not cut it quickly, rather squeeze the places, and remove the clotted blood completely with your hand, or as possible there with what instruments are available.
If however a flow of thick blood from the incision of an artery or vein opposes you; then cauterize the vein until the blood is cut off. Then care for yourself with the rest of the treatment, until it is healed.
On the treatment of Hydropisis.
Chapter LIV. We now describe the division of types of Hydropisis, and how water accumulates: and signs of each type, and its treatment with medications.
And that which is treated with iron, it is only the type of ascites alone: and it does not approach with iron the type of tympánitis: nor deeply the type of hypoascaris: for it is deadly.
If you have been treated for this type of hydropisis tympánitis with medications, and the treatment did not succeed: then consider. For if weakness has already come upon the sick person, or there is another illness in addition to hydropisis, such as cough or loose bowels, and similar ones: then beware of treating him with iron, for it is dangerous.
If you see the sick person exuding strength, and there is no illness other than hydropisis alone, and he is not a child nor an old man: then there is a way of operating on him, that you lift the sick man standing between your hands, and the attendant follows him and expresses his abdomen with his hand by pushing water to the lower part of the chest.
Then take a pointed sponge (spatiumile). It should have two pointed parts, long and having sharp tips like a spatiumile. However, it should contain something of shortness to prevent you from piercing through it into the intestine during the operation and damaging it.
Then observe. For if the hydropisis is generated from the intestines, then it is necessary that you extend with a section of about three fingers from the navel downwards along its upper part above the breastbone.
If, however, the generation of hydropisis is due to liver disease: then make your incision on the left side from the navel with three fingers.
And if its generation is due to the spleen, then let the incision be on the right side: and it is not necessary that there should also be an incision on the side towards which the sick person will lie, so that superfluities do not flow towards the weak place.
Then perforate the whole skin with an instrument. Then introduce yourself into that incision, and with the Spatula, slide your hand under the skin, as if you are scraping it: let the quantity that is scraped off be the size of a nail or about that.
Then perforate the Spatula until it reaches the empty place: and it is the place for water. Then remove it (the spleen), and introduce an instrument into the opening, which has this shape. And it is like a cannula: it is made of silver, copper or brass, smooth and polished; on its lower part there is a small hole, and on both sides there are three holes, two from one side, and one from the other: and the end of it is cut, in the manner of a reed incision, as you see; at the upper end of it is a loop.
For when the instrument reaches the water, then she immediately descends onto the instrument, therefore evacuate from the water a quantity of an hour.
Because if you evacuate more than is necessary from it, perhaps the sick person may die from the resolution of his animal spirit; or he may suffer a syncope that approaches death.
But evacuate from it according to its power, and according to what the dispositions of the sick person indicate to you from the power of his pulse, and from the goodness of it.
Then remove the instrument and retain the water.
This is because it is retained immediately on account of the skin which retains the hole that is on the spleen; about which I have told you to perforate it in this way.
Then on the second day, if you see that the patient can bear it, remove the instrument again and extract a small amount of fluid from water.
Keep it for several days without fear, and beware of error until there remains only a small amount in the water.
If you fear for the patient and let out much water, then care for him with warm sand, steam baths, sun and expect thirst, and care for him with the strongest medicines until he is cured. Then cauterize his stomach, spleen, and liver after removing the water, as I have described in what went before.
Chapter on the care of infants who are born where their bladders have not been pierced.
Chapter fifty.
When a child is born from the womb of his mother and the head of the afterbirth is not pierced or the opening is narrow or misplaced.
Therefore, it is necessary to pierce it immediately at the time of birth with a very sharp spatula in this manner.
Then place a fine nail made of lead into the opening and bind it; hold it for three or four days.
When he wishes to urinate, remove it (the nail) and mix it (with something). Then return it (the child) (to its mother's womb).
And if you do not put lead there, it is now possible that the urine that flows over the area will prevent the wound from closing.
The one whose opening is narrow, is treated with lead as we have said, for many days until it becomes wider.
Those in whom the opening is in a wrong place are injured. Because the opening is at the end of the tailbone of those who are born; therefore, it cannot urinate towards the front until it raises the tailbone with his hand to the higher parts. The generation is not in him, therefore, because the seed cannot reach the womb in a straight manner; and it is a very foul disease.
And the method of operation in that case is to make the sick one lie on his back. Then stretch out the head of the instrument with your left hand and make an incision at the place of the priapium, with a sharp or pointed tip, similar to cutting a reed or like rooting something, so that the middle part comes out like the head of the instrument; and let it fall through the hole in the middle as required.
And be careful during your operation to avoid bleeding. For this often occurs. Therefore oppose it with what causes the bleeding and take care of the wound until it heals.
Chapter on Albather (swelling) that occurs in the foreskin and head of the penis, rotting, blackening, and sticking.
Chapter 65.
These Albathers often occur in the penis, and it is a swelling of foul flesh.
And from this one kind is malignant, and another is not malignant.

If the Albather is in the foreskin of an uncircumcised penis and a part of the Albather is inside the foreskin and a part outside, then remove the Albather that is inside first, until it consolidates, and then take care of the outside; because when you treat it at the same time, the foreskin will not heal before it protrudes.
And it also happens in the testicles, and blackening and corruption of the prepuce. Therefore, it is necessary that you hollow out everything that has already blackened, and what is about to be corrupted or already is corrupted.

Chapter LVII.
On the cleansing of infants, and their cure due to mistake happening to them.
Circumcision is not a solution for continuity, like other wounds; however, since it comes from our operation, with our will, and its use is particularly in boys, it is necessary that we mark the operation as better in it, and guide the way to health more easily.
Therefore, I say that the ancients did not write about circumcision in any of their books; because they do not use it in their laws, and it is only what we have acquired through experience.
Because I have found that most craftsmen and phlebotomists use cleansing by cutting with a nail and forceps; they use alfecated, ligatured, and incised with the nail.
And indeed I have already tested all these methods, and have not found a better cleansing with forceps or ligature with thread.
Because in the cleansing with a nail, the skin often escapes. Because the foreskin has two layers of skin; therefore, perhaps the upper layer is cut, and the lower layer is torn; it is forced to incise again, and pain will occur. And when the cleansing that is made with alfecated, that is, with the finger, as shoemakers use, it is not cut off at the end of the male member; because perhaps it enters into its opening.
But in cleansing with the nail, perhaps iron enters, and ruins your operation; and indeed the skin of a boy is short by nature, and often such things occur that do not require cleansing; and I have seen this myself.
The experiment with forceps and ligature using thread was good to me, because the sharpness above is like the sharpness below, since the sharpness that is above is in proportion to the sharpness that is below. When you press your hand, the two sharpnesses correspond and cut according to one operation at once: and a compression is made in a similar shape, enclosing the skin of the branches from every side, so that no error occurs altogether.
The method of operation is that you make a guess, especially if it is from those who understand slightly, but you do not do it unless you tie the thread on the branch alone: and leave it until another day.
Then let him rejoice and be happy in every way as possible for you, because he receives his understanding from it. Then let him stand between your prepared hands of the appropriate size and let him not be sitting: and conceal the forceps in your hand or under your foot, so that the boy does not see them at all nor anything from the instruments.
Then insert your hand into his branch and blow on the skin, and pull it up until the head of the branch comes out. Then clean it yourself from that which adheres to it with dirt.
Then tie the marked place with double thread. Then bind below it a little bit more ligature. Then hold with your index finger and thumb the place of the lower ligature well, and cut between two ligatures. Then peel off the skin quickly upward, and extract the head of the branch. Then let the blood run out gradually (it is better), and put powder on top of it: and place a cloth on top of it in which a lamb's wool that has been boiled in rose water, crushed with fresh good olive oil has been spread; and leave him on top of it until another day: and take care of him with the rest of the treatment, until he is healed.
The form of the forceps for excision is as follows.
The tips of the two ends should be concave, and they should meet: let no branch of the nail protrude into them; and let the length of the two points be equal to the length of the two handles evenly.
However, an error occurs during excision, because perhaps the entire inner skin escapes, or a part of it at the incision site.
Therefore, one should stretch it out from your hour with your nail before the excision of the place and cut it evenly.
If you cannot hold it with your nail, then pull it out with a tweezers and cut it.
If it passes three days and what is below the inflamed area remains swollen, then let that go until the swelling subsides and the abscess becomes soft; peel off the scab with ease, and cut it according to how it is prepared for you: and beware of the tip of the probe. For it will not harm him thus.
Therefore take care of it with that which consolidates the wound with the powders, which we mentioned in the treatment of powders; and if it is cut beyond the measure from the skin and goes to the top, it will not harm him even thus.
Therefore take care of it until it heals.
Chapter LVIII.
Section on the extraction of a retained bladder in the bladder.
Urine retention in the bladder, comes from a blockage made of stone, or frozen blood, or pus, or born flesh, and similar things from what we said in the mode of treatment division.
And if the urine does not resolve and you see that its retention is due to a stone already in the neck of the bladder: then it is necessary that he who is sick be laid flat on his knees. Then his feet should be placed on top of his back, and he should stretch out his abdomen from the upper part of his back, and he should tighten his breath as much as possible for him. So when the neck of the bladder is pressed toward the backside to expel the stone, urine will be released.
If it does not resolve as we said and the patient is very strong over the sick person: then it is necessary to administer extraction with an instrument called syringe, which has this form (S-shape). It should be made of silver, and be thin, soft, concave like a feather pen reed in fineness, long like the palm of one hand and half: the tip should have a fine cannula.
And the method of urine outlet through this is that you take a doubled thread, tie it at its end with wool or cotton, good ligature: and introduce the end of the thread into the lower part of the syringe: and cut with scissors if there is any excess from the wool, but introduce forcefully into the cannula as one squeezes.
Then grease the syringe with oil or butter and white egg: and have the sick person sit on a chair, and warm the bladder, and his penis with moist oils and olive oil and warm water.
Then introduce the syringe into the penis gently until it reaches the root of the penis.
Then double it from above the part of the navel.
Then push the syringe into it until it reaches the bladder and feels weakened already approaching an empty place: this is not done according to this order, unless because the channel through which it goes has a twist in it.
Then stretch out thread with wool slowly. Wool follows flax.
Then pull it out and let the linen run through the urine way: then repeat the syringe, and do not stop doing that until the bladder is emptied, and a weakened alleviation is found.
§ On the quality of clysterization of the bladder with syringe.
Chapter LIX.
When there is an ulcer in the bladder or blood congeals in it or pus collects in it and it is necessary to distill water and medicines into it: then let it be done with the instrument called Clepshydra, and this is its form.
It is indeed mute, that is, closed. And in it there are three openings, two on one side and one on the other, as you can see.
The concave place where the thing that pushes is should be according to the quantity required for it without addition, until when something is pulled with it, it is attracted from humidities: and when it is pushed, with it it is expelled far away: this is how the clepshydra works, which shoots naphta, that is, Greek fire in the battles of Mars.
When it is desired to shoot humidities into the bladder, insert the end of the clepshydra into the humidity and pull with it what pushes upwards: because humidity is attracted into the concavity of the clepshydra.
Then insert its end into a rod, as we have said in a syringe. Then push moisture with it, for indeed the moisture immediately reaches the bladder and makes a weak person feel it.
Make a fine clyster for cleansing the bladder.
Make it from silver or gold; its head should resemble a syringe slightly, and below it there should be a cavity in which a cord can fall.
Then take the bladder of a sheep and place moisture within it for cleansing the bladder. Then tie it between two cavities with a strong thread, and heat the moisture slightly over fire.
Then insert the end of the clyster into a rod, then press your hand upon the bladder with moisture and pressure appropriate for cleansing until a weak person feels it, because the moisture has already reached the bladder.
If, however, the bladder is not present to you, then take a piece of parchment and make a circle out of it, and pierce it from every roundness. Then insert a strong thread into those holes, as they are rolled up. Then join the circle like glue; place on it what you wish from moisturizers, oils and waters.
Then tie it in the instrument; use it like you did with the bladder by squeezing with your hand until moisture reaches the bladder.
Chapter 60.
Chapter on Stone Extraction.
We have already said about the types of stones and their treatment with medicines, as well as the difference between a stone generated in the kidneys or bladder and its signs; we have also discussed surgery on stone with hand and section; this is a stone that is specifically generated in the bladder, it is held in a rod and I am explaining it with clear exposition and abbreviation.
I say therefore, that a stone formed in the bladder happens most often to children.
And among its symptoms is that the urine comes out from the bladder like water in its subtlety: and there appears in it white sand, and the sick person rubs his staff, and labors with it, and it hangs down often. Then the anus rises up and comes out together with it in many of them.
And the healing of children is easy until they reach fourteen years of age. It is difficult in old people. But in young men it is in the middle, because it is between that and its cure: and the healing is easier if the stone is larger; and if it is small, the cure is reversed for it.
When we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the sick person with an enema, which extracts all the feces that are in his intestines; for it sometimes prevents the detection of the stone during examination.
Then the sick person is to be received with his feet, shaken and moved towards the lower parts; so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder or jumps out from a high place several times.
Then make him sit between your hands, and his hands should be under his buttocks, so that the bladder is completely lowered towards the lower parts.
Then inquire about him and touch him from outside.
If you feel a stone within the space, then approach immediately with cutting upon it.
If it does not fall down when touched completely, then you must push the index finger with oil from the left hand if the sick person is a child; or the middle finger if the young man is full; and insert it into his anus, and inquire about the stone, until it is under your finger; and turn it gradually towards the neck of the bladder.
Then press upon it with your finger and push it towards the outside at the place where you wish to make the incision; and command the servant to press the bladder with his hand, and command another servant to extend the testicles with his right hand upwards; and with one hand, remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the part from the place where the incision is.
Then insert a spatula cutting (it), whose shape is as follows: And find (it) where it is between the anus and the testicles, not in the middle, towards the left side of the natives' (left); and make the incision over the stone (the kidney stone), and place your finger in the anus; and make the incision crosswise, so that the incision on the outside is broad, and the incision inside is narrow, according to the quantity, so that the outgoing of the Stone from this incision is not too large.
Perhaps the finger, which is in the anus, presses the stone at the incision, and comes out without difficulty.
And know that from the Stone are its angles and edges, why its outgoing is difficult on account of this.
And it is smooth, like a gland, and round; and the outgoing of it becomes easy.
To him who has angles and edges, add (the stone) to the crack (or fracture).
If it does not come out in this way, then you must fumigate (or cauterize) on top of it; or tie a ligature tightly around it, whose end is like the moon, which will squeeze the stone and not escape from it; or insert a subtle instrument beneath it with curved tips.
If you cannot do this (fumigate/cauterize) on top of it, then enlarge the opening slightly. If something stops you from doing so with blood, cut it off with a scissors.
If however the stone is greater than one, then press primarily on the large stone towards the bladder. Then cut above it. Afterwards, press a small one behind it; and similarly do if there are more than two.
If very large, then ignorance is that it separates from above by making a large cut. Since it happens that a patient dies from one of two things, either by dying or from frequent urine discharge; for this reason, the place does not heal completely.
But administer its expulsion until it comes out; or insert tools into the fracture with forceps until you extract it piece by piece.
When you have finished the operation, then fill the wound with turpentine, aloe, and dragon's blood; tie it up, and put over it a cloth soaked in olive oil and wine, or rose oil, and cold water; to let the abscess settle warmly.
Then turn the patient onto his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day. When you undress him, anoint the place with water and oil.
Then treat him with dymphneun ointment and basilicon ointment until he is healed.
If a hot abscess or one that corrodes occurs in the wound, and similar things happen; just as if blood congeals in the bladder and urine is prevented from coming out of it; and this is recognized by the expulsion of blood with urine. Therefore insert your finger into the wound and extract the blood. For if it remains, it provokes the corruption of the bladder and its rotting.
Then clean the wound with vinegar, water and salt; and apply everything that agrees with its healing until it heals completely.
And it is necessary during the whole treatment that you tie together both thighs and gather them, because of the medicines that are placed on the place.
If the stone is small and it is in the penis sheath and it obstructs the urine flow, then cure it with what I mentioned before, before you reach incision. For many times you are exempted from incision by this treatment, now I have proved that.
And take a perforating iron from an anvil, whose shape is like this: triangular at the end and sharp, fixed in wood.
Then take a thread, tie it with the penis under the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
Then insert the perforating iron into the penis with ease, until the perforating reaches the stone; and turn the perforating by your hand slowly in the same stone; and press the perforation until you make it penetrate from the other side.
Therefore urine is discharged immediately.
Then press your hand on what remains of the stone from the outside part of the penis. It breaks and comes out with urine, and heals the sick one.
If this treatment is not prepared for you for some reason that prevents it; then tie a thread under the stone and another above the stone. Then cut above the stone on the same penis between the two ties. Then remove it. After that, loosen the ligament and wash off the congealed blood that forms on the wound.
And it is not necessary to tie a thread under the stone unless to prevent it from returning to the bladder; and another thread above, unless when the thread is loosened after the removal of the stone, the skin returns to its place, covers the wound; and for this reason it is necessary that you do this when you tie the thread above, so that you lift the skin to the higher part, so that it returns at your convenience, and covers the wound, as we said.

Chapter LXII.
[Chapter Title] On the Section of a Watery Hernia.
A watery swelling is not anything other than an accumulation of moisture in the albino scrotum, which contains the egg: and it is called a scrotum.
And sometimes it is within its own pouch prepared for it by nature in the part of the egg, until it is thought to be ripe: which is another kind of egg and is the skin of the scrotum that we mentioned: and such a thing does not happen often.
The generation of this [swelling] comes from the weakness that happens to testicles, for this material flows towards them. And sometimes it happens due to a blow on the testicles.
This moisture has many colors. Indeed, the color of this [swelling] is either becoming yellowish, or red like blood, or dirty, black, or watery white: and such a thing is worse.
The signs by which it is known where the accumulation of water is, are these. For if it is in the white scrotum that we mentioned, then the abscess is round and slightly longer than an egg shape: and the testicle does not appear because moisture contains it from all sides.
And if the moisture is within its own pouch, then the abscess is round with a part of an egg shape: and for this reason the man dies because it is another kind of egg.
And if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white scrotum, then it falls under touch.
When the vision perceives the color of the moisture, then test it for the color of the moisture in an abscess with a probe square, whose shape has been mentioned before. According to what goes out in the tracks of the probe, judge about that which is within it.
When we come to the treatment with iron, then it is necessary that you order the weak man to be bled if possible for him, and see his body full.
Then it lies on its back upon a low table, and many cloths are placed beneath it.

Then pierce the albugine full of water through a large hole, and drain out all the water.
Then separate the two lips of the incision with scissors, and stretch the albugine to above; and do not touch the skin of the testicles enclosing it; and cut the albugine in any way possible for you to cut it, either entirely or piecemeal, especially the delicate side. For if you do not examine carefully, in the incision of it there is no security that water will not return.

Then take care of it as other wounds, until it is healed.
If you find the egg corrupted by blackness elsewhere, then it is necessary to tie vessels, which are suspending, fearing blood flow.
Then remove the testicle with its suspending ligament, and extract the egg; afterwards take care of it as I have said.
If water is gathered in two parts, then you know that there are two branches; cut the other part equally as you have done on the other one.
And if it is even so that the operation becomes one, then do this: afterwards remove blood. And insert wool immersed in oil or in rose oil; and place another wool outside which you have soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over the two testicles, and look inside the abdomen; and put double cloths on top of them, and they are pillows; and tie them above with a ligament having six sections.

And at times this branch is artificially treated with a cautery in the place of the section using iron; and it is so that you take a sharp knife-like cautery and cut the skin of the testicles; and it is lit, as I have said; until when the bladder filled with water appears; then take the cautery, according to this form.

De caunditate operis quod vocatur rinotomia
On the care of Fleshy Roots [or Root-like Growths]
You should know that during the operation called rhinotomy, there is a risk of serious consequences in many configurations [or situations]. For this reason, it seems advisable to me to avoid it [the operation].
And I remember the operation and the appearance of the excised growths [or lesions].
I say that many growths occur in the body, from which the testicles are formed; this happens due to various causes [or reasons].
Or it is due to an excess of something sharp or acidic that flows towards the testicles. Or from a blow [or impact].\]   Caput LXIV.
And the color of the growth is similar to that of the body and it does not cause pain; it is a severe growth.
Perhaps it is a stone-like growth whose color is dark and there is no sensation in it [or from it].
Sometimes it occurs due to a knotting of the arteries and swelling of them [or its], as I have already mentioned; or from swelling of the veins.
That which is caused by swelling of the arteries can be known through the position of the growth, as when you press it with your fingers. And it is not necessary to touch it completely [or directly].\]   Caput LXV.
