That which is made from swelling of veins, does not disperse anything under pressure with fingers.
It is now possible that on this kind a section may be made and on the rest of the flesh: and it is to make an incision in the skin of the testicles. Then stretch the egg upward and remove it along with its white membrane: and release the suspension from the bladder, and tie the bladder: and cut the suspension after you have removed it from all parts of the egg.
If therefore the egg is consolidated with those born flesh, then you must draw out the egg and cut it.
And if there is an adhesion between something from the sifaket or in that which is between the bladders: then it is necessary to release all that adhesion and cut it with a round incision.
But if there is a birth of flesh in the place of the adhesion which is behind: then it is necessary to cut all of it and draw out the egg, as we have said.
When your operation is completed, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine: then take care of it with the rest of the treatment until it heals.
Chapter LXIIII (62nd Chapter).
Chapter on the Care of Branches, which is with Vine.
A vine is an abscess enclosed by some enclosure resembling a bunch of grapes with the softening of testicles; and it is difficult to move and exercise or walk on a weak person.
And in the treatment of this illness there is fear because of what happened before its memory.
But it is necessary to say that the operation on it should be done according to what the first ones did.
Therefore I say that you must make the weak one sit on a raised seat. Then push down on the sack supporting the testicles. Then hold the skin of the testicles with your fingers, with forceps close by the rod: and let another servant hold it, and stretch it with a strong extension.
Then make an incision with a broad, sharp, crosswise cut in the direction of the vessels, until the vessels are exposed.
Then scrape away from all sides, as I told you in the removal of arteries in the temples.
Then insert a needle with a double thread into them and tie it at the first places where knots occur; and tie it again at the end of these. Then cut it in a straight middle section along the body length, and draw out what has accumulated from foul, corrupted moisture.
Then care for the wound with treatment of other wounds where pus is being generated, so that the vessels nourishing one of the testicles fall away. For it is not bad in this way.
If, however, knots occur in all the vessels, then they must be drawn out because of this for the testicles along with the vessels: lest the nourishment of the egg is deprived due to the incision, and it rots or burns and is not a help with them.
Chapter LXV.
§ On the treatment of intestinal branches.
The outcome of this branch is from an incision which happens on the extended sifach above the abdomen in the groin area from the side of the abdomen.
Why do the intestines descend from that rupture to one of the testicles? And this rupture is either from the sifach, or its extension.
These two types occur due to many causes: either from a blow, or a jump, or a loud noise, or heavy lifting, and similar things.
And the sign is when it is from extension of a fistula. It happens gradually over a long period of time and not suddenly; it is an abscess equal in depth to the turning (meaning, it protrudes from the skin): because a fistula presses on the intestine.
And the sign of it (meaning the fistula) when it is from incision of a fistula, because it causes intense pain suddenly at its beginning; and it is an abscess different (meaning, it appears under the skin near the surface); and that is due to the exit of intestine, and its course towards the exterior through the fistula.
And sometimes it comes out with the intestine; and this is called Intestinal Ramie (Ramex intestinalis) or "Zirbia"; and sometimes it happens with flatulence.
And sometimes it runs into the intestine with feces and is retained there; and in this case it is a danger to the sick, because it causes severe pain, especially when it is pressed.
And in treating this disease with iron there is fear; therefore one must be careful to avoid accidents in it.
The method of operation is that you instruct the sick person to reduce his intestine with his own hand into the concavity of its own depth, if he obeys. Then he lies on his back on his neck between your hands and raises his legs.
Then you stretch the skin that follows the skin upwards and cut the whole skin of the scrotum along its length. Then fix the two lips of the incision with hooks according to what you need for opening the incision with them; and the incision should be in accordance with its size, so that it is possible for the egg to come out from it.
Then scrape the fistula (sifach), and everything under the skin of the scrotum until the white of the fistula becomes hard all around; then insert your little finger into what follows the testicle, into where there is the white of the fistula, which is under the skin of the egg, and between the fistula and follow it, without any adhesion that is in the back part of the egg.
Then move with the right hand to the inner skin of the testicles; and as this is done, extend the white linen cloth upward with the left hand; and lift out the egg with the linen cloth to the part of the incision; and instruct the attendant to spread the egg upward; and you solve the adherence which is behind the complete solution.
And ask your fingers if there is nothing there from the intestine rolled up in the hard white linen cloth. If you find anything from it, then push it downward to the lower abdomen.
Then take the hook, in which there is a thick thread, made of linen from ten threads; and insert it at the end of the white linen cloth, that is to say, at the tunica, which follows the incision: on the skin of the testicles; then cut the ends that project from the thread until there are four threads. Then bind together some of them with a figure in the form of a cross; and tie it with the silk mentioned earlier, which is beneath the ligament of the testicles: so that no pus from those things that nourish them may pass to them: lest there be a hot abscess. And place the ligament again outside the first ligament, at a distance of more than two fingers from it. And after these two ligaments, let a piece of the silk, which is beneath the skin of the testicles, remain of the size of a finger; and cut the rest entirely in round form, and remove the egg from it.
Then cut at the lower part of the skin of the testicles with the incision from which blood and pus run, as we have said in that which has been mentioned before.
Then apply wool soaked in oil and place it on the wound; and administer the ligament as we have said. And sometimes the white sifach is cauterized as we have said, after its incision, fearing blood flow. This sentence translates to: It often happens that... (The rest of the sentence is missing in your quote.) And release the ligament until it falls by itself.
If however the case persists, then it should be scorched with hot water: and place upon it what we have said until it falls.
Then take care of the wound with the treatment of wounds, until it is healed.
Chapter 66.
Chapter on windy nose (or nasal congestion).
In this windy nose, I have not seen anyone who dared to treat it with iron.
And first they said that it happens as we have said in the windy nose which is with the grape vine. That is, to tie vessels after the section on it below with ease: then cut in the middle, and treat afterwards with what opens it up until the vessels fall out: and take care of the wound as we have said until it heals.
Chapter 67.
Chapter on rupture that happens in the groins.
When rupture occurs in the groins as we have said, and a place comes out, and nothing from the intestines descends to the testicles: and if it does descend, that is not enough, and it returns in all hours: but if it continues with this condition, a fissure is added in the sifach until the intestines descend into the sifach.
And it happens from the extension of the sifach, which is in the groins as we have said. That is, because the sifach extends: then it is softened, and the place is opened and comes out.
Its treatment is with cautery, as its narrative has preceded.
And sometimes it is cured with iron, according to this method: and there is, that the sick one lies on his back upon your hands. Then cut the place of the rupture of abscesses and prominences, with a cut along its width, according to the size of three fingers.
Then tie the algus (a kind of bandage) and, which are under the skin, until when it appears album (white matter) that is below the skin following it.
Then take the lancet and place it upon the prominent part from the album, and press it to the depth of the abdomen.
Then make two incisions upon the extremity of the radius (arm) from the album, and sew one of them with the other; then extract the extremity of the radius.
And do not cut the algus (bandage) at all, nor stretch it, nor anything else, as I told you in the treatment of intestinal branches (hernia).
Then treat that with the treatment for wounds. When therefore you cut the threads, clean it and restore the wound, until it is consolidated (healed).
For the sifach (another kind of bandage) contracts and no additional prominence of rupture is added.
And cautery is better in this place, because it is closer to health.
Chapter LXVIII.
Chapter on the softening of scrotum skin (hydrocele).
The skin of the scrotum is often softened in some men, because meat that is between it becomes soft and its appearance is spoiled.
Therefore, it is necessary for the one who asks for its treatment to make the sick man lie on his back and cut all the skin that has been softened over the natural skin.
Then gather the two flaps with stitches: and if you wish, remove three or four times the excess of softened skin with stitches, or a firm one.
Then cut between the sutures.
Then care for the healing of the remaining wounds until the thread falls out.
Head LXIX.
[Title: On Castration.]
You should know that castration is forbidden under our law; therefore, it would be permissible for me not to mention it in this book of mine. Its mention is only necessary for the sake of two methods.
One reason is that it should be known by the physician when he is asked about it; and so that he may know its treatment when it occurs.
The other reason is that we often need the castration of certain animals, for the sake of our benefits from it, such as sheep, hogs, cats, and similar animals.
I therefore say that castration is performed in two ways. Or by rubbing (attrition).\]   Aut per subtractionem Or by cutting and separating (fissure and section).
In the first (attrition), the method of operation is that we make the animal sit in warm water until its testicles soften and become limp and hang down. Then rub them with your hand until they dissolve and do not appear under touch.
In the castration by cutting and separating (fissure and section), it is necessary that you hold the animal and press its scrotum with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensory ligament and cut over all the egg (ovum) with one incision, until two eggs are revealed: then cut each of them after you have peeled off the skin and do not leave anything on it except a thin piece of membrane that is above the vessels.
And this method of castration is better than the one by rubbing (attrition), because rubbing may leave something from the testicles, for which reason the animal desires copulation.
Then care for the wound until it heals.
Head 70.
Chapter on the care of Hermaphrodites: two methods.
Hermaphroditus is from men according to two modes. One of them is because there appears in him what follows the space or in the skin of the testicles, in that which is between two testicles, the figure resembling a female vulva, in which hairs are present; and sometimes urine flows from it what is in the skin of the testicles.
In women there is a single kind, and it is the female's nipple on the forehead like a small man's testicle protruding to the exterior; of which one is like a man's Priapus, and two are like two male testicles.
The treatment of the three kinds, two from men, and one from women, is: because it is necessary to cut the added flesh until the impression of them escapes. Then treat these wounds by the treatment of other wounds.
However, in the second kind of men's, from which urine emerges, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no operation, nor is there any treatment at all.
Chapter LXXI.
Chapter on Incising Tentiginis and Protruding Flesh in Women's Wounds.
A Tentigo may be added to what is natural, until it becomes obscene and unsightly; and sometimes it swells so much in some women that it expands like in men, and reaches intercourse.
Therefore, it is necessary to hold the excess of Tentigo with the hand, or with a hook, and cut it; and not to make deep cuts, especially at the root, so that bleeding does not occur.
Then treat this itself by the treatment of wounds, until it heals.
Flesh that arises is the flesh that is born in the opening of the matrix, until it fills it; and perhaps it emerges to the exterior like a tail; and because of this some call the illness tailed. Therefore, it is necessary to cut it as we cut Tentigo and heal it until it heals.
Chapter on the Alratic treatment, which is the female's nipple not pierced.
Chapter LXXII.
The artery (or vein) of a woman should be unbroken, or the opening should be small. It is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to the preceding illness; and it itself occurs either from tissue born naturally added or subtle or thick; and it forms either in the depth of the womb or in its sides or above or below it; and it prevents coitus, impregnation, childbirth, and perhaps menstruation.
And the knowledge of this (condition) is obtained by the examination of an obstetrician, if the protrusion is visible nearby.
But if it is not visible, then search for it with your fingers or a probe.
If the protrusion is from subtle thick tissue and it is near two lips; then approach it and tear it off.
It is (also) to place small beads on top of two lips.
Then place the tips of both your hands simultaneously, and the woman should be on her back with extended legs. Then spread the two lips forcefully until the subtle thick tissue is torn and the protrusion is opened.
Then take thread and wet it with oil, place it on the site; and let the woman sit on it daily, so that the area does not harden from another cause.
If the thick tissue is large and thick; then it should be cut with a broad, flat instrument like a myrtle leaf.
If the protrusion is from tissue born naturally; then hang it with tweezers and cut it; and have medicines with you that stop blood flow without causing bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, and pitch mixed with egg white.
Then administer a wide cannula made of lead to prevent the wound from hardening quickly, hold it for several days; and apply flax linen, then treat the rest with the usual treatment until it heals.
And when sometimes the birth in the womb occurs of flesh of other things: therefore it is necessary that they are to be cut according to this manner: while it is not a Cancerous aposteme, for a Cancerous aposteme, which is in the womb, there should be no opposition at all with iron.
Chapter LXXIII.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids, Athehelil and Bothor for red ones in women's ulcers.
Hemorrhoids indeed are the opening of the vein's orifices, until much blood constantly flows out of them.
When therefore hemorrhoids become chronic, they become piles: and I have already said regarding their division of their kinds and the signs of them; and here I will say what receives treatment from them, and what does not.
Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids which are in the opening of the womb and do not appear to the sense: then there is no treatment with iron for them.
But those which are on the opening of the womb above where the sensation falls upon them, are those which can be treated.
Therefore, it is necessary to introduce a woman into a cold house. Then extend Athehelil with forceps, or with rough cloth, and cut them from their roots.
Then powder over them on the flow of blood from one incision without crushing: such as ashes of incense, and dragon's blood, and pitch, and similar to them.
Then push his feet against the wall at the hour of one. Then lay her down in cold water.
If the flow of blood persists: then make her sit in a decoction of sumac, and pomegranate rind, and unripe lemons, and similar to them.
Then take barley flour, and knead it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with it on his back.
If therefore blood is cut with it, good; and if not, make to adhere winds (blow) on the back, and nipples, without incision.
Then take wool and immerse it in the juice of thistle, or the juice of argol, or the juice of wild olive leaves, that is, agalantha, Pontic wine, and make to adhere leech.
When therefore the abscess has ceased, then care for the place with ointments until it heals.
Albath, however, is red and resembles the heads of onions, and has a rough appearance.
Therefore it is necessary that you cut what appears from it, according to what I said in the onion, equally; and care for it until it heals.
Chapter LXXXIV.
§ On Perforation of a Dead Fetus in the Womb.
In the womb various species of abscesses occur, such as cancer, stone-like abscess, ulcers, adubelas, alekilas, that is, herpes, fistulae, hemorrhoids, ragadiae, thistle and hot abscess.
And I myself have already said all these diseases and their species, and the signs of them, and their cures, in division; it is necessary that I say in this treatise about hot abscess that occurs in the womb, which is one of those abscesses that collect pus, and you wish to know how its opening with iron is done.
Therefore consider it. Then if the pain of the abscess in its onset is sharp with striking and burning, and fever: and you see it redden; if it falls upon sensation, then do not hasten with its perforation; and care for it with what helps for maturation until when the sharpness of the symptoms subsides.
Then it is necessary that you make the woman sit on a bench which has two arms, and she should recline or lean upon her back, and gather her feet towards the lower part of her belly: and her hips should be expanded, and she should place her arms below her knees, and tie each one with a bandage suitable for that.
The midwife should then sit on the right side, and administer the tool for opening the matrix. (The matrix is another name for the womb.)
And it is necessary that when you are going to administer this tool, that you feel with a deep rod the depth of the woman's matrix: so that what enters from the instrument is not more than the depth of the matrix, and does not harm the weak (woman).
If the instrument is too deep, then it is necessary that you place pillows on top of the depth of the woman's matrix: so that the entrance of the instrument is not all the way into the depth of the matrix: and it is necessary that you place a rebozo (a long narrow piece of cloth used as a shawl, or in this case probably referring to a twisting motion) on the upper side of the instrument: and that you hold the instrument and turn the rebozo around until the depth of the matrix opens.
When it appears that there is an imminent delivery, and it is touched with the hand, and it is soft and smooth: then it is necessary that she (the mother) moves herself towards her head with a broad spatula (a large flat tool).
When the pus comes out (from the birth canal), then it is necessary that you place a linen cloth soaked in rose oil or green oil, in which there is some styptic (a substance used to stop bleeding) on the wound: and place the linen cloth, and make an incision in the depth of the matrix.
And place outside on the matrix (the birth canal), and on the comb (a tool used to separate the birth passage) a clean wool cloth soaked in water in which wormwood has been boiled.
Then it should be treated with an appropriate ointment two days later, until it heals.
The matrix and the wound are sometimes cleansed, so that they are cleaned with water and honey; then, with water in which the root of the lily or long aristolochia has been boiled; then, it should return to an ointment.
If the wound is hidden within the matrix internally, then it is necessary to prohibit its treatment with iron; rather, it should be treated as previously said for division.
Chapter 70.
Doctrine of obstetrics, how to treat living embryos that have come out in an unnatural manner (in the form of a monster).
It is necessary for the obstetrician to know first the shape of a normal birth.
Therefore, the signs of this [normal birth] are as follows: when you see a woman pressed toward the lower parts, and she desires to smell the air, and there is a fetal head felt above her [womb], and she quickly gives birth; then you will know that this delivery is in the natural form, and its exit is over the top of the head, and the posterior part with it; either suspended, or hanging from the navel.
If you see these signs, then it is necessary to press the womb so that the embryo descends quickly.
For when it descends over its head, it will also descend the posterior part with it; and it should be cleaned from these excess fluids using good cleanliness.
But if it is other than this delivery, it is unnatural, inadmissible.
Because sometimes a fetus comes out with its feet first, and its body comes out before its head, and one of its feet or hands; or the head and one hand come out; or the navel comes out; and perhaps it turns over to its neck, and similar unnatural forms.
It is necessary therefore for the Obstetrician that he should be wise, skilled in all these matters, and let him beware of error and deception; and I am showing every figure from them, and how there is understanding in it, and it shall be signified by that, and it shall stand upon it.
When the fetus comes out upon its own head in its natural delivery, and it becomes strong upon the woman, and labor is difficult for her, and you see the power of hers already weakened: then make her sit on a chair, or women hold her; and warm up her belly with fennel decoction, and with moist oils.
Then the midwife introduces a small spatula between her fingers and finds the second finger, and cuts it with it, using her own nail, until what is within her due to moisture runs out; and press the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
If it does not descend, then it is necessary that the woman be cleansed with fennel mucilage, with sesame oil.
Then order her after the cleansing, that she be pressed; and make her sneeze with a snuffbox, and hold her nose and her own for an hour. The fetus will come out immediately.
If two hands of the fetus come out first, it is necessary to reduce them gently little by little. If it does not obey in the entrance, then place the woman on a chair and lift up her feet; then strike the chair on the ground; and the woman must be held so that she does not fall due to the blow.
If the hands do not come out and the fetus dies; then cut them and extract the remaining fetus; and tie her hand with cloth, and extract it equally; for he will come out himself.
Outcome of the embryo above its feet. When the fetus comes out above its feet, then it must be pushed up; afterwards, turn the fetus gradually; finally, lay him flat.
Then take one of its feet and stretch it gradually.
When they have come out up to the hips, then order him to be pressed and let him sneeze with his mouth open; for he will be born if God wills it.
And if it does not come out as we have said, then gradually withdraw the fetus until you place him in a natural position. For he will be born then with an easy delivery.
If it is forbidden as we have said: then take from the mastic tree resin and sesame oil, and soluble gum; crush all well in a mortar with good pounding; then anoint with it the woman's womb and below her belly. Then let her sit in warm water until she feels the afterpains.
When you see that the lower parts are now warmed, then give her a fumigation of myrrh and apply it. When one hour has passed, then let her sit on a chair. Then let her sneeze; and pinch her nose and mouth; and press the lower part of the belly with gentle pressure. For the child will be born immediately.
Outcome of the fetus above knees and hands. When it comes out in this manner, then order him to introduce his hands gradually. Then the woman lies on her back and let her feet hang down; and she herself lies on the bed and clasps her hands together. Then press gently on the abdomen of the woman. Then remove what is beneath his feet from the puluinaribus until it is prepared below. If the fetus does not come out, then grasp his feet and move them forcefully. Then press what is above the hypocondria gradually until the fetus ascends to higher places. Then insert your hands and feel the fetus gradually; and order the woman to press herself until the fetus comes out.
The fetus exits with a broad hanging from the hands. It must be reduced by means of the hand. If it cannot be reduced (by the hand), then lift the woman and make her walk.
If she cannot walk, then lay her on a bed and strike her legs forcefully.
Then apply the ointment you have prepared from mucilages.
If she receives the birth, then make her sit on a seat. Then strive for the reduction of the hand and feel the fetus according to its natural shape; and make the woman sneeze and order her to press herself until it comes out.
The fetus exits above its neck with spread hands, and its face is turned towards the back of its mother. The midwife must hold the hand of the fetus, then turn it gradually and feel it easily.
When it is felt, then place it on the oil and mucilages that I have mentioned.
Then order her to move it gently. When you have done this, then make her sit on a seat and order her to lean towards the right side. Then order her to press herself; and make her sneeze with force.
The outcome (of the surgery) is a preterm baby on the side. When the fetus descends to the opening of the womb in this manner with the presenting part (i.e., second twin or breech), then you should cut the presenting part with your nail until it is evacuated due to moisture.
If the fetus hangs with its face and neck, then you should make an incision from the navel to prevent it from being retained and dying.
Then push the fetus to the interior (to deliver it) until you place it in the correct position. And tell the woman to compress herself several times: for it will come out with an easy delivery.
Delivery of twins or multiple babies. Know that twins are born often, and sometimes three, and even four. However, this is unusual and rare.
But five is indeed beyond nature, and they do not live fully: it contains them, even though the second one binds them together with the cord connected to each of their navels. And they can be separated by cutting through the sifach, which distinguishes between them and connects them with a bond at their navels.
Sometimes they come out as a single fetus does in a natural delivery, easily. And sometimes they come out with an unnatural exit, as we have mentioned.
If some of them are difficult in childbirth and reach the conditions we have described as unnatural, then care for them as we have mentioned: let a skilled midwife be present, who performs with ease and slowness and takes every measure to help according to all possible shapes so that what is prepared may lead to their salvation.
Remembering that which forms in the womb from embryos and miscarries.
Sometimes one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, or more than ten are formed in the womb and miscarry: I have already witnessed a woman who miscarried seven, and another fifteen, all fully formed.
What was done was measurement by the glorious wise one.
This whole matter should be in the science of obstetrics. Perhaps it will reach a similar one, therefore oppose it with what is needed.
Chapter LXXVI.
Chapter on the extraction of the dead fetus.
When you care for a dead fetus with what I said in the division from the medicine, and it does not come out, and you must perform an operation with your hand, then you should consider.
If the woman is of sound virtue and not with any accident from which her loss is feared: then she should be laid on her back on the bed, with her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised; and a servant should hold her from two sides, or tie her to the bed, so that her body is not pulled out during the extraction of the fetus.
Then the mouth of the womb should be moistened with oils, albumen of egg and linseed meal.
Then the obstetrician should anoint his hand with these oils and mucilages; then he should introduce it into the womb gently. Then he should ask her where a place is to be found for the hooks in the fetus, and places corresponding to it.
Therefore consider then if the fetus is prepared to descend onto its head; then fasten hooks in its eyes, or neck, or mouth, or palate, or under its beard, or in its armpits, or near the ribs, and under the breastplates.
If the descent is onto its feet, then on the chest and middle ribs.
And it is necessary that the hook be held with the right hand; and make a wound at the place between the fingers of the left hand; and introduce it gently with the hand, and fasten the hook in one of those places which we said, until it reaches an empty spot.
Then fix another hook or third one, if needed: so that the constriction is equal and it does not slip to one side.
Then extend the extension equally and not let it be just along a straight line but move it towards every direction in order to relieve its opening: as it is done with a tooth during its extraction.
And it must be softened that which is between [the hooks]. If a part remains stuck, then the midwife should bind certain fingers with oil and insert them from that side in order to turn it with them.
If a part of the fetus comes out then the hooks should be moved to another higher place: do this until the whole fetus comes out.
If a hand comes out before the others and cannot be retracted due to its swelling: then a cloth should be wound around it. Then remove [the hand] until when the whole one comes out, cut it at the junction of the foot or elbow: and thus you must do with the other hand and both feet.
If the fetal head is large, or if there is swelling in its delivery or water has gathered in its head: then a pointed spatula (Spatumile) should be inserted between the fingers and the head should be crushed and water extracted; or it should be broken with the instrument called Almisdac, whose shape comes with the shapes of the other instruments in the chapter that follows this.
Similarly do so if the fetus is of large-headed nature: then it should be separated with an algengatum; or extract it with a misdach, as we said. Then pull out the bones with forceps.
If the head comes out and swells at the neck: then it is squeezed, until the moisture within the chest is released.
If it does not become complicated and does not obey towards the exit: then cut off the head piecemeal, as far as possible for you.
If it is below the abdomen [location of the wound] and is an abscess or contains hydrops: then it should be perforated, until the moisture runs out from it.
But if the fetus is above its feet, then its pulling is easy, and its direction towards the bone of the matrix is light.
But if it gets twisted in the abdomen or chest: then you should extract it along with the cloth that you have wrapped over your hand; and open the abdomen or chest, until what is inside runs out.
But if other limbs are removed and the head returns: then let the midwife insert her left hand. If the mouth of the matrix is open, then insert your hand deep into the matrix and search for the head with it and pull it towards you with your fingers up to the mouth of the matrix; then insert a hook or hooks and pull it along with them.
If the mouth of the matrix is twisted due to a hot abscess that has occurred to it: then it should not be pressed on it, but rather warm liquids and ointments should be administered; and apply plasters; and sit in water that softens and moistens.
If the fetus is on its side, it can be turned over; then administer what I have said for a live fetus.
If that cannot be done, then cut it piecemeal and extract it.
And you must not leave anything of the placenta inside at all.
When you complete your surgery, then administer what I have said for hot abscesses that occur in the matrix.
If bleeding occurs, then it should be let down into cold water, and administer the remaining treatment.
I myself have seen a woman, in whose womb a child had died; then she became pregnant again on top of that one, and another child also died. After a long time, a boil occurred on his navel, which became swollen until it was opened; and it began to discharge pus.
I was therefore called for his treatment, and he was treated for a long time; but the wound did not heal.
Therefore, I applied to him some strong adhesive plasters; and bone came out from the place. Then a few days passed, and another piece of bone came out. I was therefore amazed when there was no bone in the womb.
Therefore, you thought because the children who had died were of bones.
I therefore asked for the wound and extracted many bones from a woman who was in good condition; and she lived like this for a long time, and hardly discharged pus from the place.
I did not fix this foreign object here unless there was knowledge about it and assistance from the physician-artist in treatment.
Chapter LXXVII.
Chapter on the shapes of necessary instruments for extracting a child.
The form of the Spindle which opens the uterus.
Here below is the form of the Stricture Device, by which books are equalized, having equally two spindles at both ends of two pieces of wood. However, this Spindle should be more delicate than the Stricture Device: and it should be made either of Ebony or of Boxwood.
And the width of all the pieces should be like two fingers: and the edge of each one is like a single finger, and the length of each is a palm (hand) and half, or slightly less: and in the middle of two pieces there are two additional parts made of the same kind of wood, which have already been fixed to both ends, whose length is half a palm and a little more: and the width of either one is like two fingers or a little less.
And these two additional parts are inserted into the cavity of the matrix (womb), so that it opens when you rotate the two spindles.
Another form resembling this one, but more delicate and lighter.
It should be made of Ebony or Boxwood, similar to the form of forceps (tweezers). However, at its end there should be two additional parts as you see here above: and the length of each of the additional parts is like a palm: and the width of either one is like two fingers.
When you wish to open the uterus with it, then make the woman sit on the bed with her feet hanging down, with what is between her thighs opened. Then insert these two connected additional parts into the uterus: and you are holding the lower end of the instrument between her thighs. Then open your hand with the instrument in the same way as you do with forceps, equally according to the amount that you wish from the opening of the mouth of the uterus, until the midwife does whatever she wants.
Form of Dizziness other than what the ancients called Form of Forced Delivery, by which is delivered the fetus.
Forma of Misdelivery, by which a large head is crushed: and it resembles a pair of forceps, having teeth at the end, as you see.
And sometimes it occurs in the shape of a long forceps as you see, having teeth like those of a saw, by which it is cut and crushed.
Form of a Shears having one spine.
Form of a Shears having two spines.
Form of Spatula having two ends for cutting off the head.
Form of two wider Spatulas.
These instruments are used in all cases, and the more their number and types multiply, the quicker they are for use by an artist, and the higher among men, because of their quantity.
Therefore do not neglect that an instrument is prepared by you. For it is indeed essential for their use.
Chapter LXXVIII:
Chapter on the Second Extraction (Cesarean section).
When the Afterbirth is retained during childbirth, then it is necessary to instruct the weak woman to retain her breath. Then make her sneeze with powder and press your hand over her mouth and her nose. If it comes out through this way, it is good.
If not: then take a pot, and make a hole in the cover; place within it herbs opening the womb, such as camomile, rue, anise, fennel, hartshorn, wood-sorrel, centaury; take all these herbs, or some of them, and immerse them in water, and put them over fire.
Then place a plug of reeds over the hole of the pot's cover and another end into the womb; hold it until the vapor reaches the cavity of the womb.
Then make her sneeze again, as I have said. The afterbirth will come out easily.
If it remains after this treatment and does not come out: then order the midwife to immerse her hand in sesame oil or althea mucilage. Then she will insert her finger and seek for the afterbirth. When she finds it, then take it and gradually pull it out.
If it is attached deeply in the womb, then insert the hand as I have said, until when she finds the afterbirth and pulls it out gradually along with its right and left side; this must be done without falling from the strong pull: indeed, it should be rotated easily to the right and left sides; afterwards, add more to the force of the pull. It will then obey and be preserved, and come out from the attachment.
If the bone of the matrix is dislocated, as we have already narrated: treat it with stimulation (or shaking) and with a remedy from an earthenware pot with herbs.
If it does not come out with all that we have mentioned, then be careful not to tire yourself by repeatedly attempting extraction.
However, whatever comes out from the matrix bone towards the woman's hip, tie it up (or bind it). Then cleanse her with a four-drug ointment (a mixture of olive oil, castoreum, rose oil and galbanum). For in a few days it will rot her, dissolve, and come out.
However, when it begins to rot, let it be raised from her towards the stomach and head, and it will harm the already weakened part. Therefore, appropriate fumigations should be administered for this purpose.
Some of the ancients have already tried fumigation with nasturtium and dried figs.
The shape of the instrument used for fumigation during retention (or delayed delivery) of a second child or menstruation.
Make it similar to an alca, or from a jar; place the broad end over the fire; position the fumigation on plums; hold it there until the fumigation is consumed; then repeat another one.
Chapter LXXIX.
Chapter on the treatment of an unperforated anus.
Many boys are born with unperforated anuses, which have been cauterized by a sharp scalpel (a surgical tool used for circumcision). The obstetrician must therefore pierce it with his finger; and if not, he should pierce it with a sharp spatula; and let him be careful not to touch the muscle.
Then place warm linen soaked in wine and oil upon it. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
If one fears it may close up again, then place a leaden tube in the opening and remove it when the child wants to be born.
And now it happens that anus closes, even from consolidation of the wound or abscess. Therefore, one must remove that consolidation, and then treat it as we have said with lead.
Chapter 80.
Chapter on the treatment of fistulas occurring in the lower part.
Fistulas that occur in the lower part are nodation and swelling that occur near the external anus; or in the space of one part; and it is a single fistula or multiple fistulas.
When that nodation has matured, it opens and watery white fluid or thin pus flows out of it.
And sometimes these fistulas penetrate. Therefore, penetrating fistulas are recognized by what comes out through defecation and wind when the sick person uses the toilet; and possibly a worm may come out of them.
And there are fistulas when they penetrate into the space as far as the bladder and as far as the root of the penis. And there are fistulas that penetrate to the junction of the hips and to the sacral node.
From this it is recognized that the penetrating fistula reaches the anus; and even if it does not penetrate, it is to introduce your index finger into the anus; and insert a probe made of copper or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
If there is a curvature in it, then insert into it a fine probe made of lead, or a hair from horse's mane, until you feel the probe, or a hair on your finger.
If you do not feel it fully nor does anything come out of the incision nor pus nor worms as I said, then you will know that it is non-penetrating; therefore approach for treatment.
And when a fistula is penetrating to the bladder or the urinary meatus, its signification is the discharge of urine from it; and the prevention of this is by the consolidation of the place with medicines.
But if it penetrates to the juncture of the hip or the hip bone, its sign is that the probe reaches there if there is no curvature up to the bone; and the finding of pain around the part, and that pus always discharges from it; and that medication does not work in it nor does the place consolidate with ointment.
And in all penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all; and the cure for them is labor and futility to one who is foolish about it.
But in the one that is non-penetrating and not old, healing is hoped for with a knife; according to what I tell you, and I have already proven it; and it is, as lying weak on your hands upon its back, and its legs lifted up above the hips of itself, and the hips are inclined towards the belly of itself. Then insert a probe made of lead or copper if there is curvature in the fistula, until you know where the probe has reached.
But if a sick person feels it around the anus, then you should insert your index finger into the anus.
If therefore you feel that a thing has already begun to penetrate your finger by itself, which you perceive to be between your finger and the flesh, then certainly you will know it is penetrating; do not then labor on it, because there is no cure for it, as we have said.
They say that the flesh heals in some people and that the remedy expected for it is to heat a thin cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been mentioned before, and then to introduce the heated cautery into the fistula until it reaches the anus. Then repeat this twice or thrice until you know that all the added flesh near the fistula, which is similar to a bird's feather pen, has been burnt away.
Then cover the burned flesh with linen strips soaked in butter until the burnt flesh comes out; then cover it with ointments that promote healing and consolidate the flesh.
If it heals, it is good.
And if not, then it will never heal with any other treatment.
If it comes out and does not reach your finger that is in the anus, and there is a thick membrane of flesh or sifac between it and the fistula; and you see that the fistula follows the skin surface which follows after; then cut the skin from the beginning of the fistula, and while cutting with the fistula, you go cutting as far as the tip of the fistula until the cutting reaches where the tip of the fistula ends, and the fistula is released and falls off.
Then clean the burnt flesh that is similar to a bird's feather pen, so that nothing remains from it.
If blood overwhelms you and it dissolves between you and your operation, so that the flesh separates; then it is better to cauterize it with fire or with a sharp medicine.
Since the cautery with fire brings good habits to it, burning of those added tissues, and the removal of blood and draining of moistness are added to it.
Then, for treatment, the linens are rolled up in butter or boiled cabbages until the place releases pus, and the burnt tissues emerge in the pus.
Then, for wound treatment with hardening ointments that cause firm flesh; there are medications consisting of styptic and drying agents.
For when it is healed, then it is cured; do not fear repetition.
If the fistula has already reached deep into the anus and it is extended from the body; then insert your finger into the anus and examine it.
If you feel a thickening between you and her, and there is a membrane from the sheep's bladder or flesh, and it is close to penetration; then there is no operation on this unless through faith and hope.
This is because a single method is administered in it: either to cauterize her as we said; or to excise it until you reach its hollow, so that it is possible for you to insert linens and cure it from the inside. And do not proceed much with the excision, so as not to cut the muscles holding the anus, and there may be an unfortunate outcome of defecation without will. Then, for treatment, do as we said.
Perhaps it will heal; or you remove the membrane itself, and clean it after cutting it up to near the anus, as we said, either with a thickening or with another sharp tool. Then, clean those tissues filtered during the excision as much as you can with examination.
Then attempt the restoration of the entire wound with a section, and at the superior part where it solidifies; and a fistula remains open in the interior part of the anus, and it will be easier on the weak.
And sometimes a fistula is drained in this manner; and it occurs when you insert a probe into the fistula, which is on the side of the anus near the body surface with skin and anus margin; then take a probe with a perforated end, which resembles an awl (aleskef), prepared from calfskin, in this shape. And insert into it a thread wound from five strands, and around that. Then insert the probe with the thread into the fistula until it reaches its hollowed part.
If the thread penetrates the internal anus margin, then pull out the thread from that hole; so that you insert your finger into the anus and pull out the end of the thread, and gather both ends together; tie each one separately and let it be for one or two days; and as much as the thread cuts into the flesh, tighten it well until the tissues between the two ends of the thread fall off and drop; then care for the wound until it solidifies and heals.
But if the fistula opening is not penetrating; then make it penetrate however you prepare it, except if it goes too deep. For you do not have the skill to do that without cutting it (the fistula).
Then do as I said until it heals.
The shape of the spatulate needle used for draining a fistula whose sharpness is very acute on one side and the other side is not acute, so as not to cut what is unnecessary, as you can see.
Head, LXXXI (81st entry)
§ On the suture of hemorrhoids from which blood flows upon their incision; and care for fissures (cracks in anus).
Piles are of two kinds. Either they are inside the anus, like bladder stones or cherries; or they are themselves like the seeds of a pomegranate. Some are small and others large; blood comes out from them always, some are single, and there are many. They are outside the anus and at its extremities.
However, those that are outside the anus are mostly dry, from which citrus juice or a little blood runs continuously; and they are in color like the body.
And the treatment for those that are inside the anus is to advise the sick man to take a laxative; and they are squeezed out, until the anus appears, and they appear to you. Therefore, hang them with hooks; or hold them with your nail. Then cut them off at their roots.
If they cannot be held in place with hooks due to their moisture and softness, then take them with rough cloth or a glove made of double wool, and remove them with your fingers. Then cut them, and sprinkle warm powders on the cuts to help stop the bleeding. Or cauterize them as described in the chapter on cauterization. Then care for them with the remaining treatment until they heal.
If the anus does not respond to emptying, then give the sick man a mild enema with which to cleanse what is in the anus, so that it will quickly obey emptying when he is squeezed.
If the piles are outside the anus, then their condition is light and easy; it is to take them with your nail or with a hook, and cut them off. Then care for them as I said, until they are healed.
And if it is necessary to avoid incision with iron, then suture them in this manner. Take a thread wrapped around, and introduce it into the point. Then bring out the hernia upwards, and make it penetrate with the point into the root on the other side: wrap two ends of the thread around the point of the needle, and let them be wide: and tie the hernia tightly with a strong stitch. Then tie the thread, and draw out the needle.
Do this with all hernias, and let one of them go free; do not sew it up, so as to avoid an excess of bleeding.
Then place a linen cloth soaked in rose oil or pitch over the anus, and put it on the anus: and tell the patient to rest. Then let him go until he faints.
When hernias fall down, care for them with ointments and the rest of the treatment, until they are healed.
Chapter on treating fissures. For they often occur due to the drying out of feces and constriction by nature.
When they become old and medicine is of no use for them: then it is necessary to shave them with a spatula or with your nail, until they become moist and the upper skin which prevents their healing is removed. Then care for them until they heal as required.
If they do not heal: then shave them more vigorously than the first time, until they bleed a lot, and after that care for them until they are healed.
Chapter on the treatment of hemorrhoids, both internal and external, and hernias and worms.
Head, LXXXII.
Know that Almirmar is not other than a round knot similar to the head of a nail: and it forms throughout the body, especially in the lower parts of the feet and fingers, and it happens that pain occurs during walking.
Therefore, it must be cut off which is around the nail head, and it should be held with forceps or with a hook, and it should be pulled out from its root.
Then care for that [area] and if you wish, cauterize it according to what was mentioned in the previous chapter.
An excrescence, however, one is a small eminence that is rough, filtered, rounded above the surface of the body. And it frequently occurs in children's hands.
Its treatment is to stretch the excrescence and cut it; or tie it with silk thread; or with hair until it falls off. And if you wish, cauterize it with fire or a sharp medicine as mentioned before; and now the excrescences that grow inward and not outward can be removed with an instrument I will mention later.
Formica is also a small, rough excrescence that is thick and projecting above the surface of the body, penetrating deeply: and when cold is found in it, it feels like a bite by an ant, and it occurs throughout the body; and it most frequently occurs in hands.
Its treatment is to take a reed from the goose's feather or strong vulture's feather; and place the reed on the Formica until it forms a circle around its parts. Then rotate your hand with the reed until it cuts what is around the Formica; and place it deep into the flesh, and remove the Formica from its root.
And if you wish, do it with an air or iron cannula in this shape.
The upper part of the cannula should be pulled up to its limit, wrapping around the deaf ear so that it may be held onto and turned (the cannula).
And if you wish to cauterize a scabies, do it as described for the cauterizing of Athil's ear in the chapter on cauteries.
Chapter LXXXIII.
Chapter on the shapes of instruments used for enemas in diseases of the anus, and for the solution of the stomach, and for colic.
When an enema is made of silver, or of gold, or of molten copper, or of beaten copper.
And sometimes it is made small, and large, according to those in which they are administered.
Therefore that which is administered for the cure of small children should be small; and for those with weak or painful anuses, so also their enemas.
Large enema.
The upper part of the cannula, that is, where it is tied to the uterus, should be wide according to this method; and there should be a distinction so that it may be tied to the uterus as you see, and the lower end which enters into the anus, should be deaf, that is, not open, soft, very fine, pulling to fineness; and in one side of its there should be two holes, and in the other side one hole.
And the size of the hole should be according to the thickness of the rays, and not too thick, and the uterus in which medicines are placed should be from an animal's bladder; or from a sheep's skin, which should be small like an ass's foot; whose root should be one palm.
And it should be perforated with many holes as it is turned, and the space between each hole should be the thickness of a finger. Then introduce into those holes a thread, preferably from a raw cord, which should be one of ten cords or about the same, and tie it up with it like an asafetida bag. When this is placed within the uterus, a clyster (enema) is to be tied off at the top with strong constriction between two distinct points. Then perform a clysterization with it.
And this is the circle shape (diagram) depicted here, and of the holes.
The quality of performing a clyster with it is: to fill the uterus or bladder with a medicine that has been heated according to the capacity of the patient's tolerance, and be careful that it is not too hot or too cold.
Then the patient lies on his back, and lifts his legs towards the top; and place beneath him a blanket, that is, leather or cloth upon which people lie.
Then anoint the end of the clyster with oil, or with white goose fat, or with slippery elm gum, or similar substances. Then introduce it (the clyster) into the anus with ease. Then let the servant take hold of the uterus with both hands and squeeze it forcefully until all that is in the clyster passes into the intestines.
Then remove the clyster and the patient lifts his legs towards the side of the bed.
If the medicine forces him to evacuate, then hold it as much as possible. And if he sleeps with it throughout the night, it is more effective in healing.
If you perform a clyster on him for diseases of the bowels and his evacuation is hastened, then repeat the clyster until he is cured.
If there are hemorrhoids or raw ulcers in the anus, then make the clyster very fine and gentle, like those used to clysterize children.
And this should be the form of a subtle suppository that is applied on tight skin.
Chapter LXXXIIII.
I have already said in the division of the treatment of wounds that it was fitting for a book, and here I will say their treatment with hand, and with medicines according to completion.
Therefore, wounds are distinguished according to the kind of injury they are and according to the place where the wound falls.
Therefore, as for the kinds of wounds, they are like the blow of a stone: either a cut by a sword or knife: or a strike with a lance, wood, or arrow: and similar to these things from many other objects.
Wounds that are made according to the parts of the body are like a wound that falls on the head, neck, chest, abdomen, or back; and similar to these members.
And I am telling the treatments of some wounds, so that I may place this reasoning and rule for the remaining wounds.
And I will begin with simple head wounds, because the reminder of compound wounds will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore. When a simple head wound occurs and there is no bone fracture, consider then if it was from a blow of a stone or similar, and only the skin has been broken, and the wound is large, and you fear impending abscess from hot suppuration: then hurry, and immediately apply a phlebotomy of the head: do not delay this: and extract as much of it as its virtue allows, if nothing prevents phlebotomy, especially if the blood that flows from the wound is scant. And let the phlebotomy be on the opposite side of the wounded part.
And let the phlebotomy be on the opposite side of the wounded part. And let the sick person avoid filling himself with food and drink, and heavy meals.
But if something prevents reduction, then let him reduce from food, and avoid meat and wine.
Place hot poultice made of cooked linseed soaked in rose oil alone, or with wine containing resin (mastic), upon the ulna if it happens to have a hot abscess.
If you are free from the hot abscess, then place upon the ulna if it is fresh with its own blood and has not changed air, later I will tell you about the powder; and if already the air has changed for it, then place some unguents on it until it heals.
If the ulna is large or from a sword cut and similar ones: and if its edges are not gathered together by blisters, then gather it with suture, as I will tell you about suturing of wounds in the abdomen.
If the ulna has already been exposed from bone and hangs without retention except for a small suspension, then cut it. Then care for the ulna with medicines and restore firm flesh to its place instead of skin, and instruct the sick man to eat foods with thickness such as heads (of animals) and cooked wheat until it is soft; and similar things.
If you find putrefaction on the skin that is not adhering to the bone, then cut out the entire putrefied part and throw it away; then care for that.
If, however, in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows and it does not separate with the medications, then seek above the artery. If you find it not cut, then cut it with a spatula or tie it. If necessity requires it and the remedies we have mentioned do not work, then cauterize (it) until the blood separates.
If these wounds are small and simple, their outcome is easy and light; therefore, apply this powder to them, as it solidifies them before the air changes.
Method for the cauterization of a tumor. Recipe one part of olibanum, two parts of dragon's blood, and three parts of unburnt lime: grind it all very well, and sieve it: fill the wound with it and apply a good pressure until it adheres well to the top, and let it coagulate with blood.
Then tie it on top with small cords, and leave it untouched until it does not separate. For the medicine will not be uprooted from him until he is healed.
And sometimes lime alone does this when there is no olibanum and dragon's blood available to you in the present. The same operation also works with many large wounds when it should be placed on them and tied, and the wounds are fresh with their own blood which has not been altered by air.
If the air has altered it in some way, especially when it is in summertime, then there is no purpose to this powder: cure it with what we have said, so that you place some digestive ointments on it or place over it poultices made from barley flour mixed with water and honey until it emits pus. Then cure the rest in the usual manner until they are healed.
If a fracture occurs with the wound in bone and it is small, then extract it with trephine (Gesti): and I will now speak about the treatment of skull fractures in the future.
On neck wounds.
If a wound occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple skull wound.
If the nerve or artery in the neck has been cut, then if it is a nerve, there is no artificice except to suspend its treatment until it recovers strength, like in case of zygias and zeges, and similar ones. Because they harm nerves, and they contract them.
And do not place anything cold directly on the wound at all: because the substance of nerves is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is above the limbs; let it be remedied with soft medicines such as lime mixed with sweet water several times infused with oil, or with rose oil, or with pitch, when it is washed even with sweet water; and other mineral stones, and unguents in this manner, and ointments that are moist.
If the wound is large, then administer suture; or the edges of it with threads and fibers. Then take care of it until it heals.
If the wound has depth or if a cavity occurs in its lower part, where already pus gathers, then pierce it more deeply at a lower location in it.
If an artery has already been cut in the wound and its blood flow is flowing out: then separate or sever it, and tie it; or cauterize it if there is a need for that.
If the trachea has already been pierced, either completely or partially, and the lungs have been saved: then gather the skin flaps with suture over the neck of the trachea, and do not touch the trachea, but sew it up, and reduce it to its natural shape. Then sew it up tightly with a suitable stitch, and let it heal for several days. Then take care of it with ointments containing styptic and astringent properties, until it heals.
If the wound has already made an impression on the bone, then probe it; if there are fragments of bone in it, extract all of them or as many as you can; and what cannot be prepared, leave it alone until the wound rots, separates, and purges its discharge.
If a wound is recent, then sprinkle powder upon it, as I have told. If it appears that bone is visible in the wound, and a fistula forms: then treat it with the method described in its respective chapter.
Chapter on Wounds Treated with Spatulas.
If it is a wound from a lance or knife, and its depth can be seen, then examine it. If a windy discharge comes from the wound when someone who is sick is breathing heavily, then you know that the wound is fatal.
If the depth is not apparent, and it is a recent wound with its own blood, then do not apply powder to it from the first hour, nor press it so that the blood does not remain in its depth and return to the heart and kill the sick person: instead, put on it an attracting ointment, and dissolve it twice a day.
If the ointment is not available to you, then put in the opening of the wound an old piece of cotton, so that it absorbs what comes out from it due to moistness: and make the sick person sleep on the wound, so that it heals as it accumulates in it.
If already three days or more have passed since the wound occurred, and no spasm occurs in the sick person, nor a bad heart tremor, nor a narrowing of breathing, and you see good indications of recovery: then know that the wound is well. Treat it with linen cloths, and the rest of the treatment, until it heals.
If healing does not occur, and it always opens up, then know that a fistula has formed. Treat it from its respective chapter.
If the wound is from an incision by a sword or knife, and it is simple on the surface of the chest or back, then treat it with that which came before in stitching, if it is large: or with powder, if it is small.
If however he has already made an impression on the bone and cut off fragments from it: then examine the wound, and hasten to extract those fragments, if they are separate. If however they are not separated, then leave them alone until the wound rots, for the extraction of them will be easier when it has rotted.
As for other wounds on other members, the judgement in their cure is the same as we said.
Chapter on Wounds of the Abdomen, and the Exit of the Intestines, and Their Removal.
Rupture which happens in the abdomen is great, middle, or small.
Therefore from a great rupture sometimes the intestine or number of intestines comes out.
Thus it requires insertion [of them], and their suture is more violent and difficult.
And a small rupture also occurs in another way [difficultly]. Therefore it will be more difficult to reduce [them] if you do not hurry in inserting them to their place immediately: because it swells, opens, and becomes enlarged; therefore the entrance is made difficult.
For this reason it is better to make a middle rupture because the reduction of the intestine is not difficult with it, as it is in these two cases [great and small ruptures].
Know that the suture of the abdomen is according to four modes.
Two common sutures come together in the suture of the abdomen and in the suture of other wounds of the body; and two other sutures communicate with the remaining wounds. However, they are more proper to the suture of the abdomen; and I tell you one by one with their explanation and declaration.
Therefore I say that if the wound is small and something from the intestine comes out of it and it is difficult to reduce it, then it is according to one of two modes. Because of the smallness of the rupture, as we said; Or because there is an inflation in the intestine due to the cold of air.
When therefore that is so, then it is necessary that you heat it, so that you immerse a sponge or wet cloth in warm water alone. Or boil in water squill, cyperus, cumin, and wormwood with it, until the inflation is resolved.
Sometimes it does that wine in which there is stipulation; and it is better than water alone in the resolution of inflation.
When therefore you see that the inflation is already resolved, then moisten the intestine with water in which artemisia has been boiled, or with wormwood. For by this it is healed the entrance of it with a small opening.
If however there is an extrusion of it after this treatment, then sew up the rupture with a little, with the instrument with which hemorrhoids are cut.
And the first treatment is better when it is prepared, than cutting; and it is not forced to cut after necessity and lack of instruments.
Let one part of it be twisted, sharp, and another part not sharp; and the end should not be subtle with the subtlety of a needle, but rather slightly blunt; and that resembles a sheath, as you see.
When therefore the wound is enlarged and enters the intestine, then it is necessary that the return of it should be according to its natural form in its proper place, if possible above it; because it is better.
When however the rupture is large in the lower part of the abdomen; then it is necessary that you make the sick person lie on his back and place his legs higher than his head. And if it is in the upper part of the abdomen; then place his head and chest higher than his lower parts.
And similarly, if there is a rupture in one of two parts of the stomach, then place your intention and always consider this: that the part containing the wound should be higher than the other part.
And it must be done for large wounds and medium-sized wounds.
For small wounds, do that which is prepared for you.
Then make it so that a faithful servant, who will hold the rupture with his whole hand, is present among your hands. And gather his lips. Then take something for the one who follows to sew with, a little after a little. And this is the common method of suturing one.
It is that you should take a needle or a number of needles according to the size of the wound. Then release from the end of the rupture the width of a finger ring, that is, of the doctor. And sew the needle one over what you insert the thread into it at both ends of the skin, as well as both ends of the sifac which is beneath the skin from the inside, until you make it penetrate from the other side. And you have already gathered the two ends of the skin, and the two ends of the sifac. And there are four rows.
Then sew with double thread around the needle several times from both parts at once, until the two lips of the wound are gathered together with proper closure.
Then release the thickness of a finger and sew another needle into it. Afterwards draw it straight with thread, as you did with the first needle. Therefore do not cease to do that with the one you need from the needles until you complete the closure of the entire wound.
And let the needles be of medium thickness between coarseness and fineness because fine needles deeply cut the flesh, and coarse ones are difficult to enter the skin. Therefore it is necessary for them to be of medium thickness in both fineness and coarseness.
It is not proper that the needle be fashioned in two extremities of the skin closely joined: so that the flesh is not cut quickly, and the wound is opened before its consolidation, and even when sutured, they should not be stretched out, so that the wound is prevented from consolidating.
Then cut the end of the needle, so that it does not harm the weak person during sleep; and place threads from cloth all around, which hold the ends of the needle; and leave them until you know that the wound is already consolidated.
And this kind of sewing with needles in this manner is more appropriate for small wounds. Because one or two needles, or about that number, are sufficient for their sewing (i.e., the stitches).
The second common sewing is when you gather with the stitching the edges of four: the edges of two skins and the edges of two sifac in place of one, with the needle containing the thread wound evenly in fineness and coarseness.
Then, when you penetrate with the needle these four edges, pull back the needle from the side where you started, so that the thread fixed above the wound falls out: so that the stitching is like the sewing of cloth where the cloth is sewn together, and place between every stitch a quantity equal to the thickness of a little finger.
This kind of stitching is known by men.
And with this stitching I sewed my own wound that happened to me in the belly of a man who had been wounded with a knife, and the wound was larger than one palm; and about two palms had come out from the intestines from the middle intestine, and the tear was in the middle of the belly.
I therefore brought it back after his intestines had remained outside the wound for twenty-four hours.
The wound has been consolidated about fifteen days hence: and I healed it, and it became healthy: and he lived for many years afterwards, having returned to his accustomed ways.
And the physicians had judged that it would not heal.
And it was a miracle that I did not heal it with ointment. Because I was in a place where no ointment could be found nor any medicine. Therefore I placed hot mustard on the wound twice a day, and attended to its cleaning with water and honey until it healed.
I shall now describe two types of stitches according to the story's account.
And it begins with a sharp stitch: and you insert the needle from outside to inside.
When the needle penetrates the skin and follows the length and breadth of the entire body: release the tip at the side where you inserted the needle, and let it pierce another end from the inside to outside at the opposite extreme.
And when you have made it penetrate, then let it pierce again in the same side from outside to inside: and release the tip where you released it before, and let the needle pierce another end from the inside to outside at the opposite extreme: and let it pierce together with your previous penetration, until it reaches the entire thing.
Then begin again from this same side, and take out the stitch with its opposite end, which is on the other side of the skin that it penetrated.
Then bring it back into the skin and take out its opposite end with this end: and take out from the skin the end that was on the other side of it, and do so alternately until you have extracted the entire stitch according to this example.
The final stitch of this suture is to sew together the skin layers in such a way that one side of one end of the skin is sewn with one stitch; and to leave the other side with the other end, until it is complete.
The second type of suture mentioned by Galen.
This discourse was narrated to be similar to the way some physicians perform it, as they gather all parts that are naturally connected and bring together their corresponding ends; and apply one end to the other's corresponding end, and the edge (mirach) of one to the other's edge. And this is done as I told you.
You should make an incision at the edge (mirach) near you from the outer part, and make it penetrate to the interior only; and leave the two ends of the skin. Then turn the incision, and make it penetrate from the outer part to the interior through both ends of the skin, on either side.
Then turn both and make both penetrate from the inner part to the outer through two edges on the opposite side.
And this method of suture is better than the common easy one, and it is the suture of which the previous mention has been made.
Therefore, this is also a discourse by Galen.
And some have said. The abdominal suture is repaired with two incisions (acubus). To insert one thread into each of them: and begin with the incision of the needle, from what is near you, and make it penetrate to the other side, following the suture of those who are equal in thickness (coria).
And know that when a rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, then the suture of this place is more difficult than that of other parts of the abdomen.
The judgment of medication for a wound is the judgment of other wounds.
When you have a new wound with its blood, before it changes due to air: and you reduce the intestine, and clean it, and prepare it: then place it on a powder of meat.
If the air has already changed the wound: then place on it certain ointments that you have present, so that it produces pus: and let them fall off, and be bound up with lint and myrrh. Then care for it as the care for other wounds, until it heals.
If there are no medications present for you, then immediately place on it a hot, old cloth that begins to emit pus: and change it twice a day as I have taught you, until it heals.
For you do not need other medications when the wounds are simple.
If you fear that the wound may communicate with the principal members in injury, then it is necessary that you immerse a soft wool in oil of moderate heat or rose oil: and place it in the surrounding areas which are between the groin and under the armpits.
If it feels pain or punctures or putrefaction in the intestines (for this often occurs): then cleansing of the bowels with wine of soap, black and warm: especially if putrefaction has already reached the intestine and become a discharge penetrating to its hollow.
And know that what is from the large intestine is easier to heal: and what is from the small ones, harder to heal.
The intestine called Jejunum does not accept healing from a wound that occurs in it at all: and this is because of its large number, which is from veins, and the size of them, and because of the subtlety of its body, and because of the proximity of its nature to nerves.
If however what proceeds from the wound is a bone splinter, and you grasp it freshly, reduce it according to your reduction method of equalizing intestines.
If it has passed beyond (the wound), and has become green or black, then you must tie it with a thread above the site where it has become darkened, to prevent bleeding. For there are veins and arteries in bonesplinters.
Then cut the ligament beyond it, and place two ends of the thread hanging from below the wound on its outer side: to facilitate the pulling away from you of its attraction, and extraction of the bonesplinter at the site of the splintered bone, and draining of pus from the wound.
Memory of a wound that occurs in the Intestine.
When there is a rupture in the intestine and it is small, it can be restored in some people: therefore, because I have seen someone who was wounded in his abdomen by a lance strike, and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound was old, and it became a fistula, and pus and gas escaped from it.
I therefore administered treatment until I was not confident in his healing; neither did I cease to refine it until he was healed and the site consolidated.
After I saw the site already consolidated, I feared for the sick man that an accidental evil might occur in his abdomen; and no accidental evil occurred to him from it. And he remained in better conditions for himself, eating and drinking, and defecating, and entering the bath, and exercising in his own diets.
And some of the experiencers said that when a wound occurs in the intestine and it is small, then it must be tied according to this method. And it is, to receive ants with large heads. Then gather two lips of the wound and place one ant with an open mouth upon the two lips of the wound. When its head is on them, and it closes its mouth, cut off its head; for it clings and cannot be detached.
Then place another ant near the first one, and do not cease until the ant, after the second, is equal to the entire size of the wound.
Then reduce it and let the wound heal. For these heads remain attached to the intestine until the intestine is fed, and it heals, so that no harm comes to the sick person completely.
And now it is possible that the intestine may be tied even with a fine thread: what has been removed from the animal's intestine remains attached to it after it is introduced into the point.
And it is, to receive the end of this thread from the intestine and let much flesh be cut away. Then tie a fine thread at its end. Then introduce the thread into the point and let the intestine come out with it. Then reduce it to separation.
This method of sewing with ants and the intestine is not excepted except by way of trust and hope.
Know that a large wound, wide, especially if it is on one of the thin intestines: then there is no artifice except subtlety, and there is no healing at all.
Chapter on Wounds and Fistulas.
Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes old and decayed, and turns into an ulcer, and does not consolidate, and always emits pus, and cannot be cut off: then it is called universally in whatever member it may be a Fistula, and we call it a Zuchimen.
A fistula, in truth, is a hard, white knot; one without pain, having the hollow shape of a bird's feather; and on account of this some call it Risatus, that is, feather.
In some hours it [the fistula] becomes wet, emitting pus. Perhaps moisture is divided at some hours. And at times this moisture is much and at times little; and it is thick and at times thin.
I have already stated in the division [that] every ulcer that does not heal nor is born from it flesh, is not this but due to one of nine causes.
One of these [causes] is when the amount of blood in the body is too little or it is malicious; or because there is hard flesh between it and its lips preventing the growth of flesh; or because there are many sores and putrefaction; or because the ulcer itself is rotten, and the matter that is emitted from it is of bad quality; or because the medicine is inappropriate for healing it; or because corruption falling in the region is a kind of pestilence, as happens in Caesaraugusta, where digestion of illnesses becomes difficult, and recovery from boils by nature is slow; or because there is one bone, or a number of bones [present].
And I have shown all these causes and their signs, as well as the treatments of them with medicines in the division; now here it is necessary that I tell you the cure for a fistula and a boil, which is performed by the way of an operation using hand.
Therefore, know that a fistula occurs in all members of the body. For there are fistulas that reach to large veins and arteries, nerves or tendons; or intestines, bladder, or one of the ribs; or spinal bones, or some of the joints composed in composition, such as hands and feet; and there are those that approach the proximity of a principal member or similar.
