This fistula, according to this method, is one of difficult healing, and it does not admit treatment, and attending to it is labor and ignorance.
If any fistula has a depth that does not reach the places I mentioned and you hope for its cure, trust in it, and wish to attain knowledge of it, then take a probe made of copper or iron, if the fistula follows a straight course, and examine it along with itself.
If there is a twist in the fistula, then investigate it with a slender lead probe. Since lead, because of its softness and curvature, adheres to twists.
If the fistula has many openings, it is not possible for you to sign it with a probe. Seal therefore the opening from among its openings.
Because moisture, which you seal it with, flows towards other openings and runs out of them.
Then examine and investigate carefully according to the method that is possible for you: so that you may know whether there is a bone or nerve there, and whether the fistula has a deep depression or a shallow one; or whether it is a single fistula with many openings, and stands over the whole thing, with all your strength, through questioning the sick person, by inquiring about pain when pressure is applied to the place, and similar signs and causes of bleeding.
When you have therefore firmly stood over all these matters, then go to treatment according to confidence; and it is necessary for you to consider at this time whether the fistula is near, appearing in a safe place far from a joint, a nerve, an artery, or vein, or in one of the places I mentioned to you; then cut the fistula as stated before in my narration, remove what is in it from filtering and decayed flesh that arises in its opening from flesh or ulcer, and similar things, and treat it until it heals.
If a Fistula is of great depth and straight, then it is necessary to cut it deeply as much as possible for you. Then clean it thoroughly from all the corrupted flesh of it.
Then administer a linen cloth wrapped in sharp medicines and insert it into the concavity of the fistula as far as you have grasped with iron, do this repeatedly until the sharp medicine corrodes all that remains in the concavity of the fistula due to decay.
Then restore it with ointments that produce healthy flesh until it heals.
If it does not heal through this, then cauterize it as we have said before.
If the cause of the fistula is a bone, and you are certain about this, then investigate it and cut it out as I have told you; if it does not forbid you anything from the vein or nerve or principal member, as we have said.
If a bone is discovered and there is some decay and blackness within it, then scrape it until all the decay is removed. Then treat it with that which causes it to heal, until it heals.
If it does not heal and discharges pus as it did; then you will know that you have not reached the complete removal of the decay.
Investigate it again above and find out its reason and thoroughly clean it with your utmost strength.
Then restore it. If it heals, that is good; if not, then you will know that the decay is in a deep and distant part of the body which you have not reached. You are therefore not skilled enough for it except to let nature take its course.
If the bone is small and decayed and if it is possible for you, pull it out with fine forceps suitable for that.
If there are many bones, then carefully make an attempt to draw them all out, without leaving anything within them with your strength.
If something from the moistures opposes you, and there is no fear or mistake in the incision: then cut those moistures and flesh, if they are there, and free the bones.
If there is no preparation to remove the bones from your time, then place something above the wound that decomposes it; and leave it until it decomposes, what is within the circumference of those bones from the flesh and moistures.
And keep the wound so that it does not harden. Tie the incision that you made during your operation. Or place on it, if you are afraid, a piece of cotton soaked in ground sulfur mixed with oil; or a piece of cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, or some green ointments.
For when those moistures have decomposed, and the bones separate from them, clean away their removal, and their drawing out.
If there is a large bone, such as the thigh bone, hip bone, and similar ones, and what has been corrupted from it is a large part: then grind it with a fine rasp, until that blackness and corruption is removed. Then restore the wound.
If what is in it has become a large part and the corruption has already reached the marrow of the bone, then it is necessary to saw it, and cut it completely until the place where the corruption has reached; then take care of it until it hardens.
And I tell you of a case that happened to a man in his leg; so that you place it as an example and assistance for your operation.
There was a young man about 30 years old, who had pain in his leg, caused by something that moved upon him inside the body, that is, from within; until matter reached the calf, and there was an abscess made: and it was not an external cause.
The incision was made at the same time as the error of the physicians, until the abscess was opened, and many substances converged with it. The treatment was delayed until the leg had become fistulous, and many openings were made therein: all of which discharged pus, and bodily moisture.
Therefore, a multitude of physicians treated him for approximately two years, and there was no skilled surgeon's hand present until I was summoned, and I saw his leg, and the substances that were flowing from those openings with a great course: even the whole body of the man was already stiffened, and his color had become yellow.
I inserted a probe into one of the openings, and it reached the bone.
Then I examined all the openings: and found that they were flowing into each other from all parts of the leg.
I approached and cut through one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone: and I found it decayed: which was already rotten, blackened, putrefied, and pierced through until it had reached the marrow.
Then I sawed what was exposed to me, and prepared it from the rotten bone.
And assigned that there was no bone other than that decay which I cut off and sawed away. And now I had removed it.
Then I placed a dressing on the wound with strengthening medications for a considerable distance. It is not healed.
Then I probed and exposed the bone a second time above the first exposure, and found continuous decay with the bone: and I sawed away that which appeared to me from this decay as well.
And then I attempted a dressing for it. It is not restored.
I therefore examined it again, and did not cease to cut the bone piece by piece, and attempted its restoration; it was not restored, until I cut a bone about the size of a palm and extracted that with its marrow.
Then I healed it with medicines and it was quickly consolidated and cured; this repetition in the operation and section of it was not necessary, except due to the disposition of the patient's weakness, his small tolerance, and my fear for him concerning death; since he suffered in all hours from mal-syncopes due to excessive evacuation.
Therefore it was cured completely with healing; and new flesh hard was born at the place of the bone, and a good arrangement was made in his body, and his strength returned; and he turned back to his dispositions; and he did not suffer any harm at all from walking contrary to it.
If the protruding bone at a place of the body is already broken: then it is necessary that you tie it in this way: and it is as follows: take a ligament, and tighten it at the end of the protruding bone; and command someone to stretch it upward; and place another thicker ligament on the first one. Then tie it over the flesh that is next to the bone; and extend its end so that you draw the flesh downward; and you loosen the flesh above the place which you want to cut, so that the saw does not harm the flesh.
Place a stick or board underneath the bone below properly; because when you do this, it is not forbidden to cut the corrupted flesh.
And it is necessary that there be a saw above the corrupted place somewhat, so that the corruption is not in the hollow of the bone; and it does not appear to the sense in its appearance, and force another to saw on its behalf.
If the bone is corrupted and is not projecting, but rather it is continuous with a part of it: and the corruption is in the middle of it, or in one of its parts: then excise all the flesh from every part. Place the splint beneath.
Cut the affected part with a saw from that side where there is corruption, until the other saw-cut meets it. And make the saw-cuts according to our earlier instructions in length slightly beyond the corruption.
If the corruption is at a joint, cut through the affected joint and saw the bone where it joins from another side.
But if the corruption is at a place of two joints' connection, then it is not a fracture, but rather an abrasion.
If the corruption is at the tip of the hand or foot: then there is a very difficult matter in it. It is necessary to investigate how the corruption appears to you. And abrade it, and clean it as much as possible for you, and rectify it with whatever skill is available to you: when it does not contradict the Vein or Nerve.
And know that these saws and cutting knives for cutting the bones are many, according to the position of the bones, their preparation, their coarseness or fineness, their size, and their thickness, and their hardness or softness, and their rarity. Therefore, it is necessary to prepare every type of surgical instrument suitable for that particular operation.
And know that these operations require from you a type of instrument that suits the case when you have long-term interest. And knowledge of the methods of this art is a sign of the nature of the diseases: then you will find for yourself what suits it among the instruments for every disease.
And I confirm to you at the end of this chapter's number of instruments, which you shall place examples upon that you cut into, and a proof by which you test on other things.

On making incisions in limbs, and the suturing of bones.
Limbs rot due to either external or internal causes.
If the corruption has been treated with medicines and the treatment does not help, and you see that corruption has spread to a limb without affecting anything else, then it is necessary to make an incision in that limb as far as where the corruption stops, so that the weak one may pass away through that or escape from the greater evil which is the loss of a member.
The sign that occurs is what becomes blackened until it is considered denigrated: what fire has burnt it or what rots after the blackness; until that rottenness reaches to that which follows the affected member and spreads throughout the entire body.
Approach therefore with the incision of that [affected part], and similarly if the cause of corruption is due to the strike of certain venomous creatures such as the marine scorpion, viper, weasel, and similar ones.
If therefore the corruption or strike occurs at the end of the finger, then cut off the finger, and leave no space for the corruption to spread, so that it does not extend to the rest of the hand.
And similarly if it occurs in the hand, then cut it off from the root of the wrist, and leave no space for the corruption to spread, until it reaches the arm.
And if it penetrates into him [the patient], then cut off the arm at the elbow joint.
If the corruption passes through and you see him about the elbow: then death is present for the sick man. And beyond that in treatment, it is a question of quantity, not quality [of the medicine].
And similarly do so with the foot, when corruption penetrates into a toe; then cut it off at one of the joints; and if it reaches to the ball of the foot, then cut off the entire foot. If it rises to the knee, then cut off the leg at the knee joint.
If the corruption has already reached above the knee, then there is no cure for it except to release [the limb] and leave the sick man to death.
And the method of cutting a limb or sewing it is to tighten the lower ligament that you wish to cut and tighten another ligament above the place [of the wound]. And extend one of the ministers [assistants] to below; and extend the other minister upwards towards the top [of the limb]. Separate the flesh that is between two ligaments, with a broad spatula, until all the flesh is exposed. Then it should be cut or tied up.
It is necessary to place a linen cloth on all parts and not touch the healthy area with the knife; and harm the weak by adding injury and apply a hot poultice (to the wound).
If there is internal bleeding while you work, then quickly cauterize the place or put some powders that absorb blood on top of it. Then return to your treatment until it is complete.
Then bind the wounded member with a suitable ligament and care for it until it heals.
And I tell you what happened to a man on his foot, the same thing happening as I told you.
It is that a blackening occurs on his foot, similar to charring from fire, and the corruption first affects his toe, until it begins to affect the entire foot.
Therefore the man went away from himself, when he saw the corruption spreading in his limb with such intensity, which he discovered by pain and charring; and he cut it off at the joint, and he was healed.
And after a long time had passed, the same corruption occurred in the index finger of his other hand.
Therefore he came to me and I tried to recover the missing tissue by placing medicines on his hand after cleansing his body; but the tissue was not restored, and it began to affect another finger; until corruption started in his entire hand.
He therefore called for me to cut off his hand; but I refused, hoping that the tissue would be restored by me; and I was also afraid of death at the cutting of his hand. A man's virtue was above his misfortune.
When he had given up hope on me, he returned to his own land; and he came to me concerning him, because he hastened, and fell all over his hand: and he was healed.
I have brought this account not except for the help on that which falls under this kind of sickness; and to signify what it indicates, and according to how it is treated.
Treatise on the cure of the nose, and the quality of cleansing with medications.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy members, and the space of the abscess is prolonged until it makes a collection of pus: then it bursts or perforates, and what is in the pus comes out and leaves a place vacant as if it were a vessel; and the skin that is above it becomes like a cloth that has been worn thin; and it does not reach its ultimate corruption, nor does it press on bone, nerve, or ligament: it deserves to be called a Sinus; and it is not called a Fistula; however, if the space of it is prolonged until corruption presses on one of these members, then it is called a Fistula, or a zuken.
And the care of it is, that you cut that skin all over, as it is rolled up; and especially when it has become thin, and made like a cloth; and trust that it will not adhere to the place, due to its own corruption.
If you hope that the skin will adhere, and it does not follow from this that the ultimate corruption occurs; and if there is thickening of the skin from flesh, then treat it with Clisterium; and it is to be considered as a Sinus.
Then if it is large, and the pus that comes from it has a foul smell; then clisterize it with an Egyptian medication, which is vinegar, oil, and zeniar, taking equal parts, put together in a vessel: and cook it over fire, until the medicine turns red; and let it come to the thickness of honey.
Then take from it what you need and dissolve it with water and honey, and cleanse the sinus with it, and close its opening, and leave the medicine within it for two hours quantity.
Then squeeze it out with pressure: make this for days until the sinus is cleansed and the stench is removed.
And sometimes it is cleansed with water of ashes, when this medicine is not at hand for you: and there is, to receive the ash from vinewood, or ash from holly trees, and pour water over it. Then boil it, and cleanse with it until you are confident that the sinus is now cleansed.
If the sick person cannot bear the Egyptian medicine nor water of ashes, then cleanse it with water and honey, which is already mixed with something from crushed pomegranate rind. Or cleanse it with honey and wine mixed together, because by the nature of honey it cleanses and washes, and wine makes the sinus adhere, especially when there is an excess of dryness and thirst in the wine.
When you have done this many times and are confident that the corruption of the sinus is now removed, then cleanse it with what causes flesh to grow within it.
And there is to receive dyafinicon from a plaster, and dissolve it with rose oil and stiptic wine, or cleanse it with certain medicines and other unguents whose properties I have written in the treatise on unguents.
If the opening of the sinus is narrow and a cannula cannot enter for cleansing, then dilate it slightly with iron, or place linen wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment within it until it expands.
And similarly, if there is also a wide opening, then gather its lips with suture: and release from it the quantity to which the clyster may enter without addition.
And similarly, if there is an opening from which pus flows, it should be elevated to the upper part: then cut it in a lower place that is within it, so that pus may run out from below; because when pus is constricted in depth, it prevents flesh from generating in it.
If it is not possible for you to cut the sinus around below as you wish, then try to prepare the member with a preparation by which pus may run out from it easily according to how it is prepared for you. Try not to retain anything from the pus at all; and take healing medicines which are placed on the mark, suitable for what you wish. And spread them over a linen cloth. And let the cloth be of such size that the entire sinus may communicate through it. Then cut with scissors directly in the opening of the sinus a hole wider than the opening of the sinus itself. Then spread from soft ointments over another cloth according to the size of the hole; and place it on top with a distant position from the opening of the sinus, so that the flow of pus may be relieved; and do not remove the large cloth except after some days as if once.
He who is on the opening of the sinus, is he whom you remove at any hour, so that what accumulates in it from pus may come out; and know that, whether what flows from it is much or little, or digested, or undigested.
And with this again consider the place of the sinus itself, whether its owner feels pain there, or not there is pain there, and if there is an abscess there, or not an abscess there.
When therefore your medication is thus extended, and you see the material that comes out of the sinus opening, then you know that the sinus has already adhered or is approaching adhesion: then, therefore, dissolve it in the morning or on the third day; and when you cut the wound, then change the bandage and renew the ointment.
If for a long time there comes out from the sinus subtle pus, then do not despair of its adhesion, for its healing is approaching, since among men there are those who delay the generation of flesh in their wounds and there are those who act contrary to this.
If for many days there comes out from the sinus undigested pus, then you know that the sinus does not adhere.
If, therefore, the adhesion of the sinus is delayed and prolonged, then in its treatment add drying medicaments; but let the physicians do so that the medicines are moist in their substance and dry in their virtue, such as unguentum dyafinicon, when added to it, superfluous addition from zeugion.
And from the most remote one that is treated, it is that you receive unguentum dyafinicon, and let it be dissolved with rose oil, and let it be sprinkled on top of it ancient wine equal in substance.
Then mix it with this and use it.
And now perform an action similar to this when you do not have unguentum dyafinicon on hand, honey, when you boil it until it thickens and use it. Or take myrrh, aloe, and olibanum; grind everything together and powderize it on top of honey while it is over the fire. Then lay a linen cloth over it and stitch it over the sinus; and line with honey that you have boiled until it thickens, powderize the species on top of it and put it over the linen cloth, and stitch it up.
And sometimes it is administered to him (the patient) long aconite (Aristolochia), and the roots of celestial lily (Lilium candrum), and there is linum (flax); and wheat flour, and chicory. Use these simple remedies, or compound them, grind them well and sift the powder; and sprinkle over the honey as I have said, and use it.
If the condition of the sinus continues and is not cured by this treatment, then you should know that there is corruption deep within it; or it has already affected the bones, or other hard parts of the body, or ligaments; then treat it with fistula treatment, as mentioned before.
Chapter on the cure for corns (calluses), scraping the nails, and cutting the finger; and incision.
Corn (callus) is an abscess that arises under the nail of the thumb or big toe; and perhaps it arises in other fingers.
When the condition persists without treatment and it becomes an abscess, it is heated with a hot abscess; or it is corrupted and emits pus until it corrodes the root of the nail; and perhaps it corrodes it completely, and perhaps corruption reaches the bone, so that there is a foul odor; and the end of the finger becomes wide, and its color becomes dark.
When you treat it with the method mentioned, and your treatment does not help; then you should make an incision with a knife of the entire excess that remains from the nail. Then cauterize the wound after that. For cautionery is very helpful.
If the bone is healthy and the nail is also healthy, and empty additions under the nail are pressing the flesh towards the inside, and begin to pierce it, and hurt it; then you should place refined radium at the corner of the nail that pierces the flesh, and push it up; and cut the flesh with ease, and put on top of it what remains of the flesh from medicines for burning, corrosive, until all of it is removed. Then treat it with ointments until it heals.
If however a corruption has already pressed into the bone, then it is necessary to cut that bone and remove it; for a corrupted bone never heals while it remains in it.
If you see a corruption and a decay advancing on the finger, then cut it off at one joint, according to what has been previously remembered about it. Then treat it, until it heals.
If however the nail is rubbed or hit and there is a very strong pain, then it is necessary to bleed the weak first with leeches. Then cut off the nail with a sharp Spathamel scissors from top to bottom according to sight.
And take care that the cutting does not reach the flesh which is under the nail, for by this you will cause a very strong pain to arise over the weak place, and it will be the cause of a new growth of flesh at that location.
Then treat the place with it in order to alleviate the pains.
A finger that is added to some human hands may perhaps be completely fleshy; and it may perhaps have bones in some of them, and there may perhaps be a nail on it; and sometimes it arises from the root of the joint, or its origin is at some nodes of the finger. Therefore that which arises at some nodes of the finger does not move; and that which arises near the joint of the finger perhaps moves.
Therefore the cutting of that which is fleshy from them is easy. The purpose is to cut it near its root with a broad Spathamel.
But the treatment of that which has its origin at the root of the joint is difficult. Therefore refrain from cutting it.
In that case where a person is born on a digit at the end of the joints, then it is necessary to cut his flesh first with round incision until the bone. Then saw the bone with one of those saws suitable for that purpose. Then care for it until it heals.
Consolidations that happen to the fingers often occur either by birth, that is, born with it, or from consolidation of wounds, burns from fire, and similar conditions.
Therefore, it is necessary to cut off that consolidation until the fingers return to their natural shape. Then place linen or cloth soaked in pink oil between them to prevent consolidation quickly and separate them; or place thin lead sheets between them until the area is healed as required.
Similarly, if consolidation occurs in some fingers with the palm, then cut off that consolidation according to what is prepared and suitable for the limb's shape.
[Paragraph on Incision Error]
Worms are involved veins that are coiled, thick, filled with excessive melancholic substances which often occur in various parts of the body; and most frequently they occur in the legs, especially in those walking or laboring and carrying loads.
Therefore, it is necessary to administer purges for black bile often by strong purging.
Then let the patient's vein be punctured in the basilic vein.
The treatment for them with iron is according to two methods. One of these methods is to cut and draw out black blood. The other method is to open the vein and draw out everything entirely.
The cutting (operation) of it is according to this method. Bruise the leg first with much warm water until thick and foul blood is resolved. Then bind the ill leg from its upper thigh to its lower leg with plaster. Then cut one, or two, or three wide veins.
Then draw blood from the lower part of the leg up to the top and it is necessary that the leech should be used on the patient first. Then cut a nail if it is necessary; take out as much blood from the blood as you see sufficient and as strong as the patient can tolerate.
Then tie it up (the wound); and command him to abstain from foods that produce black bile; and repeat the evacuation and leeching when the veins are full, and this harms the patient.
The method of leeching is as follows. Shave the ill leg if there are many hairs on it. Then immerse it (the leg) in a bath; or apply warm water to the limb with a linen cloth until it turns red and the veins swell; or exercise it vigorously if no bath is present for him, until the limb becomes warm.
Then make a straight cut along the vein: or at the end of it near the knee, or at the lower part of it near the heel.
Then open the skin with a knife, and scrape the vein from all sides until it appears to sensation; and at the appearance of this, you see it turn from redness to blackness. When it has reached the flesh (vein), you see it as white like a cord.
Then insert a probe under it (the white vein) until it is drained and comes out of the flesh; hold it with a blunt probe.
Then cut another incision near that incision with three fingers. Then scrape the skin from the upper part of the vein until it appears. Then remove it with tweezers as you did before, and hang it up with another hook, as you did at first.
Then make another cut, or several cuts if necessary. Then remove, and cut the last part of the incision near the heel.
Then draw out that part which is above it [the incised piece].
And do that until you draw it out from the higher incision or all incisions, until it comes out completely; then cut it.
If it does not obey you when drawing and removing: then introduce a pointed needle with a strong thread and tie it, and draw it out; or insert a rod under it; and turn your hand over all parts until it comes out. And be careful not to cut [the vein]. For if it is cut, it will be very difficult for you to remove it, and harm may come upon the patient from it.
When you have drawn it out entirely: then put linen soaked in wine and rose oil, or olive oil, over the wound; and care for it until it heals.
If the vein is twisted and contracted with a coil-like turn, not as we have said in straightness: then you must cut it open over all parts of its twisting, and the points of its coiling.
Then hang it up with hooks until you remove it entirely; and be careful at your cut not to cut the vein or wound; for it will be difficult for you to remove or extract it. Therefore, exercise caution.
Method for treating a Wound.
Method for treating a Blind Pouch (or Cyst).
There is no inflammation in this Blind Pouch (or Cyst) as there is in other ones, nor is it pointed, so as not to wound the vein; and it is of a thick, wavy nature, soft: for if it were subtle, it would pierce the vein with its subtlety; indeed, excess thickness should be present, as we have said.
On the Extraction of the Vein in the Leg.
This Vein is generated in the legs in hot lands, as Alizegi says, and in Arabian lands, and in dry, hot lands of little softness, that is, where no herb or tree grows.
And perhaps it is generated in other parts of the body besides the legs.
Indeed, its generation is due to corruption that occurs beneath the skin, such as occurs inside the bodies of snakes and roundworms (ascarids) and worms generated between the skin and flesh.
And the sign of the onset of this Vein is that which occurs when there is a violent inflammation in the leg. Then the area is opened (or incised). Then the Vein begins to come out from that incision, as if it were the root of a plant or an animal.
When its end appears from there, then it is necessary to wind around it a piece of lead weighing one keil dram (273.3 grams), up to two drams and a knot; and let the lead hang down from the leg.
Every time something comes out of it to the exterior, wind that up in lead and knot it. If it becomes very long, then cut off a part of it, and wind the rest. Do not cut it rootwise before it comes out completely. If you cut [the tooth], it contracts, and enters the flesh; and it causes an abscess to occur, and corruption in the place, and a bad ulcer.
Therefore it is necessary that it be treated gently, and drawn out gradually, until it comes out entirely, and nothing remains of it in the body; and from this vein there comes forth in some men what is in its length five fingers and ten. And now it has come to me, because a man came out of twenty palms.
If it is cut [the tooth] to you at the hour of your treatment; then insert a rod into its hole, and pierce it through with a long hole, together with the body, until all that is in it from matter is evacuated out; and administer the corruption of the place with medicines for several days. Then care for it with treatment for abscesses.
And this vein sometimes has many branches, especially when it appears at the joint of the foot, or in the foot itself; and it occurs with many openings, and a branch comes out from every opening.
Care for it, therefore, as we have said in the division, and with what was mentioned before.
Chapter on the section of worms generated under the skin, and it is called Bouina sickness.
This sickness is called Bouina among us; because it often occurs to cows, and there is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh.
It travels throughout the body, going up and down; it is detected by sense during its movement from limb to limb, until it bursts wherever it bursts on the skin, and comes out.
And its generation is from corruption of certain humors. As worms and snakes, that is, earthworms and roundworms occur in the abdomen.
And it is feared from its mischief. Because when it is present in the body and raised to the head and reaches that place; then perhaps it opens there, and comes out, and destroys the eye; and this happens often.
Since it is to cure him and extract it, this can be done only during his wandering and its appearance to the sense.
Therefore, one must tie that which is above it, and that which is below it with a strong ligature. Then cut on top of him, and extract it.
If it sinks into the flesh, and you do not find it; then place a cautery on top of the spot with fire, until it dies.
And greater is its corruption, which corrupts the eye, as we have said.
If however you see it has reached the head near the eye; then tie under it with a good suture. Then cut on top of him, and extract it.
And the sick person must use purification of his body with medicines dissolving corrupting foul humors.
And let him beware of food causing corruption.
Chapter on the operation for Nakir's illness.
This illness is named in our land Nakir; and it is a pain that occurs in some members; then it changes from member to member.
And I myself have seen it, as I told you. I was summoned to a sick woman in certain villages. She extended her arm, and I saw a swelling smaller than a vein of the arm.
And when an hour had passed, I saw a swelling moving with a probe, like a worm crawls, ascending more quickly than possible to the arm, as if it were live silver running from one place to another.
The pain therefore receded from that place and was fixed in the arm.
Then after an hour had passed, it ran through the remaining body until it reached another arm.
Then he told me that it was revolving throughout his entire body, as I had seen.
I therefore marveled at the swiftness of its transformation from limb to limb. And indeed, before that, I had not seen this sickness appear in my eyes in such a manner. Nevertheless, I have seen many who find pain transforming from limb to limb; and I did not see it myself as I saw it in a woman.
And I do not think that it was anything other than because the woman was one of those who are from dry bodies with visible veins; from this therefore it appears that the swoon (ventosity) was transformed.
And it is necessary that it does not appear according to this reason in those who are delicate and bodies with hidden veins.
When therefore you wish to cure it and the patient feels that pain; then if it appears to you as we have said, then press upon it quickly and below it; and cut above it until the swoon (ventosity) is expelled contracted; and cauterize the place.
If however you do not see it with your eyes; then cure it with the shock of the body and with what drives out swoons and crushes them with stinking pills and pills from soporifics and similar things.
On the extraction of arrows.
Arrows are distinguished according to their types and the places within the body where they fall.
However, their diversity consists of the following: some have large points, small ones; concave or blunt. And there are those with three angles. And among them are those with tongues (points projecting from the shaft). And among them are those with stars (multiple points or projections on the shaft).
However, those which fall upon limbs, are of two types according to two modes. For limbs are either hollow, like the brain, heart, liver, lung, kidney, intestines, bladder and similar organs. When it falls into any of these limbs and you perceive signs of death (which I shall tell you afterwards), then it is necessary to extract that arrow from it, for death will follow in the one who has it, in many positions. And if you do not perceive these bad signs and the arrow is not hidden deep within the limb, then extract it and take care of the wound.
For the signs of the brain when an arrow falls into it and penetrates the bone and exits through the siphac (which is above the brain) are: as sudden fainting, blindness, dizziness, redness in the eyes, swelling, redness of the tongue, convulsions, confusion of intellect, cholera vomiting. And perhaps blood may flow from the nostrils, or ears. And perhaps speech may be cut off, and voice may be destroyed. And moisture white like plaster flows out from the wound place. And it comes out of that like liquefied flesh.
If therefore these signs appear to you, then abstain from treatment, and withdraw the arrow if it does not flow out.
The signs of the arrow when it falls into the heart are: that it is near the left breast; and it feels as if it were fixed in a hard object, not in an empty one. And perhaps the arrow has movement like the pulse: and blood runs from the wound black. And that follows coldness of the limbs, and cold sweat, and fainting. Therefore you know that death is approaching without doubt.
And the sign of the arrow when it wounds the lung is the emission of frothy blood from the wound; and vessels that follow the neck should be stopped, and the patient's color should be changed. And it breathes out a great, deep breath: and it seeks cold air.
If the arrow falls into the liver, which is in the chest: then it is near small ribs; and there is great panting with very strong pain, with sighing; and all the arms are moved.
And if the arrow falls into the stomach: then perhaps something undigested flows out from the wound.
And if the arrow falls into the abdomen, and is fixed there: something like feces flows out from the wound, or pus, or an already ruptured intestine. Therefore there is no hope for his cure, nor in withdrawing the arrow.
If the arrow falls into the bladder, and urine flows out; and something proceeds from it to the outside, and the pain is stronger than usual on the patient: then you know that it is fatal.
The remaining limbs, as the face, neck, throat, spatula, assistant, dorsal vertebrae, collarbone, thigh, shin and similar members are saved according to several compositions when an arrow does not find the artery or nerve: and there is no venomous arrow.
And I tell you what I saw about these arrows, to indicate by that concerning your cure.
That is, because a man fell with an arrow into his tear duct in the root of his nose. So I removed it from the other side, under the cheek of his ear; and he was healed, and no harm came to his eye.
And I removed another arrow from a Jew, which fell upon him in the fat of his eye beneath the lower eyelid; and the arrow was already hidden, and I did not obtain all of it from it except a small part attached to its wood; and it was a large arrow from Turkish arrows, with soft iron, on which there were no wings.
The Jew was healed, and no evil happened to his eye.
And I removed another arrow from the throat of a Christian.
And it was an Arabian arrow, and it has wings. I therefore cut across it between two gullets; and it was already submerged in his throat. I sharpened myself with it until I removed it; and the Christian was healed.
And I removed another arrow from a man who fell upon it in his abdomen; and we thought that he would die from it.
After thirty days had passed without anything being changed in his condition, I cut across it (the arrow); and I opened it up; and I removed it; and he was healed, and no evil happened to him.
I saw a man to whom an arrow fell on his back, and the wound healed over it. After seven years had passed, the arrow came out at the root of his hip.
I saw a woman to whom an arrow fell into her abdomen, and the wound healed over it; and the arrow remained within her; and no change was made in her constitution, nor did she find any harm from her own natural operations.
I saw another man to whom an arrow fell on his face; and the wound healed over it; and it remained, not causing him much pain; and many similar cases there were.
I extracted an arrow from a prince of the king which had fallen on his nose, and it had already begun to turn toward the right a little; and the arrow was hidden completely.
Therefore I was called to treat him after the loss of the arrow for three days. I found the arrow wound contracted very tightly.
Therefore, I examined it with fine tweezers and did not feel it; and he himself found the prick and pain under his right ear. I hoped that this was the prick from the tip of the arrow.
Therefore I plastered the place with an ointment containing attracting and digestive properties, believing that the spot would open up and show me a sign of the arrow so that I might cut it; but this did not happen at the spot where it had happened, showing that the arrow had passed by.
I therefore persisted with the ointment over him for many days; but it did not happen at the spot where it had happened, and the wound healed up in the meantime; and he remained weak from the extraction of it until one day he felt the arrow within his nose. And he told me this.
And he told me this. I therefore placed sharp and corrosive medicine on that wound for many days until it opened; and when I probed it, I felt a delicate tip of the arrow which was sticking in the wood.
Then I added that sharp medicine into the wound opening until we could clearly see the tip of the arrow; and it passed through me with a space of about four months.
Then, when the wound was swollen and I could insert forceps into it, and move it, it did not obey to come out; then I did not stop trying and devising ways over it with various ingenious means until on one day I began properly to extract it with well-made forceps according to the form given at the end of the chapter, until I pulled it out. Then, I restored the wound.
And indeed physicians judge that cartilage of the nose cannot be restored. I therefore restored it, and the wound healed and became healthy without blemish; nothing at all harmed him.
And I tell you the quality of extracting some arrows; so that you may put this rule and meaning on what I have not said.
Because the parts of this art and their definitions are not understood in narration; neither does the book contain it, and a wise artisan compares with little about much; and with what is present, over what is absent; and he discovers a new operation and a new instrument for descents of foreign bodies of this art when they happen.
Therefore I say that arrows do not exit from the members in which they are fixed except by two modes. Or through attraction from the place where it entered. Opposite parts of another.
And that which goes out where it came in, is either an arrow proceeding in a fleshy place, and drawn out, and comes out.
If it does not obey to come out at the hour when it fell: then it is necessary that you let it alone for some days, until the flesh around it becomes putrid; and its attraction will be lessened, and its coming out will take place.
And likewise if it has fixed itself into a bone, and does not obey to come out, then let it alone also for some days; and press it daily with attraction and motion until it comes out.
If it does not come out after several days, then it is necessary to bore around the arrow in that bone from all sides with a fine awl until the shaft enlarges. Then draw it and extract it (the object).
If the arrow has already been concealed in the body's place and is hidden from sensation; then search for it with a probe. If however you feel it (the part), then draw it out with certain instruments that are suitable for its drawing out.
If you cannot place it (the instrument) above it (the arrow), due to the narrowness of the wound and the depth of the arrowhead: and there is no bone, nerve or vein there: then pierce it (the instrument) into it, until the wound expands so that it can be possible to extract the arrow.
If there are ears attached to it (the arrow), then free the fixed flesh from them on all sides, with all means possible and means, if you cannot lift the flesh above the breakage of the ears and their twisting, until it exits.
And when you perform the extraction of the arrow in any place, then use the twisting of your hand with forceps to all parts, until it exits: and with the utmost subtlety, so that the arrow is not broken, and its drawing out and extraction become difficult for you.
If you cannot place it (the instrument) above it (the arrow), then leave it for several days until what is around it rots. Then repeat it (the procedure): the skin will relax. But if it opposes you with a flow of blood, then administer what was said in its treatment in its chapter: and be careful about damaging the vein, nerve or tendon.
And administer means for the extraction of the arrow in every way possible to you: and it should be with ease, calmness, slowness or firmness, as I told you.
It is necessary that when you draw the arrow, it should be weakened in the shape in which it was when it happened (the accident) there. Because it is more beneficial. If that is not possible for you, then administer what is possible from the shapes (diagrams).
An arrow that emerges from the opposite part goes out to something exterior or it already protrudes from there; or it makes a hump on the tip of the arrow by sensation near the upper skin, and you see it projecting: therefore, cut above it, and let the section be according to the quantity that forceps can grasp in it.
Then pull it out, for it becomes easy to come out.
If it is held in the bone, then turn your hand according to its roundness until the arrow presses into the bone and makes a swelling for itself; then pull it out.
And if not: leave it for several days; then try again until it comes out.
If the arrow is made of wood, then push it with the wood.
If the arrow breaks into pieces of wood, and you wish to apply force: then insert a concave tool into it, so that its concavity enters the shaft of the arrow; then push it with the same.
If the arrow is hollow, then push it with the tool entering into it. The arrow is anointed by this (liquid).
If the arrow is poisoned, then it is necessary that you scrape out all the flesh, in which the poison is; if this is possible for you. Then treat it with what is suitable for that (to counteract the poison).
If the arrow falls into the chest, the abdomen, the bladder, or the side: and it is close to that which you touch with your hand, and it is possible for you to cut above it: then cut, but beware not to cut any vein or nerve, and pull it out.
Then cauterize the wound, if you see one, and care for it until it heals.
And this is the form of forceps with which arrows are pulled out.
Extremities are like the beak of a bird, which have been made like iron: when they grasp onto an arrowhead, they do not let it go.
They become various, great, small, and medium-sized, according to the size of the arrow, its sharpness, and the depth and narrowness of the wound.
The shape of the projectile is concave.
And the shape of the projectile is blunt (or dull).
This is a blunt extremity like a radius to enlarge its entrance into the concave arrowhead and be driven with it.
Chapter on phlebotomy (or venesection).
Veins to be bled, whose course is customary in the body, are thirty.
Among them are sixteen in the head: two pulsating veins that are behind the ears, called the two Herbs; and two arteries that are visible in the two temples; and two veins that are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes, which are called the Watchers; and a vein prepared in the middle of the forehead; and a vein that is at the end of the nose. And two jugular veins, which are in the neck. And two veins that are in the upper lip of the mouth. And two veins that are in the lower lip. These veins are called Algecherich (or alceciri). And two veins that are under the tongue.
But the veins to be bled in the arms have five veins in each arm.
One of them is Cephalic, and it is from the forest side; and the common people call it vein of the head. And Black [one]. And it is the Middle vein, and it is made from a branch of the Basilica, and a branch of the Cephalic; and the common people call it vein of the body. And Basilica, and it is placed on the domestic side; and it is also called Titillicaris. And the common people call it vein of the abdomen. And the string of the arm, and it is placed on the elbow; and that is where phlebotomy is done, and that is which appears above the thumb by clear manifestation.
And Salvatella: and it is a vein that is between the annular and the minimum; and there are two branches to it.
And in the leg and in the foot, there are three veins. One of them is that which is below the thumb's curvature from the forest side. And the second one is the Saphenous: and its place is at the heel from the domestic side. And vein of Ankle: and its place is at the heel from the forest side.
And in another leg, there are three veins similar to those.
Chapter on Phlebotomy of the two veins after the Ears.
But the phlebotomy of the two veins which are after the Ears is beneficial for old catarrhs, and hemigranias, and sores of the head old and chronic.
And the quality of phlebotomy [is] as I have said. And it is [to be done] when the head of the sick person is shaved; and the back of his head is rubbed in the place of two veins with a rough cloth rubbing well. Then the sick person should bind his neck with a bandage until the two veins appear. The places [of the ears] are behind the ears in two depressed locations on the head. Therefore, search for them with your finger, and where you feel their pulse under your finger, mark [them] with a hot iron.
Then take the lancet, which is called the "Incisor". Then insert it [the incisor] beneath the vein into the flesh until the lancet reaches the bone. Then raise your hand with the vein and flesh towards above, and cut the vein and flesh with a shallow cut. And let the length of the incision be the size of two joined fingers, or about that much, and let as much blood flow out as you want.
Then tie it [the cut vein] with threads, and let it heal.
And now the incision of them has been completed at the beginning of the book, and their cauterization [follows].
The phlebotomy of the two arteries which are in the two times [periods] is beneficial for the old hemigraine, and the sodium pressing, and the obtalmia continuous: and for the course of discharges sharp to the eyes.
And the manner of performing the phlebotomy [on them] is as I have told you. Let the sick man tighten his neck much until two veins appear to the sensation with a clear manifestation: and let their pulse be shown under your finger. Then mark them with hot iron [or a cautery].
Then raise the skin above the vein towards above with your finger as an index, and insert the lancet from below, and raise the vein towards above. And cut it [the vein] as you did with the two other veins: and let as much blood flow out according to your need.
Then unclog the obstruction of the sick [person], and place your finger on the vein at the hour one. Then place over it [the wound] and small linen cloths, and bind it from above with strong constraint; and let it be until it heals.
And now the remembrance of them [the wounds], and their cutting, and their removal, has passed; and at the beginning of the book is the incision of the hernia.
However, the remedy for venesection of the forehead vein is after the venesection of the head, for the old diseases of the face; and for the hemicrania, and redness; and for foul ulcers.
And the quality of this venesection is as I have told you. The sick man binds his neck with a bandage until the vein appears. Then take the instrument called "Fossorium".
Place the sharp point that is at the head of the Fossorium on the vein, and strike upon it with a pick or another similar tool in this manner; and let the blood run out according to the amount you wish. Then unclog the perforation of the sick [person], and bind it until it heals.
And sometimes it is opened with a wide venesection. Nevertheless, it should not be a sharp venesection, as the other venesections, rather it should be wide. And the venesection is transverse, because the bone is near; and perhaps the venesection will be broken when it is sharp.
However, the remedy for the two veins which are in the two tear ducts of the two eyes is for the eye from scabies and redness; and for inflammation in the eye, and diseases of the face.
The quality of bloodletting for them is to tighten the sick man's neck with a lint bandage. Then, do the bloodletting and you stand above his head.
Make the bloodletting oblique, not long, with a small lancet, wide slightly, for there is no flesh at that place. If the bloodletter is subtle at the end, it may break.
Then let it run out from his blood as much as is necessary for you. Place a pot beneath them and tighten them at night, and loosen them.
The veins of the nose, when bloodletting, are for acute fever and violent sickness of the face, such as hemigraine and redness that occurs on the face; especially when it is old.
The quality of bloodletting in this case is to tighten the sick man's neck. Then hold his nose with your left hand and take a sharp, long lancet; and prick it in the middle of the septum, between that which separates the nose in its straightness. Because the vein is not visible there, and because blood begins to flow immediately.
And it is necessary that you hold the end of your hand slightly with the lancet; and let blood flow according to your need. Then tie it up at night. It heals quickly by itself.
The bloodletting of the two veins of the cheek is beneficial for constricting cough, and the beginning of leprosy, and melancholic afflictions, and impetigo and bad ulcers, and corrosive, that is, herpes or skin sores.
And the quality of phlebotomy is that it binds the sick person under both his neck with a bandage: and the craftsman stands over the head of the sick, and the sick one sits on a chair over a seat.
Then the phlebotomy vein is taken to the length of the vein, somewhat narrowly. Then take out a measured quantity of blood, or according to what you see due to necessity that is for it. Then do the same with another vein.
Then untie the bandage, and bind two veins tightly together: so that the sick person does not bleed to death. And let it be until morning. A wound heals.
On the phlebotomy of veins, Alzahraki. Veins, according to Alzahraki, are useful for phlebotomy because they help with alcohol in the mouth, and corruption of teeth: and sores, bad ulcers, fissures of lips, ulcers themselves, even those that are on the nose and around it.
And the quality of phlebotomy is that you make the sick person sit in front of you: and bind his neck with a bandage. Then roll back his lip, and look at the two veins: one of which is on the right side of the lip, and the second on its left; and the demonstration of both is shown by their blackness. And that is true because there are small, black veins around them. Cut therefore both with an incision.
If there is doubt on you and you do not know which of them it is: then turn to the larger incision, and it will be more evident.
And do the same with the two veins that are in the upper lip: and most of all, the custom is to do so: and cut the two veins that are in the lower lip.
On phlebotomy: The vein under the tongue after cephalic phlebotomy. From two veins which are under the tongue, phlebotomy is beneficial: one, because phlebotomy of the cephalic vein is for afflictions that are in the throat, and for throat pain, and for mouth pain.
And the quality of phlebotomizing them is that the sick person should sit in front of you by the sun, and clean his mouth, and look under his tongue from one side, and from the other side a vein, and from the other side another vein: and the color of both declines to blackness.
So, phlebotomize both (veins): and be careful, not to wound your hand while phlebotomizing them. Because under his are arteries, and perhaps there will be a flow of blood from these arteries.
The three veins which are phlebotomized at the elbow, are those whose phlebotomy has run into custom among all men.
And phlebotomy of them is done according to two modes. Or piercing with a broad-bladed phlebotome (myrtine), or oiling to the point of disappearing (oliuari), or cutting with a sharp phlebotome (cultellare) and it is called Alnesil. And this is its form.
And from them there are broad and narrow forms according to the width of the veins and their constriction. The form of a phlebotome (myrtine) should be broad, as you see. And it is appropriate to open curved, full, proceeding, visible, thick veins and those that contain thick, turbid blood.
This phlebotomist is of lesser width and more subtle in cuts.
It suits phlebotomy of delicate veins that contain subtle, lemon-colored blood.
The phlebotomy of the Basilica, which is one of these three veins, is beneficial. Because it draws blood from ailments that are below the neck and follow the chest and abdomen; therefore, the phlebotomist should be careful about this one, for beneath it is an artery. If [the phlebotomist] should err and add to the puncture of the phlebotomy, he will cut that artery, and there will be a flow of blood. Therefore, it is necessary that the phlebotomist not cut that [vein] while the phlebotomist punctures; rather, it should be cut by Alnesil.
If the Basilica does not appear in a clear manifestation, then it is necessary that you change it yourself or look for another [vein] or one of its branches; or use the arm as a substitute for the phlebotomy. It is clear itself, and Alnesil cuts it with the phlebotomist, as we said.
If you wish to perform the phlebotomy of that [vein], then it is necessary before tightening the arm to touch the place, until you recognize the place pulsed. Then mark the place with hot iron, then tighten the arm, and cut the vein with the concave incision with Alnesil the phlebotomist, as we said. And be careful that the puncture does not fall into the space from the place of the artery.
And when you see, as you tighten the ligament, inflation in the place that you marked with hot iron, then that inflation is the inflation of an artery; therefore, avoid it.
If you see blood rising at venesection, like the urine of a boy, and it is subtle, red: then you know, it is from the blood of an artery. Therefore, hurry up, and place your finger over it at a long distance, then withdraw your finger. If the blood is cut off (for it is often cut off), then tie the arm and let it be: and beware that the weak do not move it: and be afraid of it.
And do not move it for several days until it heals.
If the blood is not cut off, and it overwhelms you, and there is no medicine present with you in the moment, then cut the artery if it appears to you. For its ends contract, and the blood is cut off.

The vein of the arm is beneficial for venesection because it draws blood from the upper part of the head and the lower part of the body; therefore, since it is composed of a branch of the basilica vein and a branch of the cephalic vein, as we said.

And this nerve often appears to sensation. If a vein is between two nerves, then you should make an incision along its length.
Chapter on the Cephalic Vein. The bloodletting of the Cephalic Vein is beneficial, because it draws blood from the head and contributes to eye problems.
And it is appropriate to do bloodletting in this vein with a lancet coated with olive oil or myrtle oil, because it is the safest of all veins, as it is neither an artery nor a nerve.
Nevertheless, it is advisable for you during bloodletting to avoid the head and shoulder area entirely, and to find a more gentle spot: and it will not harm if the initial strike does not hit the vein, provided that you return to the same spot with bloodletting on several occasions.
Nevertheless, it may be necessary to strike the vein again in some people when it is not struck during the initial bloodletting, but such a swelling will not harm them.
Chapter on the usefulness of Bloodletting and Cautions to be Observed. The nature and accidents of bloodletting, and the remedy for them, which you should consider when practicing it.
First, you should know that bloodletting is not administered except in the preservation of health and its continuation, and as a precaution against the onset of illness.
And it shall be done venesection on one of the three veins that are in the elbow, namely, the Cephalic, the Flexor Tendon (Fusca), and the Basilic. And it shall be done venesection at the beginning of Spring after a fast, and in truth (Summer), and autumn, and winter after food consumption, when signs of congestion appear.
Venesection shall be done on the first or third day, after three hours have passed since the previous day.
Venesection which is given for illness, has no specific hour; but when it is convenient and necessary for that purpose, at night or day, and in any hour, and at any time.
It is not appropriate to venesection of children until they have reached fourteen years of age. Women who are pregnant shall not be subjected to venesection from the fourth month until the seventh. Elderly people, who have already passed sixty years, shall not be subjected to venesection.
When someone wishes to be subjected to venesection for any reason, it is necessary that they clean their bowels before the venesection with a soft enema, if there is much retained fecal matter in them; so as not to attract veins during the venesection from intestinal superfluidities harmful to the main organs.
Patients who are affected by indigestion (toctina), that is, the satiety of nausea; nor those who are hungover (crapulatus), nor those who are coming down from drunkenness, until that has been removed from them. A patient with dropsy shall not be subjected to venesection.
Venesection shall be done with caution after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, multiplying coitus (sexual intercourse), labor, exercise, insomnia, fasting, and everything that dissolves the virtue of the body or an animal.

On Windbagging, and the quality of its use.
Wounds are made from horns, and from copper, and from glass.
And ventilation is performed in two ways. With incision (scarification) and bloodletting; another way of ventilation is without incision.
And this ventilation that is without incision is also performed in two ways. Or else it is done with fire. Or else it is done without fire.
And the places for ventilation that are administered with incision and bloodletting number fourteen on the body. One of these places for ventilation is called Ventosatio Alnocrati, and it is the last on the head; and Alkehel, and it is in the middle of the neck; and ventosae Alhagdahim, which are two layers on the neck from both sides simultaneously; and ventosae menti, which is below the mandible in the lower jaw; and ventosae duarum spatularum; and ventosae Alachosos over the end of the tail; and ventosae duorum focilium, and they are in the middle of two arms; and ventosae duorum crurium; and ventosae duarum cauillarum.
And ventilation does not extract blood from small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore its effectiveness is not as with phlebotomy (bloodletting). It is not necessary to administer ventilation by fire or without fire for any illness that occurs from congestion, until the entire body has been evacuated.
If necessity requires ventilation due to illness or custom, we administer it at any hour, at the beginning of the month, at its end, and in the middle, and whenever it is needed.
Because there are people who, when their blood multiplies, until it needs to be extracted through ventilation, find a headache and pain in their head.
And from these [conditions] is he who finds swelling and redness on his face, on his head, and on his neck. And from these [conditions] is he who finds itching on his face, forehead, and darkness, and dullness in his eyes.
And from these [conditions] is he who scratches the place of his wind-inflammation. And from these [conditions] is he whose laughter increases. And from these [conditions] is he who finds the taste of blood in his mouth: or the tongue is thrust out and cleansed the blood. And from these [conditions] is he whose sleep increases. And from these [conditions] is he who sees in his dream blood and redness, and the dead, and wounds, and similar things.
When we see something from these [conditions], and properly if it is in the third month: then we command wind-inflammation to be made, after two or three hours have passed.
But the remedy for wind-inflammation of the neck is: because it contributes to heaviness in the head, and what is exuded goes to the eyes. However, it must be that this [treatment] is after the evacuation of the entire body.
And indeed wind-inflammation is in the place of cephalic phlebotomy.
But it is not allowed to use this [treatment] for one who is of cold constitution, or in whom there is catarrh. For it causes great harm to him.
And for that reason, it is not proper to use this [treatment] by the elderly and in one whose head has cold diseases.
But he who becomes habitual over it generates forgetfulness upon him.
And for that reason, you should command the wind-inflator to lay down his hand with the wind-inflation briefly towards the lower parts, fearing from the generation of forgetfulness.
Ventosatio or Alkehel, is a place for phlebotomy of Fuscae, and phlebotomy of Basilicae, and it corresponds to suffocation, constriction of breath, fissure of instruments breath, cough, and repletion.
And it is necessary that the Alkehel Ventosatio is pushed a little, because if it is placed below, it generates weakness in the heart and the stomach.
Ventosatio alhagdahim corresponds to pain in the head, migraine, ophthalmia, perforation, and dental root pain; it is a place for phlebotomy of Basilicae.
And it is necessary that you advise the Ventosator not to press his hand during scarification; so as not to cut an artery and cause blood flow.
Ventosation below the chin causes alcohol in the mouth, corruption of gums, and similar illnesses in the mouth; it is a place for phlebotomy at another location which are on the two lips.
Ventosation of spatulas causes alchafacham, which is caused by repletion and heat.
But ventosation of the internal parts of two oval-shaped areas confers benefit to phlebotomy of three veins: Basilicae, Fuscae, and Cephalicae; because it draws blood from all the small veins that are in the flesh; and these small veins draw blood from larger veins until the attraction reaches the three veins.
And it is necessary that you advise the Ventosator not to go too deep in scarification; because the place is bare of flesh, and beneath it are nerves and arteries.
But ventosation that ventosates on the testicles confers hemorrhoids of the anus and lower ulcers.
It is necessary that you instruct the Venti Sorber, it should be a large windbag and made of air, since the place requires strong suction and perhaps subtle winds break; it should be cut with deep incisions.
The winds of the legs diminish by obvious reduction, since they draw blood from the whole body and bring old pains to kidneys, womb, and bladder; they provoke menstruation, cause bile and phlegm; and they are located in place of venesection of two saphenous veins and alhorcobeni.
However, they weaken the body greatly, and cause fainting in many men.

The quality of the positioning for winds is that you place the windbag first in an empty place, and suck with moderate suction; do not prolong the positioning of winds, but place them quickly, and remove them quickly, so that humors come to the place with equal arrival; and do not cease to repeat this and continue until you see the place redden and swell, and the redness appears to be blood; then scarify, and repeat suction gradually. Then consider in positioning of bodies.

What is that which should be administered from oils for the position of Ventosaries, and what should be avoided in venting them.
In the case where the skin is thick, hard, dark, and the pores are narrow, it is necessary to anoint the Ventosaries with open, softening, resolving oils: if it is in summer, for example, aloe oil, or olive oil, or oil of sweet almonds, or seed oil of pumpkin.
And if it is in winter, then narcissus oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or savory oil, and similar ones should be used.
If there is excessive thick and cold secretion, then bitter almond oil, balm oil, white oil or dittany oil should be used, and similar ones.
If the venting is from large pores and soft flesh, then oil should be prohibited, and the areas of Ventosaries should be washed with rose water, cold water, salt water, pumpkin water, or purslane water, and similar ones after venting.
The one whose blood is much moisture, should wash the ventosaries with vinegar or with water of myrtle and sumac, and similar ones.
When the superfluities are gross, wash them with windy wine, or with rose water, or with anise decoction, or with chamomile: and similar things.
It is necessary to avoid windiness in the bath or near the bath, rather it should be administered after leaving the bath for an hour, or for two hours.
And it is not necessary that someone sleeps after windiness.

About Ventoses without incision. Ventoses which are without incision, are those placed on the liver, spleen, foot, and belly, navel, kidneys, and ankle: because these members cannot bear incision upon them.
And it is not sought through them, except attraction of blood from one member to another: such as placing the Ventose on the breasts in the sickness of nosebleed. And we use them to dissipate the cold humour of windiness unbearable in a member: such as placing the Ventose on the belly and navel. For it makes the member rarefied, and warms it up, and removes pain therefore, because it dissipates that windiness.
Also it is placed on the kidneys when there occurs an obstruction or a stone. By its virtue of attraction perhaps it opens up obstruction, or removes the stone from its place.
And likewise it does when placed on the liver and spleen for treading windiness in both of them.
These Ventoses are applied empty, with incision only. And sometimes they are administered with fire.
And sometimes they are administered full of warm water in the sicknesses of pleurisy: and that is so that the Ventose is filled, and large, with only warm water, or water in which boiled herbs that agree have been steeped.
About the form of a Ventose administered with fire.
Its length should be about the size of a hand, and its width two fingers open, as we have formed it: and its depth should be half a palm: and on its side there should be a small hole, according to the quantity that is entered by the needle: made of brass or citrine, thick edges, smooth, equal, rubbed: so that it does not hurt the member upon which it is placed: and in the middle of it there should be a transverse rod of brass or iron, where the candle with fire is placed.
And now it becomes this swollen [thing], larger than we have mentioned earlier, and yet somewhat smaller than it was, according to the sickness and age of the one who is using it.
For boys' swellings, and those of thin bodies, are different from the swellings of men, and those with large bodies.
The quality of placing this swelling with fire on a limb is that you should kindle a linen cloth with fire properly, or a small candle from wax; and place it over the middle rung which is in the middle of the swelling; so that the fire may be ignited around the lower part of the swelling, but not burn the body of the sick person.
Then it is to be placed on the limb; and a finger is over the opening I mentioned, until we hold the swelling; when we need to, we remove the finger, and the vapor comes out through that opening, and the swelling is immediately resolved.
Then, kindle the linen cloth according to its manner, and repeat it if needed.
In the swelling which is applied to the sickness of pleurisy with water, there is no rung across, nor an opening; and it is not administered unless because it is filled with water, and it is placed on the limb only.
And this is its form.
And this swelling, when it is larger, in order to hold more water, is better.
Chapter on the suspension of Sanguisugars.
Chapters XCIX. Sanguisugars are not administered in many places except in those parts of the body where it is impossible to position swellings due to their small size, such as lips, gums, and similar ones. Or on denuded parts of the body, such as fingers, nose, and similar ones.
The quality for their use is: as when coming from Leeches that are in sweet waters, cleaned of rottenness.
Then they (the leeches) should be let loose day and night in sweet water, until they are hungry, and nothing remains in their stomach. Then the body should be evacuated first with venesection (bloodletting), and with purges (emetics). Then cleanse the sick part until it turns red. Then they (the leeches) are placed upon it (the cleaned sick part).
When they are full and fall, and it is possible to suck the site with a purge, then it is more beneficial for healing; if not, then cleanse the place with vinegar. Then with much water, rub and press.
If the course of blood persists after the leeches have fallen off, and it is sweating, then immerse a linen cloth in cold water and place it upon it until the sweating stops.
If the blood increases, then sprinkle powdered zaffran (zegi) or gall nuts and similar substances from the poppy on it until the bleeding stops.
Or lay half-peeled beans on the place, and let them stay until the beans stick to the spot, for the blood will stop flowing.
And it is necessary to repeat the use of leeches when possible, if they are needed.
If leeches are forbidden from being suspended, then cleanse the place with fresh blood. Or make an incision in the places until something comes out of the blood. Then place them (the leeches), for they will stick immediately when they sense something from the blood.
When you wish for them to fall, sprinkle something from crushed aloes, salt or ashes upon them; they will fall immediately.
This Chapter is also often necessary in the art of Medicine; it is the restoration of a fracture and dislocation of bones.
Know ye, O Sons, that foolish doctors and the common people boast about this Chapter, and those who have never examined an ancient book or read a letter from it.
And therefore, because this method is lacking among the learned in our land. And I have never encountered it in a good way, and I have not attained that knowledge from it except for the length of reading ancient books and my diligence in understanding them until I extracted that knowledge from them.
Then I have applied the experiment and diligent study throughout my life.
Now I have described to you everything that my knowledge contains on this Chapter; and beyond what my experiment has failed, after I have abbreviated it for you, and released it from the prolongation of the explanation, and abbreviated it at the end of the abbreviation, and shown its conclusion; and I have formed many forms of instruments that are applied in it, since it is an addition of a decline, as I did in the two preceding Chapters.
Chapter Two.
It is necessary that we say in the prologue of this Chapter the sums and Chapters, to whose understanding the craftsman must be directed first to his station regarding their truth; namely, so that you and those who are ready know or learn this noble art, and others from you.
I say, therefore, that when anyone happens to have a fracture, or dislocation, or twisting, or fall: then it is necessary, firstly, to rush to let blood from him, and to solve it, or both at the same time: unless something forbids it, such as weakness of strength; or it happens to someone who is a child, or an old and decrepit person; or it is a time of intense heat, or intense cold.
Let him be content with his own food, cold vegetables, beans and hedgehogs; and let him abstain from wine, large meat portions, and filling himself up with any food or all food that fills the veins with blood. Until he is secure from a warm abscess, and does not fear the outflow of matter to a limb; then let the sick person return first to his own regime, with which his custom usually runs.
When the broken bone begins to heal, then it is necessary for the sick person to eat nourishing foods in abundance, thick, heavy, with viscosity; such as food made from boiled wheat and water, rice, heads of animals, hooves, entrails of cattle, eggs, fresh fish, thick wine, and similar things. With this regime, the healing of the fracture is made more quickly and better.
And know that broken bones, when they are in men who are in early old age and decrepit, it is not possible for them to be held together and consolidated according to their nature always, due to the drying of their members; and they consolidate and hold together those which are from them at the end of softness, like the bones of small boys.
Nevertheless, nature connects something similar to glue around the broken bone from every part, in which there is thickness, so that it adheres and tightens it until they are consolidated on both sides, and bind together until it comes to the end of strength and firmness, as it was at first, until something forbids it by its operations; and because of this reason it is necessary to put the nourishment of the sick person in foods which have thickness, viscosity, and heaviness, as we said.
And know that the types of fractures are diverse, according to the differences of the limbs; for the fracture of the leg is different from the fracture of the head bone; and the fracture of the chest bone is different from the fracture of the back bone; and similarly all other members are diverse one from another; and I come with the reminder of all types of fractures explained in their respective chapters distinctly from each other. The species of bone fractures are also diverse within themselves.
As for the bow-shaped fracture, there occur stars (spicules) in it. Sometimes a fracture occurs along the length of the bone; and such fractures are called 'stars', that is spicules, or additions proceeding from them, as they are in a reed when it is cut with a knife for writing. Neither proceeding; and there is a fracture with wound and rupture in the head; and there is a small cleft fracture.
And every kind has its skill or specific tool for restoration, according to which its memory will come, distinguished in their respective places.
And from the fact that a bone fracture is known, its curvature and its prominence appear to the senses; and its appearance sounds when you compress it with your hand.
When therefore no curvature appears in its place nor does pain occur with your touch when you touch the bone with movement, nor does a weak great pain arise; then there is no fracture there, indeed it may be a curvature or a small cleft; therefore it is not necessary to move it with the hand and compression at all, but rather lay medicines upon it, whose memory comes after the appropriate time; then a ligature is tightened with subtle binding.
And know that when a place bows and splits into two, there occur stars (spicules) in it, yet all parts are separated from each other; then you must begin from your hour for its correction, by aligning it before abscess (pus) hot (comes).
If however a boil becomes hot, then let it be left for some days until the boil subsides. Then lance the abscess according to whatever method is possible with kindness and skill.
And know that the restoration of it (the abscess) and its equalization is easier than that of a bone, in which fractures occur.
Then tie it (the abscess) according to when you remember about it.
If however there are fractures in the bone, then extension of this fractured member from two parts is necessary, whether it is a hand or a foot; or with your own hand, if the member is small; or with two ropes, or with a rope and your hand.
